مہر مثل سے زیادہ پر گواہی دی پھر رجوع کر لیا دونوں زیادتی کے ضامن ہوں گے
و ان شهدا باكثر من مهر المثل ثم رجعا ضمنا الزيادة لانهما اتلفاها من غير عوض
ترجمہ: اور اگر دونوں گواہوں نے مہر مثل سے زیادہ کی گواہی دی پھر انہوں نے رجوع کیا تو دونوں زیادتی کے ضامن ہوں گے کیونکہ دونوں گواہوں نے مقدار زائد کو بغیر عوض کے تلف کیا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے کسی مرد پر مہر مثل سے زائد کے عوض نکاح کا دعوی کیا مثلاً مہر مثل ایک ہزار روپیہ ہیں اور اس نے پندرہ سو روپیہ کے عوض کا دعویٰ کیا اور مرد اس واقعہ کا منکر ہے، پس دو گواہوں نے عورت کے دعوے کے مطابق گواہی دے دی اور قاضی نے فیصلہ کر دیا پھر دونوں گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو نہ یہ نکاح فسخ ہو گا اور نہ یہ دونوں گواہ مہر مثل کی مقدار کا ضامن ہوں گے۔ البتہ مہر مثل سے زائد یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ مہر مثل یعنی ایک ہزار کا اتلاف تو اتلاف بعوض ملک بضع ہے اور اتلاف بالعوض کی صورت میں ضمان واجب نہیں ہوتا لہذا مہر مثل کی مقدار کا ضمان گواہوں پر واجب نہ ہوگا مگر چونکہ مہر مثل کی مقدار سے زائد یعنی پانچ سو روپیہ کا اتلاف بلا عوض ہے یعنی ان پانچ سو روپیہ کے عوض شوہر کو کچھ نہیں ملا اسلئے ان پانچ سو روپیہ کا ضمان گواہوں پر واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اتلاف بلا عوض ضمان کو واجب کرتا ہے۔
If they testify to more than the proper dower (mahr al-mithl), then they retract, both are liable for the excess because they destroyed it without compensation. Translation: And if two witnesses testify to more than mahr al-mithl, then they retract, both are liable for the excess because they destroyed that excess without compensation. Explanation: The issue is that a woman claimed against a man for marriage with a dower exceeding mahr al-mithl, e.g., mahr al-mithl is 1000 rupees and she claimed 1500 rupees, and the man denied it. Then two witnesses testified according to her claim, and the judge decided accordingly. Then both witnesses retracted their testimony. The marriage is not annulled, nor are they liable for the amount of mahr al-mithl. However, they are liable for the excess over mahr al-mithl, i.e., 500 rupees, because the destruction of the 1000 rupees (mahr al-mithl) was destruction with compensation (ownership of bida'), and destruction with compensation does not incur liability. Thus they are not liable for the mahr al-mithl. But the excess of 500 rupees was destroyed without compensation, i.e., the husband received nothing in return, so they are liable for that 500 rupees, because destruction without compensation makes liability obligatory.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof on the retraction of testimony for a marriage dower exceeding the proper dower (mahr al-mithl). The author uses the same principle as the previous case: the witnesses are not liable for the mahr al-mithl part because it is compensated by the husband's gaining ownership of the bida'. However, any amount above the mahr al-mithl is destroyed without compensation, so the witnesses are liable for that excess. The example given is mahr al-mithl = 1000, claimed 1500, so they are liable for 500. The marriage itself is not annulled. This is a clear application of the Hanafi rule that destruction with compensation (itlaf bi-'iwad) does not give rise to liability, whereas destruction without compensation does.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower determined by the dower of women similar to the bride in social status, age, etc.
زیادہ (ziyada): The excess amount over mahr al-mithl.
اتلاف بلاعوض (itlaf bila 'iwad): Destruction without compensation; incurs liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of witnesses testifying to a marriage with a dower exceeding mahr al-mithl and then retracting, what are they liable for?
A) The entire dower.
B) Nothing.
C) Only the excess amount over mahr al-mithl.
D) Half the dower.

Key Takeaway
Witnesses retracting testimony on an excessive dower are liable only for the excess over mahr al-mithl, not for the proper dower itself.

Shahadat — Testimony

Liability of Witnesses Retracting After Testifying in a Sale with Low Price
Ruling on witness liability after retraction in a sale with underpayment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which retracting witnesses are liable for the shortfall in a sale case and apply the Hanafi principle of itlaf bi'l-ʿiwaḍ.

Core Idea
Witnesses liable only for uncompensated loss; full compensation removes liability.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines a nuanced scenario: witnesses testify to a sale at a price below market value, then retract after the judge's ruling. The Hanafi school holds them liable for the shortfall, reasoning that they destroyed part of the property without compensation. The discussion also addresses the effect of the seller's option (khiyar al-shart) and why the seller's silence does not absolve the witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
Read the passage to find the two cases: (1) witnesses testify to a sale at full market price, and (2) witnesses testify to a sale at less than market value. Note the different rulings.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
In the first scenario, witnesses are not liable because full compensation was received. In the second, they are liable for the shortfall (the uncompensated portion).
3
Understand the underlying principle
The text relies on the Hanafi principle that destruction with compensation (itlaf bi'l-ʿiwaḍ) is treated like no destruction, so no liability. Destruction without compensation (itlaf bila ʿiwaḍ) triggers liability.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle analogy) from general property damage rules.
4
Analyze the objection regarding seller's option
The passage raises an objection: if the sale had a seller's option, the seller's own silence after the option period might seem to cause the loss. The answer traces causation back to the witnesses' testimony as the original cause.
The attribution (isnad) of the loss to the witnesses is key.
5
Apply the rule to analogous cases
Consider how this ruling applies to modern property transactions where witnesses retract after testifying to a low price. The same principle of uncompensated loss governs.

Source Text

سوال یہ ہے کہ جب گواہوں نے کم قیمت کے عوض بیع کی گواہی دی جس میں بائع کو خیار شرط حاصل ہے تو گواہوں نے بائع کی کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی ہے کیونکہ گواہوں نے ایسی بیع کی شہادت دی ہے جس میں بائع کو خیار شرط حاصل ہے اور جس بیچ میں بائع کو خیار شرط حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں مبیع سے بالغ کی ملک زائل نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ گویا اس بیچ میں گواہوں کے گواہی دینے کے باوجود مبیع یعنی غلام سے بائع کی ملک زائل نہیں ہوتی ہے لیکن جب خیار کی مدت ( تین دن ) گذرگئی اور بائع خاموش رہا تو اس کے خاموش رہنے سے بیج نافذ ہوگئی اور مبیع اس کی ملک سے نکل گئی بہت بائع کا مدت خیار میں خاموش رہنا اور بیچ کو رد نہ کرنا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ بائع اس بیچ پر خود راضی ہے۔ اور قیمت سے کم کے عوض مبیع اپنی ملک سے نکالنے پر راضی ہے۔ پس جب گواہوں نے کچھ تلف نہیں کیا بلکہ یہ سب کچھ بائع ہی کا کیا ہوا ہے تو گواہوں پر مقدار نقصان کا ضمان کس طرح واجب کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بیع بشرط خیار البائع اگر چہ بائع کی ملک سے مبیع کو نہیں نکالتی اور بائع اپنے اوپر سے ضرر دور کرنے پر قادر ہے بایں طور کہ مدت خیار میں بیع فسخ کر دے مگر مدت خیار میں بیع فسخ نہیں کی بلکہ اس بیع پر راضی ہو گیا اور اپنے نقصان پر بائع کی رضامندی گواہوں سے منمان کو ساقط کر دیتی ہے۔ لیکن مبیع سے بائع کی ملک زائل ہونے کا سبب وہی مبیع سابق ہے جس کو گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے ثابت کیا ہے۔ لہذا مدت خیار گذر جانے کے بعد سقوط خیار کے وقت مبیع سے بائع کی مالک زائل ہونے کا حکم اسی بیج سابق کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ جس بیع کو گواہی سے ثابت کیا گیا ہے۔ پس جب زوال ملک کا حکم بیع سابق کی طرف منسوب ہے اور بیع سابق گواہوں کی گواہی سے حاصل ہوئی ہے تو اس مبیع کا تلف کرنا گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ اور جب مبیع کا تلف کرنا گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہے تو جس قدر مبیع کا اتلاف بلا عوض ہے اس کا ضمان بھی گواہوں پر واجب ہوگا۔
Chapter on retraction from testimonies: A testimony was given in favor of the buyer's claim, then after the judge's ruling the witnesses retracted their testimony. These two witnesses will not be liable to the seller. Because although the witnesses through their testimony destroyed the seller's sold item (the slave), the seller received full compensation for it. Therefore this is destruction with compensation, and it has passed previously that destruction with compensation is on the level of no destruction, so liability is not obligatory. And when in the case of destruction with compensation liability is not obligatory, then upon these witnesses liability will not be obligatory either. And if the buyer claimed to purchase the mentioned slave for less than its value, e.g., five hundred rupees, and accordingly the witnesses testified, and then after the judge's verdict the witnesses retracted their testimony, then both witnesses will be liable to the seller for the amount of loss, i.e., five hundred rupees, because they destroyed that portion of the slave which corresponds to five hundred rupees without compensation. That is, the slave's value is one thousand and the seller only received five hundred rupees, so it is as if the witnesses destroyed half the slave without compensation. And it has passed previously that in the case of destruction without compensation, liability is obligatory upon the destroyer. Therefore, upon the witnesses liability will be obligatory for the amount that was destroyed without compensation, i.e., five hundred rupees which is the amount of loss. The author of al-Hidayah said that in the case of testifying to a sale at less than the value, the witnesses will be liable for the amount of loss, whether the sale is definitive and executed or suspended due to the seller's option. This statement is actually the answer to a question. The question is: When the witnesses testified to a sale at a low price in which the seller has a stipulated option (khiyar al-shart), then the witnesses have not destroyed anything of the seller's because they testified to a sale in which the seller has a stipulated option, and in a sale where the seller has a stipulated option, the seller's ownership of the sold item does not cease. Thus, in this sale, despite the witnesses' testimony, the seller's ownership of the sold item (the slave) does not cease. But when the option period (three days) passed and the seller remained silent, then through his silence the sale became effective and the sold item left his ownership. But the seller's silence during the option period and not revoking the sale is a sign that the seller is satisfied with this sale and is satisfied with removing the sold item from his ownership for a low price. So when the witnesses did not destroy anything, rather all of this was done by the seller himself, then how can liability for the amount of loss be imposed on the witnesses? The answer is that a sale with a condition of the seller's option, although it does not remove the sold item from the seller's ownership and the seller is able to remove harm from himself by rescinding the sale during the option period, but he did not rescind the sale during the option period; rather he agreed to the sale and his consent to his own loss removes liability from the witnesses. However, the cause of the removal of the seller's ownership from the sold item is that same previous sale which the witnesses established with their testimony. Therefore, after the option period passes and the option lapses, the ruling that the seller's ownership ceases from the sold item will be attributed to that previous sale which was established by testimony. So when the ruling of removal of ownership is attributed to the previous sale and that previous sale came about through the witnesses' testimony, then the destruction of the sold item is attributed to the witnesses. And when the destruction of the sold item is attributed to the witnesses, then for whatever amount of destruction without compensation, liability will also be upon the witnesses.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the liability of witnesses who retract after testifying in a sale case. The text first states the general rule: if the witnesses testify in accordance with the buyer's claim and the buyer pays the full price, there is no liability because the seller received full compensation. Then it addresses a scenario where the buyer claims a price less than the market value. In that case, the witnesses are liable for the shortfall, as they have destroyed that portion without compensation. The author then addresses a subsidiary issue: what if the sale was subject to the seller's option (khiyar al-shart)? The objection is that the seller's ownership does not cease immediately, so how can the witnesses be said to have destroyed anything? The answer is that although the seller's silence after the option period indicates consent, the original cause of the ownership transfer is still the sale established by the witnesses' testimony. Therefore, the destruction is attributed to them, and they are liable for the uncompensated portion. The reasoning relies on the Hanafi principle that destruction with compensation is like no destruction, while destruction without compensation entails liability.

Key Terms
رجوع عن الشهادة (rujūʿ ʿan al-shahādah): Retraction of testimony after the judge has passed a verdict based on it.
ضمان (ḍamān): Legal liability or responsibility to compensate for loss or damage.
اتلاف بالعوض (itlāf bi'l-ʿiwaḍ): Destruction of property for which full compensation is received.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale case, the witnesses testified that the buyer purchased a slave for 500 rupees (market value 1000), and the judge ruled accordingly. After the witnesses retract, what is their liability according to the Hanafi school?
A) No liability because the seller consented
B) They are liable for 500 rupees
C) They are liable for the full 1000 rupees
D) They are liable only if the sale had an option condition

Key Takeaway
Retracting witnesses are liable only for the uncompensated portion of the loss; if full compensation was received, no liability arises.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
12 min
Witnesses Retract Testimony of Pre-Consummation Divorce
Ruling and reasoning on witness liability after retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction in pre-consummation divorce and explain the underlying qiyas reasoning.

Core Idea
Witnesses guarantee half the mahr because they confirmed a vulnerable obligation that was otherwise prone to cancellation.

This lesson examines a ruling from the chapter on retraction of testimony (Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat). When witnesses testify that a husband divorced his wife before consummation, and then retract, Hanafi law holds them liable for half the mahr. The reasoning hinges on the vulnerable nature of the mahr obligation before consummation and the principle that the confirmer (mu'akkid) bears the liability of the original causer (mujib).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act triggers liability? Here, it is the retraction of testimony that established half the mahr as a binding obligation. The ruling is that the witnesses must guarantee (daman) half the mahr.
The obligation is wajib, not fard, because the proof is qiyas (zanni).
2
Locate the proof
The author provides two analogical proofs (qiyas). First, the mahr before consummation is vulnerable to being dropped entirely (e.g., wife's zinā or apostasy). The witnesses' testimony made it binding. Second, separation before consummation is analogous to faskh (annulment), which drops the entire mahr; thus the half that becomes obligatory is solely due to the witnesses.
The text also cites examples from Ibn al-Humam to illustrate the principle.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illa) is that the witnesses' testimony confirmed a guarantee that was on the verge of being dropped. The phrase 'akadda damanan 'ala sharaf al-suqut' shows this. The analogy to the muhrim catching game or the coercer of divorce shows that the confirmer (mu'akkid) is liable for what the causer (mujib) would have been liable.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because the link is not explicit in the texts.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The well-known Shafi'i position is that the witnesses only guarantee if they were false witnesses (shuhud zur) or if the judgment was executed. Imam Ahmad and one narration from Malik and Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi view.
The difference stems from how each school treats the effect of retraction before execution of judgment.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon (mufta bihi) in the school. No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded.
The authority weight is high as it comes from the core books of Imam Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
دو گواہوں نے کسی مرد پر اپنی بیوی کو دخول سے پہلے طلاق دینے پر گواہی دی پھر رجوع کر لیا نصف مہر کے ضامن ہوں گے
وان شهدا على رجل انه طلق امرأته قبل الدخول بها ثم رجعا ضمنا نصف المهر لانهما اكدا ضمانا على شرف السقوط الاترى انها لو طاوعت ابن الزوج او ارتدت سقط المهر اصلا ولان الفرقة قبل الدخول في معنى الفسخ فيوجب سقوط جميع المهر كما مر فى النكاح ثم يجب نصف المهر ابتداء بطريق المتعة فكأن واجبا بشهادتهما
ترجمہ اور اگر دو گواہوں نے کسی مرد پر گواہی دی کہ اس نے اپنی بیوی کو اس کے ساتھ دھول سے پہلے طلاق دے دی پھر انہوں نے رجوع کیا تو دونوں نصف مہر کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ اسلئے کہ ان دونوں نے ایسے عمان کو موکد کر دیا ہے جو ساقط ہونے کے قریب تھا۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ عورت اگر ابن زوج سے مطاحت کرے یا مرتد ہو جائے تو مہر بالکلیہ ساقط ہو جاتا ہے اور اس لئے کہ دخول سے پہلے فرقت مسح کے معنی میں ہے۔ پس وہ پورے مہر کے ساقط ہونے کو واجب کرتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ نکاح میں گذر چکا ہے پھر ابتداء نصف مہر بطریق متعہ واجب ہوگا ۔ پس یہ ان دونوں کی گواہی سے واجب ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت نے دعوی کیا کہ میرا شوہر مجھ کو دخول سے پہلے ہی طلاق دے چکا ہے اور شوہر اس کا منکر ہے۔ پھر عورت کے موافق دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ اس عورت کے شوہر نے دخول سے پہلے اس کو طلاق دیدی ہے۔ پس اس گواہی کے مطابق قاضی نے زوجین کے درمیان تفریق کر دی اور اس عورت کا مہر اگر مسمی تھا تو شوہر پر نصف مہر واجب کر دیا اور اگر مہر مثل تھا تو شوہر پر متعہ واجب کر دیا اس فیصلہ کے بعد دونوں گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو یہ دونوں گواہ مہرسمی کی صورت میں نصف مہر کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ اسی کے قاتل امام احمد ہیں۔ اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عورت کے ساتھ دخول سے پہلے مہر کے ساقط ہونے کا ہر وقت امکان ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر عورت نے اپنے شوہر کے اس بیٹے کو جو پہلی بیوی سے ہے وہلی پر قدرت دے دی یا اس نے شہوت کے ساتھ اس کے بیٹے کا بوسہ لے لیا۔ یا العیاذ باللہ عورت مرتد ہوگئی تو مہر بالکل ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ یعنی دخول سے پہلے اسطرح کے نشوز اور نافرمانی کی وجہ سے شوہر کے ذمہ سے مہر بالکل ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال جو مہر شوہر کے ذمہ ہے دخول سے پہلے وہ موکد نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ساقط ہونے کے قریب ہوتا ہے لیکن گواہوں نے طلاق کی گواہی دے کر نصف مہر مؤکد کر دیا ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول کی وجہ سے شوہر پر نصف کا ادا کرنا واجب ہو جاتا ہے اور مؤکد ( پختہ کرنے والے ) پر وہی واجب ہوتا ہے جو موجب ( واجب کرنے والے) پر لازم ہوتا ہے اور گواہ اپنی گواہی سے اگر کسی پر کچھ لازم کرتے اور پھر وہ اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیتے تو ان پر ضمان واجب ہوتا۔ پس اسی طرح جب دو گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے نصف مہر مؤکد کیا ہے اور پھر اس سے رجوع کیا ہے تو ان پر بھی ضمان واجب ہوگا ۔ موجب پر جو واجب ہوتا ہے مؤکد پر بھی وہی واجب ہوتا ہے۔ علامہ ابن الہمام نے اس کی نظیر میں دو مسئلے ذکر فرمائے ہیں ۔ ۔ اگر محرم نے بحالت احرام حرم کا شکار پکڑ لیا پھر دوسرے آدمی نے اس کو قتل کر ڈالا تو شکار کی جز اور تاوان پکڑنے والے پر واجب ہے اور وہ قتل کرنے والے سے رجوع کرے گا۔ کیونکہ قاتل نے شکار قتل کر کے اس کی جزاء کو مؤکر کر دیا ہے ورنہ اگر یقتل نہ کرتا تو ہوسکتا تھا کہ پکڑنے والا محرم تو بہ کر لیتا اور اس شکار کو چھوڑ دیتا اور تاوان اس کے ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا۔
- ایک شخص نے دوسرے شخص کو طلاق قبل الدخول پر کراہ کیا اور اس نے بحالت اکراہ طلاق دے دی تو شوہر پر نصف مہر واجب ہوا اور شوہر اس کو اکراہ کرنے والے سے واپس لے گا۔ کیونکہ اکراہ کرنے والے شخص نے طلاق دلا کر نصف مہر مؤکد کر دیا ہے۔ ور نہ ہو سکتا تھا کہ عورت ارتداد یا ابن الزوج سے مطاوعت وغیرہ کوئی ایسی حرکت کر بیٹھتی جس کی وجہ سے فرقت واقع ہو جاتی اور مہر بالکلیہ ساقط ہو جاتا ۔
اصل مسئلہ پر دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دخول سے پہلے فرقت فتح کے معنی میں ہے کیونکہ معقود علیہ مین بضع عورت کی طرف بغیر تصرف کے صحیح، سالم لوٹ آیا اور فسخ نکاح سے پور امبر ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ کتاب النکاح کے بارب السمبر میں گذر چکا ہے اور فسخ نکاح سے پورا مہر اسلئے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے کہ فتح کی صورت میں عقد نکاح ایسا ہو جاتا ہے گویا نکاح منعقدی نہیں ہوا۔ اور شوہر پر نصف بطریق متعہ ابتداء گواہوں کی گواہی سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب نصف مہر شوہر پر گواہوں کی گواہی سے واجب ہوتا ہے گویا شوہر پر نصف مہر گواہوں کی گواہی سے واجب ہوا ہے پس جب نصف مہر شوہر پر گواہوں کی گواہی سے واجب ہوا تو رجوع کرنے کے بعد شوہر کیلئے مہمان بھی انہیں گواہوں پر واجب ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرقت قبل الدخول کو فسخ کے معنی میں کیوں کہا ہے، براہ راست فسخ کیوں نہیں کہا۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نکاح ، لزوم کے بعد فسخ کو قبول نہیں کرتا ہے۔ مگر چونکہ مبدل یعنی بضع صحیح سالم بغیر تصرف کے عورت کی ملک کی طرف لوٹ آیا اس لئے یہ نسخ کے مشابہ ہوگا اور عین فسخ نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter on retraction from testimonies. If two witnesses testify that a man divorced his wife before consummation, then they retract, they guarantee half the mahr. Because they have confirmed a guarantee that was on the verge of being dropped. Do you not see that if the woman committed zinā with the husband's son or apostatized, the entire mahr falls. And because separation before consummation is in the meaning of annulment, it necessitates the dropping of the entire mahr, as has passed in the Book of Marriage. Then half the mahr becomes obligatory initially as a gift, so it becomes obligatory by their testimony. Translation: And if two witnesses testified against a man that he divorced his wife before consummation with her, then they retracted, then both will be guarantors of half the mahr. Because they have confirmed a guarantee that was close to being dropped. Do you not see that if the woman committed zinā with the husband's son or apostatized, the mahr is completely dropped. And because separation before consummation is in the meaning of annulment, so it necessitates the dropping of the entire mahr, as has passed in marriage. Then half the mahr becomes obligatory initially as a gift, so it becomes obligatory by their testimony. Explanation: The scenario is that if the woman claimed that her husband divorced her before consummation and the husband denies it. Then two witnesses testify in favor of the woman that her husband divorced her before consummation. Then according to this testimony, the judge separates between the spouses, and if the mahr was specified, he made half the mahr obligatory on the husband, and if it was mahr al-mithl, he made a gift obligatory. After this decision, the two witnesses retract their testimony, so these two witnesses will be guarantors of half the mahr in the case of specified mahr. Imam Ahmad holds the same view, and one narration from Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i also agrees. The evidence is that before consummation, the possibility of the mahr being dropped exists at all times. Thus, if the woman gave the husband's son from a previous wife the opportunity to have intercourse with her, or if she kissed his son with desire, or if she apostatizes, then the mahr is completely dropped. That is, due to such nushuz and disobedience before consummation, the mahr is completely dropped from the husband's liability. In any case, the mahr that is owed by the husband before consummation is not confirmed but is close to being dropped. But the witnesses, by testifying to the divorce, have confirmed half the mahr. Because divorce before consummation makes the payment of half obligatory on the husband, and the one who confirms (mu'akkid) is liable for what the one who causes (mujib) is liable for. If witnesses cause something to become due from someone and then retract, guarantee becomes obligatory on them. So similarly, when two witnesses have confirmed half the mahr through their testimony and then retracted, guarantee will be obligatory on them. What is obligatory on the one who causes is also obligatory on the one who confirms. Allamah Ibn al-Humam mentioned two analogous cases: (1) If a muhrim catches game in the Haram while in ihram, then another person kills it, the penalty and compensation for the game are on the catcher, and he will recourse to the killer. Because the killer, by killing the game, confirmed its penalty; otherwise, if he had not killed it, the catcher might have released it and the penalty would have fallen from his liability. (2) A person coerced another to divorce before consummation, and he divorced under coercion, then half the mahr becomes obligatory on the husband, and the husband will take it back from the coercer. Because the coercer, by making him divorce, confirmed half the mahr; otherwise, it was possible that the woman might have committed apostasy or zinā with the husband's son or some such act that would cause separation and the mahr to be completely dropped. The second evidence on the original issue is that separation before consummation is in the meaning of annulment, because the subject matter of the contract, i.e., the sexual organ, returned to the woman's ownership sound and intact without any use. And in annulment of marriage, the entire mahr drops. As has passed in the Book of Marriage in the section on mahr. And in annulment, the entire mahr falls because in annulment, the marriage contract becomes as if it never took place. And half the mahr becomes obligatory initially as a gift by the witnesses' testimony. So when half the mahr becomes obligatory on the husband by their testimony, just as half the mahr was imposed on the husband by their testimony, then after their retraction, the husband will recoup from these witnesses. As for why the author of al-Hidayah said that separation before consummation is in the meaning of annulment and not directly annulment, the answer is that marriage after its establishment does not admit annulment. But since the subject matter (the sexual organ) returned to the woman's ownership sound and intact without any use, it resembles annulment but is not actual annulment.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on retraction from testimony (kitab al-ruju' 'an al-shahadat). It addresses the case where two witnesses testify that a husband divorced his wife before consummation, the judge rules accordingly and makes half the mahr obligatory (or a gift if mahr was unspecified), and then the witnesses retract. The ruling is that the witnesses must guarantee half the mahr. The commentary provides two main reasons. First, the mahr before consummation is vulnerable to being completely dropped due to certain acts by the wife (like zinā with the husband's son or apostasy). The witnesses, by testifying, have made this non-binding obligation binding (mu'akkid), so they are liable when they retract. This is analogous to qiyas: the mu'akkid (confirmer) bears the same liability as the mujib (the one who originally caused the obligation). Second, separation before consummation is analogous to faskh (annulment), which would drop the entire mahr, but here half is established as a gift through the testimony. Thus, the witnesses are the cause of this obligation, so they must compensate. The text also cites two examples from Ibn al-Humam: the muhrim catching game and the coercer of divorce, both illustrating the principle. Finally, it clarifies why the author said 'in the meaning of faskh' rather than actual faskh: marriage after its establishment does not admit annulment, but it resembles it because the subject matter returns intact.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay compensation; here, the witnesses must pay half the mahr to the husband.
مهر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife in marriage; here, half becomes obligatory due to divorce before consummation.
متعہ (mut'ah): A consolatory gift given to a divorced woman; here, it refers to the half mahr (or a gift in lieu of half mahr if mahr was not specified) after pre-consummation divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the witnesses guarantee half the mahr when they retract their testimony that a man divorced his wife before consummation?
A) Because they deliberately lied and caused harm
B) Because they confirmed a guarantee that was on the verge of being dropped, making it binding
C) Because they physically seized the mahr from the husband
D) Because the wife lost her right to the mahr entirely

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract testimony that established a vulnerable obligation (here, half mahr in pre-consummation divorce) must guarantee that amount because they acted as mu'akkid (confirmers).

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Witnesses' Guarantee After Retracting Testimony of Emancipation
Ruling and justification for witnesses' guarantee after retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses retract testimony of freeing a slave, identify the legal basis (destroying property without compensation), and explain why wala' remains with the master.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses guarantee the slave's value because they destroyed the master's property without compensation.

When witnesses testify that a master freed his slave, the judge enforces the emancipation. If they later retract, the Hanafi school holds them financially liable for the slave's market value. This lesson unpacks the reasoning: the witnesses directly caused the loss of the master’s property (the slave) without any exchange, triggering the principle of daman al-itlaf. We also examine why the clientage (wala') remains with the original master, not transferring to the witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What exactly is the legal consequence for the witnesses? State: they must pay the slave's value (al-qimah) to the master.
The ruling is a financial guarantee (daman), not a criminal penalty.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
Find the explicit reason given in the text: 'because they destroyed the property value of the slave from him without compensation'. This is a qiyas (analogy) to general liability for destruction of property.
The proof is not a direct text but an analogy based on the principle of itlaf.
3
Understand the legal basis: itlaf without 'iwad
The witnesses' testimony caused the slave to be freed, which is equivalent to destroying the master's property (the slave's value) without receiving any compensation in return. In Hanafi law, causing loss of valuable property (mal mutaqawwim) without exchange obligates the causer to make it good.
This is a well-established principle: man atlafa shay'an fa-hwa damin.
4
Examine the exception: wala' remains
Why doesn't the wala' (clientage) transfer to the witnesses? Because the act of freeing (itq) is attributed to the master's own action, not the witnesses' testimony. The witnesses merely caused the legal confirmation; the emancipation itself is the master's deed. Therefore, wala' stays with the manumitter.
This preserves the master's right of inheritance and guardianship over the freed slave.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some Shafi'i and Maliki scholars argue that since the freeing is a religious act (qurbah), no financial liability arises. The Hanafi response distinguishes: the act has both a religious aspect (emancipation) and a property aspect (loss of the slave's value). The property loss is compensable.
This illustrates how different analytical lenses lead to different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو گواہوں نے غلام آزاد کرنے کی گواہی دی پھر دونوں نے رجوع کرلیا تو دونوں غلام کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے
قال وان شهدا على انه اعتق عبده ثم رجعا ضمنا قيمته لانهما اتلفا مالية العبد عليه من غير عوض والولاء للمعتق لان العتق لا يتحوّل اليهما بهذا الضمان فلا يتحول الولاء اليهما
ترجمہ اور اگر دو گواہوں نے اس بات پر گواہی دی کہ اس نے اپنا اعلام آزاد کیا ہے پھر دونوں نے رجوع کیا تو دونوں اس غلام کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ اسلئے کہ ان دونوں نے مولیٰ پر اس غلام کی مالیت مفت تلف کی ہے اور والا ء آزاد کرنے والے کیلئے ہے کیونکہ اس ضمان کی وجہ سے آزاد کرنا ان دونوں گواہوں کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہوگا۔ پس ولا بھی ان دونوں کی طرف منتقل نہیں ہو گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو شخصوں نے گواہی دی کہ عارف نے اپنا غلام آزاد کر دیا ہے۔ قاضی نے اس کے مطابق فیصلہ دے دیا۔ پھر دونوں گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو یہ دونوں گواہ مولیٰ کیلئے غلام کی قیمت کے بقدر مال کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ دونوں گواہ خواہ مالدار ہوں، خواہ تنگدست ہوں کیونکہ ان دونوں نے جو کچھ تلف کیا ہے یعنی غلام وہ ال متقوم ہے اور یہ تلف کرنا بلا عوض ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ بلاعوض تلف کرنا ضمان کو واجب کرتا ہے۔ اسلئے دونوں گواہ مولی کیلئے غلام کی قیمت کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ اور غلام کی ولاء مولی کیلئے ہوگی۔ کیونکہ گواہوں کی گواہی کے ذریعہ آزادی مولی کی طرف سے متفق ہوئی ہے۔ یعنی آزاد کرنے والا
If two witnesses testify that he freed his slave, then both retract, they guarantee the slave's value. He said: And if they witness that he freed his slave, then they retract, they guarantee its value because they have destroyed the property value of the slave from him without compensation. And the wala' (clientage) belongs to the manumitter, because the freeing does not transfer to them by this guarantee, so the wala' does not transfer to them. Translation: And if two witnesses testified that he freed his slave, then both retracted, then both will be guarantors of the slave's value. Because they have destroyed the property value of the slave from the master without compensation. And the wala' belongs to the manumitter, because the freeing does not transfer to these witnesses by this guarantee, so the wala' does not transfer to them. Explanation: The scenario is that two persons testified that the master freed his slave. The judge gave a verdict accordingly. Then both witnesses retracted their testimony, so these two witnesses will be guarantors of an amount equal to the slave's value for the master. Whether the witnesses are wealthy or poor, because what they have destroyed, i.e., the slave, is a property of value (mal mutaqawwim), and this destruction is without compensation, and it has passed earlier that destruction without compensation necessitates guarantee. Therefore, both witnesses will be guarantors of the slave's value for the master. And the wala' of the slave will be for the master. Because through the witnesses' testimony, the freeing is confirmed from the master's side, i.e., the manumitter.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a second ruling from the same chapter, covering the case where witnesses testify that a master freed his slave. The judge rules accordingly, and the slave is freed. Then the witnesses retract. The ruling is that they guarantee the slave's value (the market value at the time of judgment) because they have destroyed the master's property without any compensation. The wala' (clientage) remains with the master and does not transfer to the witnesses, because the act of freeing (itq) is attributed to the master's action, not the witnesses'; the witnesses only caused the legal consequence. The commentary emphasizes that the slave is a valuable property (mal mutaqawwim), and causing its loss without exchange (bi la 'iwad) triggers liability under the principle of itlaf (destruction). The witnesses are liable regardless of their financial status, because liability for destruction is not conditioned on ability to pay.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): The act of freeing a slave; here, the testimony results in the legal emancipation of the slave.
ولاء (wala'): Clientage; the right of inheritance and guardianship that belongs to the manumitter after freeing a slave. Here, it remains with the master despite the witnesses' guarantee.
مال متقوم (mal mutaqawwim): Property that is legally valuable and protected; the slave is considered mal mutaqawwim, so its destruction incurs liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the wala' remain with the master even after the witnesses guarantee the slave's value?
A) Because the witnesses are not Muslim
B) Because the freeing is attributed to the master, not the witnesses
C) Because the witnesses paid the value, so they become the new masters
D) Because wala' is automatically transferred with compensation

Key Takeaway
Witnesses who retract testimony of slave emancipation must pay the slave's value because they destroyed the master's property without compensation, but the clientage (wala') stays with the original master.

Retraction from Testimony of Qisas: Liability for Diyah, Not Qisas
Inter-madhhab dispute on retraction of qisas testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on witnesses who retract after testifying to qisas and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Doubt and weak causation spare witnesses from qisas, but they still owe diyah.

This passage presents a disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on what happens when witnesses retract after testifying to qisas and the execution has already occurred. The Hanafi school holds that witnesses only pay blood money (diyah), not retaliatory execution. Imam al-Shafi'i argues they should face qisas. The dispute hinges on the nature of causation (tasbib) and the role of doubt (shubhah) in averting hudud penalties.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: witnesses guarantee diyah, not qisas. This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school.
The ruling applies regardless of the heir's choice to execute or pardon.
2
Identify the opponent's objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that witnesses caused the death causally (tasbib), similar to coercion (ikrah), so qisas should apply, even more so because the heir is aided by the testimony.
The Shafi'i analogy: witnesses are like a coercer who forces someone to kill – here the testimony forces the judge's hand.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi response: no direct killing (mubasharah) and no valid causation because a cause must usually lead to the result. Here, pardon is recommended (mandub), so death is not inevitable. Additionally, the judge's voluntary act cuts attribution, and doubt (shubhah) always prevents qisas.
Doubt is established because retraction creates uncertainty about the original testimony.
4
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi = diyah only; Shafi'i = qisas on witnesses. In practice, Hanafi courts will only impose financial liability, not corporal punishment.
This affects sentencing and the rights of heirs.

Source Text

و ان شهدوا بقصاص ثم رجعوا بعد القتل ضمنوا الدية لا يقتص منهم وقال الشافعي يقتص منهم لوجود القتل منهم تسبيبا فاشبه المكره بل اولى لان الولى يُعان والمكره يمنع ولنا ان القتل مباشرة لم يوجد وكذا تسبيبا لأن السبب ما يفضى اليه غالبا و ههنا لا يفضى لان العفو مندوب بخلاف المكره لانه لا يؤثر حياته ظاهرا ولان الفعل الاختيارى مما يقطع النسبة ثم لا اقل من الشبهة وهى دارئة للقصاص بخلاف المال لانه يثبت مع الشبهات والباقى يعرف في المختلف

ترجمہ اور اگر گواہوں نے قصاص کی گواہی دی پھر قتل کے بعد رجوع کیا تو وہ دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے اور گواہوں سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ گواہوں سے قصاص لیا جائے گا کیونکہ گواہوں کی طرف سے قتل سبب بن کر موجود ہوا ہے۔ لہذا یہ مکرہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا بلکہ اس سے بھی بڑھ کر اسلئے کہ ولی کی اعانت کی جاتی ہے اور مکرہ کو منع کیا جاتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قتل مباشرت نہیں پایا گیا اور یونہی گواہوں کا سبب قتل ہونا ( بھی نہیں پایا گیا ) کیونکہ سبب وہ ہے جو عام طور پر مسبب تک پہنچا دے اور یہاں گواہوں کی گواہی مفضی نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ معاف کرنا مستحب ہے۔ برخلاف مکرہ کے اسلئے کہ ظاہر وہ اپنی زندگی کو ترجیح دے گا اور اسلئے کہ فعل اختیاری ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جو نسبت کو قطع کرتا ہے پھر شبہ تو سے کم نہیں ہے اور شبہ قصاص کو دور کر دیتا ہے۔ برخلاف مال کے اسلئے
If they testify to qisas, then retract after the execution, they guarantee the diyah; qisas is not taken from them. Al-Shafi'i said: qisas is taken from them because the killing occurred from them causally, so they resemble a coerced person, even more so because the heir is aided while the coerced is prevented. Our proof: direct killing did not occur, nor did causation, because a cause is that which usually leads to the effect, and here it does not, because pardon is recommended. Unlike a coerced person, because he apparently prefers his life. Also, voluntary action cuts attribution. Then there is at least doubt, and doubt prevents qisas. Unlike property, which is established despite doubts. The rest is known in al-Mukhtalaf. Translation: And if witnesses testify to qisas, then retract after the killing, they are guarantors of diyah, and qisas is not taken from them. Imam Shafi'i said: qisas will be taken from them because killing from them occurred as a cause. So they resemble a coerced person, even more so because the heir is aided and the coerced is prevented. Our proof: direct killing is not found, nor causation, because a cause is that which usually leads to its effect, and here it does not lead because pardon is recommended. Unlike the coerced, because he apparently values his life. Also, voluntary action cuts attribution. Then there is at least doubt, and doubt prevents qisas. Unlike property, which is established despite doubts.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This lesson presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding witnesses who retract after testifying to qisas (retaliatory execution) and the qisas has already been carried out. The Hanafi position: the witnesses are liable for diyah (blood money), not qisas. Imam Shafi'i argues they should face qisas because their testimony causally led to the execution, making them akin to a coercer (mukrih), and even more since the next of kin is aided while a coercer is prevented. The Hanafi response: there is no direct killing (mubasharah) nor valid causation (tasbib). A valid cause is something that usually leads to the result. Here, the witnesses' testimony does not usually lead to death because it is recommended for the heirs to pardon (affuw is mandub). So the causal link is weak. Additionally, the execution is carried out by a judge, a voluntary act that cuts the attribution. Furthermore, there is doubt (shubhah) about the validity of the retraction, and doubt prevents qisas. This doubt does not prevent financial liability (diyah), which is established despite doubts. So the Hanafi ruling stands: witnesses pay diyah, not qisas.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, specifically execution for murder.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide.
شبہ (shubhah): Doubt or ambiguity that averts hadd punishments but allows financial liability.
تسبیب (tasbib): Causation, a legal link between an act and a result, requiring it to be the common outcome.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi law, what do witnesses owe if they retract after testifying to qisas and the execution has occurred?
A) Qisas (retaliation)
B) Diyah (blood money)
C) Nothing, because retraction nullifies testimony
D) Imprisonment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, doubt and weak causation prevent qisas on retracting witnesses, limiting liability to diyah only.

Ruling on Wal' When Witnesses Retract Testimony of Emancipation
Explains that wal' remains with the original master despite witness retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wala' when witnesses retract testimony of emancipation and explain why emancipation cannot be transferred.

Core Idea
Wala' follows the emancipation; emancipation once established by qadi's judgment cannot be transferred.

This lesson examines a nuanced case from the chapter on retraction of testimonies. Witnesses testify that a master freed his slave; later they retract and pay compensation. The key legal question is whether wala' should transfer to the witnesses. The Hanafi ruling, grounded in the hadith 'al-wala'u liman a'taqa', affirms that wala' remains with the original master because emancipation itself cannot be transferred, and the qadi's judgment overrides the master's denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the main legal act under discussion? (Retraction of testimony regarding emancipation). What is the ruling? (Wala' remains with the original master).
The ruling is derived from the hadith and the principle that emancipation does not accept transfer.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary proof used by the author. Here it is the hadith 'al-wala'u liman a'taqa' (wala' is for the one who emancipates).
This hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The hadith explicitly assigns wala' to the emancipator; the imperative structure indicates obligation (wujub).
The word 'liman' (for the one) is general and inclusive.
4
Address the counterargument
What is the objection? That witnesses paid compensation and became owners, so wala' should go to them. How does the author rebut? Emancipation cannot be transferred; it is a personal act.
The text uses the principle 'al-itaq la yaqbal al-intiqal' (emancipation does not accept transfer).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the master's denial irrelevant? The qadi's judgment legally overrides the master's denial, so emancipation is attributed to the master.
The qadi's judgment is binding and gives the lie to the denier.

Chapter of Retraction from Testimonies. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume 10. The master is the one. And in the hadith it is said: 'Al-wala' is for the one who emancipates.' So when wala' is for the one who emancipates, and the emancipator in this issue is the master, then the wala' of this slave is for the master. At most it can be said that when the witnesses retracted their testimony and paid the guarantee of the slave, and the guarantor becomes the owner of the guaranteed item after paying the guarantee, then these two witnesses became owners of this slave after paying the guarantee and they became his emancipators. When these two witnesses became the emancipators of the slave, the wala' of this slave should be for these witnesses. The answer to this is that when the slave was freed by the master through the witnesses' testimony, this emancipation does not transfer to the witnesses by paying the guarantee because emancipation does not accept transfer. So when emancipation does not transfer to the witnesses, then wala', which is subordinate to emancipation, also does not transfer to the witnesses. In summary, wala' is established for the master. Question: But if it is objected that it is appropriate that wala' should not be for the master in this issue because the master denies emancipation. Because if the master did not deny emancipation, what need was there for testimony? Testifying to emancipation is proof that the master denies it. When the master denies emancipation, what question of wala' arises for him? Answer: The answer is that the master is undoubtedly a denier, but in this matter the qadi's judgment has given the lie to him legally, and one who is legally given the lie is not considered. So in this issue, the master's denial is not considered. When the master's denial is not considered, emancipation is actualized from the master and wala' goes to him.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a complex ruling-with-proof from the chapter on retraction from testimonies. The author first establishes the general principle from the hadith 'al-wala'u liman a'taqa' (clientage belongs to the one who emancipates). In the scenario, witnesses testified that a master freed his slave; the master denied it but the qadi accepted the testimony. Later the witnesses retracted and paid the slave's value to the master. The question arises: should wala' transfer to the witnesses? The author argues no, because emancipation itself cannot be transferred once it has occurred; wala' is a legal consequence of emancipation and follows it. The objection that the master's denial should negate his right to wala' is refuted: the qadi's judgment legally overrides the master's denial, so emancipation is attributed to him. The ruling is clear: wala' remains with the original master.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): The legal bond of clientage between a freed slave and his emancipator, entailing inheritance and other rights.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction; the act of a witness withdrawing his testimony after it has been accepted by the court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The master, because emancipation cannot be transferred.
C) The slave himself, because he is now free.
D) The qadi, because he gave the judgment.

Key Takeaway
Wala' remains with the original master because emancipation, once established by qadi's judgment, cannot be transferred to the witnesses who retract and pay compensation.

8 min
Liability of Retracting Witnesses: Qisas or Diya?
Inter-madhhab dispute on liability after retraction from qisas testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on witnesses' liability after retracting qisas testimony, state the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on the concepts of tasbib and shubha.

Core Idea
Retracting witnesses pay diya, not qisas, because the heir could forgive — doubt prevents the sword.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the liability of witnesses who retract after their testimony led to a qisas execution. The core issue is whether the witnesses' causation (tasbib) is strong enough to warrant qisas or whether doubt (shubha) reduces it to financial compensation (diya). Understanding how Hanafis prioritize shubha over causation in criminal cases is essential for grasping their protective approach to severe punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi position: witnesses liable for diya, not qisas. Recognize that they rely on the absence of direct killing and the principle that a cause must generally lead to the effect.
The phrase 'al-sabab ma yufdi ilayhi ghaliban' is key.
2
Identify the Shafi'i ruling and its basis
State the Shafi'i position: witnesses liable for qisas. Understand their qiyas to the one who compels (mukrih), who faces qisas despite not directly killing.
Shafi'is emphasize that the heir is assisted, unlike the one compelled who is prevented.
3
Compare views on the strength of causation
Hanafis argue that testimony does not inevitably lead to death because forgiveness is recommended. Shafi'is counter that the heir is encouraged to execute, making causation stronger than in compulsion.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in liability.
4
Understand the role of shubha in preventing qisas
Hanafis invoke shubha (doubt) as a barrier to qisas, based on the Prophetic principle 'daru’u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat'. The possibility that the witnesses were mistaken or that the heir might forgive creates doubt.
Property obligations (diya) are not blocked by shubha.
5
Note the Hanbali distinction
Imam Ahmad differentiates based on intention: if witnesses admit mistake, diya; if intentional lying, qisas. This reflects a middle position.
The Hanbali view is mentioned for comparative context.

گواہوں نے قصاص کی گواہی دی پھر قتل کے بعد رجوع کر لیا تو دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے
و ان شهدوا بقصاص ثم رجعوا بعد القتل ضمنوا الدية لا يقتص منهم وقال الشافعي يقتص منهم لوجود القتل منهم تسبيبا فاشبه المكره بل اولى لان الولى يُعان والمكره يمنع ولنا ان القتل مباشرة لم يوجد وكذا تسبيبا لأن السبب ما يفضى اليه غالبا و ههنا لا يفضى لان العفو مندوب بخلاف المكره لانه لا يؤثر حياته ظاهرا ولان الفعل الاختيارى مما يقطع النسبة ثم لا اقل من الشبهة وهى دارئة للقصاص بخلاف المال لانه يثبت مع الشبهات والباقى يعرف في المختلف
ترجمہ اور اگر گواہوں نے قصاص کی گواہی دی پھر قتل کے بعد رجوع کیا تو وہ دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے اور گواہوں سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ گواہوں سے قصاص لیا جائے گا کیونکہ گواہوں کی طرف سے قتل سبب بن کر موجود ہوا ہے۔ لہذا یہ مرہ کے مشابہ ہو گیا بلکہ اس سے بھی بڑھ کر اسلئے کہ ولی کی اعانت کی جاتی ہے اور مکرہ کو منع کیا جاتا ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قتل مباشرة نہیں پایا گیا اور یونہی گواہوں کا سبب قتل ہونا ( بھی نہیں پایا گیا ) کیونکہ سبب وہ ہے جو عام طور پر مسبب تک پہنچا دے اور یہاں گواہوں کی گواہی مفضی نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ معاف کرنا مستحب ہے۔ برخلاف مکرہ کے اسلئے کہ ظاہر وہ اپنی زندگی کو ترجیح دے گا اور اسلئے کہ فعل اختیاری ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جو سبت کو قطع کرتا ہے پھر شبہ سے تو کم نہیں ہے اور شبہ قصاص کو دور کر دیتا ہے۔ برخلاف مال کے اسلئے کہ وہ شبہات کے ساتھ ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور اس کا باقی بیان مختلف الروایۃ میں معلوم ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص مثلاً حامد نے دعوی کیا کہ خالد نے میرے باپ کو عمد انا حق قتل کیا ہے اور خالد اس کا منکر ہے۔ پھر دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ واقعتاً خالد نے حامد کے باپ کو عمد ا نا حق قتل کیا ہے قاضی نے اس شہادت پر فیصلہ دیدیا اور حامد نے اپنے باپ کے قصاص میں خالد کو تل کر ڈالا اس کے بعد گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر لیا تو یہ گواہ خالد کے ورثاء کے لئے دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے اور دیت گواہوں کے عاقلہ پر واجب ہوگی اور ان گواہوں سے قصاص نہ لیا جائے گا۔ یہی مذہب حضرت امام مالک کا ہے اور حضرت امام شافعی کے نزدیک گواہوں پر قصاص واجب ہوگا۔ امام احمد کامذ ہب یہ ہے کہ گواہوں نے اگر یہ کہا کہ ہم نے غلطی سے گواہی دی تھی تو وہ دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے اور اگر یہ کہا کہ ہم نے جان بوجھ کر جھوٹی گواہی دی تھی تو ان پر قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
امام احمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خالد تو قصاصاً گواہوں کی گواہی سے قتل کیا گیا ہے گویا اصل قاتل گواہ ہوئے ۔ اب اگر گواہوں نے خطا گواہی دے کر رجوع کیا تو یہ قتل خطا ہوا اور اگر عمدا گواہی دے کر رجوع کیا ہے تو یہ قتل عمد ا ہوا اور شریعت کے مطابق قتل خطاء میں دیت واجب ہوتی ہے اور قتل عمدا میں قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اخطاء گواہی دے کر رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں گواہ دیت کے ضامن ہوں گے اور عمدا گواہی دے کر رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں گواہ قصاص کے ضامن ہوں گے ۔ یعنی ان پر ۔
قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ گواہ خالد کے قتل میں صرف مسبب ہیں یعنی خالد کو قصاصا قتل کرنے کا سبب انھیں گواہوں کی گواہی ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر یہ گواہی نہ دیتے تو خالد کو قصاصانہ قتل کیا جاتا اور گواہ قتل کے مرتکب نہیں ہیں بلکہ قتل کا مرتکب مقتول کا ولی یعنی حامد ہے۔ اسی طرح مکرہ یعنی زبردستی کرنے والا مسبب ہے اور مرتکب نہیں ہے مثلاً عارف نے واصف سے کہا کہ تو شاہد کوقتل کر دیے۔ اگر تو شاہد کو قتل نہیں کرنے گا تو میں تجھ کو قتل کروں گا۔ پس اس اکراہ کی وجہ سے واصف نے شاہد کو تل کر دیا تو عارف اکراہ کرنے والا اس قتل میں مخلص مسبب ہے اور قتل کا مرتکب نہیں ہے۔ اور حاصل یہ کہ گواہ مسبب ہونے اور مرتکب قتل نہ ہونے میں مکر و اکراہ کرنے والے) کے مشابہ ہیں اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ کراہ کی صورت میں مکروہ (اکراہ کرنے والے) کو جو مسبب ہے نہ کہ مرتکب قصاصا ل کیا جاتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح قل کی گواہی میں چونکہ گواہ مسبب ہیں اور غیر مرتکب ہیں اس لئے رجوع عن الشہادت کے بعد ان کو بھی قصاصا قتل کیا جائے گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ گواہ مسبب ہونے میں مکرہ سے بھی بڑھ کر ہیں کیونکہ شہادت سمیت اور مفضی الی القتل ہونے میں اکراہ سے بڑھ کر ہے اس طور پر گواہوں کی گواہی کے بعد قاتل کا قتل تقریبا یقینی ہو جاتا ہے اور اس کے قتل پر ولی قصاص کی مدد بھی کی جاتی ہے اور کوئی شخص ولی قصاص کو قصاص لینے سے منع نہیں کرتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اکراہ کہ اکراہ کی صورت میں قتل یقینی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قتل نہ ہونا اغلب ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ جب عارف نے واصف کو اس بات پر مجبور کیا کہ وہ شاہد کو قتل کر دے تو واصف (مکرہ) کو شرعاً بھی اس قتل سے روکا جاتا ہے اور عادہ بھی روکا جاتا ہے۔ شرعا تو اس لئے کہ مکرہ یعنی واصف کو معلوم ہے کہ میرا یہ قتل شرعا ممنوع اور حرام ہے لہذادہ نوف آخرت اور داعیہ ایمان کی وجہ سے خود بھی اس ناحق قتل سے گریز کرے گا اور عادہ بھی کچھ نہ کچھ انسان اس طرح کی حرکتوں
And if they testify to qisas then retract after the killing, they are liable for diya; qisas is not taken from them. Al-Shafi'i said: Qisas is taken from them because killing occurred from them by causation, so it resembles compulsion, indeed more so because the heir is assisted and the one compelled is prevented. Our proof: Direct killing did not occur, nor causation, because the cause is what generally leads to the effect, and here it does not lead because forgiveness is recommended. Unlike compulsion, because he apparently does not care for his life. And because voluntary action cuts off attribution. Then there is at least doubt, and doubt prevents qisas. Unlike property because it is established despite doubts. The remainder is known in al-Mukhtalef. Translation: And if witnesses testify to qisas then retract after the killing, they become guarantors of diya and qisas is not taken from them. Imam al-Shafi'i said that qisas will be taken from them because killing occurred from them by causation. So they resemble the one who compels, indeed more so because the heir is assisted and the one compelled is prevented. And our proof is that direct killing did not exist, nor causation, because the cause is what generally leads to the effect, and here the testimony does not lead because forgiveness is recommended. Unlike compulsion because apparently he prefers his life. And because voluntary action cuts off attribution. Then there is at least doubt, and doubt prevents qisas. Unlike property because it is established despite doubts. The remainder is known in al-Mukhtalef. Explanation: The scenario is that a person, e.g. Hamid, claimed that Khalid intentionally and unjustly killed his father, and Khalid denied it. Then two witnesses testified that indeed Khalid killed Hamid's father intentionally and unjustly. The qadi gave judgment on this testimony, and Hamid killed Khalid in qisas for his father. Afterwards the witnesses retracted their testimony. Then these witnesses are guarantors of diya for the heirs of Khalid, and the diya is obligatory on the witnesses' 'aqila, and qisas is not taken from them. This is the madhhab of Imam Malik. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, qisas becomes obligatory on the witnesses. Imam Ahmad's madhhab is: if the witnesses said they testified by mistake, they are liable for diya; if they said they knowingly gave false testimony, qisas becomes obligatory on them. Imam Ahmad's proof: Khalid was killed in qisas due to the witnesses' testimony, so the real killers are the witnesses. If the witnesses retracted after testifying by mistake, it is qatl khata, and if they retracted after testifying intentionally, it is qatl 'amd. According to shari'ah, diya is obligatory for qatl khata and qisas for qatl 'amd. Therefore, in case of mistaken testimony, witnesses are liable for diya; in case of intentional false testimony, they are liable for qisas. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: The witnesses are only the cause (musabbib) of Khalid's killing; the actual perpetrator is the heir (Hamid). Just like the one who compels (mukrih) is only the cause, not the direct killer. Since the one who compels is subject to qisas, so too the witnesses. The author of al-Hidayah says the witnesses are even more cause than the one who compels because their testimony almost certainly leads to execution, whereas the one compelled may resist due to religious or natural aversion.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on the liability of witnesses who retract after their testimony led to a qisas execution. The Hanafi position (also Malik's) is that the witnesses are liable for diya (blood money), not qisas, because their action is not direct causation (tasbib) that generally leads to death—the heir might forgive (which is recommended), so the link is not strong. Hanafis argue that qisas is a severe penalty and shubha (doubt) prevents its application; here, the presence of the heir's voluntary action and the possibility of pardon create shubha. Shafi'is analogize witnesses to the one who compels (mukrih), who is liable for qisas even though he did not directly kill. They argue the witnesses are even more cause because the heir is encouraged to take qisas and not prevented. Hanbalis make a distinction based on intent: if witnesses admit they were mistaken, they pay diya; if they admit they lied intentionally, they face qisas. The commentary explains these views, with the Hanafi argument that the witnesses' testimony is not a 'cause' in the strict sense because it does not invariably lead to death (the heir may forgive). The passage also discusses the difference between causation for criminal liability (where shubha prevents qisas) and financial liability (which remains).

Key Terms
مسبب (musabbib): One who sets in motion a chain of events that leads to an effect, without directly performing it. Here, witnesses are musabbib of the killing.
شبهہ (shubha): A legal doubt or ambiguity that prevents application of severe punishments like qisas.
مکرہ (mukrih): One who compels another to commit an act; in the context, the one who compels is liable for qisas even though not the direct killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, retracting witnesses after their qisas testimony led to execution are liable for:
A) Qisas (execution)
B) Diya (blood money)
C) No liability
D) It depends on whether they admit they were mistaken

Key Takeaway
Retracting witnesses in qisas cases are liable for diya, not qisas, because the presence of shubha (doubt) and the heir's voluntary choice break the causal chain for criminal liability, but financial liability remains.

Shahadat — Testimony

8 min
Why Witnesses in Qisas Are Not Liable for Retaliation: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Arguing why witnesses are not subject to qisas while the coercer is, with proof and rebuttal of Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witnesses' liability in qisas after retraction and evaluate the Shafi'i analogy using the proofs of predominant forgiveness and shubha.

Core Idea
Forgiveness is predominant, breaking the causal link; shubha precludes qisas.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a critical inter-madhhab dispute: when witnesses in a qisas case retract their testimony after the execution, are they liable for qisas? The Hanafi school argues they are not, while Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes them to coercers. The text provides two proofs and a rebuttal that clarify the school's position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: witnesses are not liable for qisas; the coercer (if any) is liable.
The Hanafi ruling is a negation of qisas liability.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes witnesses to a coercer, arguing that since testimony causes execution, witnesses should be liable for qisas.
This is a qiyas argument.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi proof
The first proof: forgiveness is recommended and predominant, so testimony does not necessarily lead to death. Thus witnesses are not the cause of death.
The concept of 'ghalabah al-'afw' (predominance of forgiveness) breaks the causal chain.
4
Analyze the second Hanafi proof
The second proof: the act of killing is attributed to the one with valid choice (the heir), not witnesses. Even if causality is accepted, shubha (doubt) precludes qisas. Additionally, in coercion the coerced's choice is corrupted, whereas witnesses act voluntarily, so the analogy fails.
Shubha is a well-established bar to qisas in Hanafi law.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi, witnesses may still owe diyah due to financial shubha, but are not executed. Under Shafi'i, they could be executed.
Diyah is due because financial matters are not nullified by shubha.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد - ہم
ان دونوں روایات سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ معاف کرنا اللہ ، اور حبیب اللہ دونوں کے نزدیک پسندیدہ اور تقویت ایمان اور ترقی درجات کا ذریعہ ہے۔ بہر حال جب قاتل کو معاف کرنا مندوب اور باعث اجر و ثواب ہے تو اغلب یہ ہے کہ مقتول کا ولی قاتل کو معاف کر دے گا اور جب معاف کرنا اغلب ہے تو شہادت مفضی الی القتل نہ رہی اور جب شہادت مفضی الی القتل نہیں ہے تو یہ شہادت قبل کا سبب اور گواہ مسبب نہ ہوئے اس کے برخلاف مکرہ ( جس پر ا کراہ کیا گیا) ہے کہ جب اس کو کسی نے یہ دھمکی دی۔ اگر تو فلاں مثلاً شاہد کو قتل نہیں کرے گا تو ہم تجھ کو قتل کر دیں گے تو یہ اکراہ بالعموم مفضی الی القتل ہوگا کیونکہ بظاہر یہ ہے کہ مکرہ ( واصف ) اپنی زندگی کو ترجیح دے گا یعنی اپنی زندگی کی خاطر مکرہ ( واصف شاہد کو قتل کرنا گوارا کرے گا اور جب یہ بات ہے تو اکراہ مفضی الی القتل ہونے کی وجہ سے سبب قتل اور اکراہ کرنے والا ( عارف ) مسبب ہوا ۔ اور پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ قصاصا مسبب قتل کیا جاتا ہے غیر مسبب قتل کو تل نہیں کیا جا تا پس گواہ جو مسبب قتل نہیں ہیں قصاصا ان کو قتل نہیں کیا جائیگا، اور مکرہ (اکراہ کرنے والا ) چونکہ مسبب قتل ہے۔ اس لئے اس کو قتل کیا جائے گا اور چونکہ اکراہ کرنے والا مسبب ہے اور گواہ مسبب نہیں ہیں اس لیے گواہوں کو اکراہ کرنے والے پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا جیسا کہ امام شافعی نے قیاس کیا ہے۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہم اس بات کو تسلیم کرتے ہیں کہ گواہ قاتل کے قتل کا سبب ہے لیکن فعل قل جو ولی قصاص کی طرف پایا گیا ہے وہ ولی کے اختیار صحیح سے پایا گیا ہے اور جو فعل کسی سے اس کے اختیار صحیح سے صادر ہوا ہو ۔ اس کی نسبت اسی کی طرف ہوتی ہے دوسرے کی طرف نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس یہاں بھی فعل قتل کی نسبت ولی قصاص کی طرف ہوگی اور گواہوں کی طرف نہ ہوگی اور جب فعل قتل گواہوں کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے تو گواہ ، قاتل کو قصاصا قتل کرنے والے نہ ہوں گے اور جگئے قاتل کو قتل کرنے والے نہیں ہیں تو ان پر قصاص بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور اگر یہ بھی تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ گواہوں کی طرف قتل کی نسبت منقطع نہیں ہوئی ہے بلکہ بحیثیت مسبب کے ان کی طرف قتل منسوب ہے تو پھر بھی گواہوں پر قصاص واجب ہونے میں شبہ ضرور ہے کیونکہ قاتل کے قتل کا حقیقی مرتکب تو ولی ہے اور گواہ سبب قتل ہیں۔ لہذا ایک اعتبار سے یعنی سبب قتل ہونے کے اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں اور ایک اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں اور ایک ، اعتبار سے ولی قاتل ہے اور جب ایک اعتبار سے ولی قاتل ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے گواہ قاتل ہیں تو گواہوں پر قصاص واجب ہونے میں شبہ پیدا ہو گیا اور شبہ قصاص کو دور کر دیتا ہے۔ لہذا گواہوں پر سے قصاص دور کر دیا جائے گا یعنی ان پر قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ رہا یہ سوال کہ دیت چونکہ قصاص کا بدل ہے اور قصاص شبہ سے دور ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے دیت بھی شبہ سے دور ہو جانی چاہیے اور گواہوں پر قصاص کی طرح دیت بھی واجب ہونی چاہئے تھی تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دیت مالی شبہات کے ساتھ ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا دیت مالی ، شبہ کے باوجود گواہوں پر واجب ہو جائے گی اور قصاص جو شبہات سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کے ساقط ہونے سے دیت مالی ( جو شبہ سے ساقط نہیں ہوتی ) کا ساقط ہونالازم نہیں آئے گا۔
صاحب نامہ نے فرمایا کہ مکرہ یکسر الراء اکراہ کرنے والے پر) قصاص اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ گر فتح الراء ( جس پر اکراہ کیا گیا) کا اختیار فاسد ہوتا ہے اور مکرہ بکسر الراء کا اختیار صحیح ہوتا ہے اور اختیا مسیح کے مقابلے میں اختیار فاسد معدوم ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس مکرہ مافتح الراء، مکرہ بكسر الراء کیلئے بمنزلہ آلہ کے ہو گیا ہے اور فعل قتل جو کہ بفتح الراء کی طرف موجود ہوا ہے۔ وہ درحقیقت مکرم بكسر الراء کی
اشرف البدایہ جلد - دہم
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
طرف سے موجود ہوا ہے اور جب فعل قتل مکره بكسر الراء پرواجب ہوگا نہ کہ مکر و فتح الراء پر ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اس مسئلہ کا باقی بیان فقیہ ابواللیث کی مختلف الروایہ میں مذکور ہے۔
From the Book of Retraction from Testimonies: ... Forgiveness is recommended and is a means of strengthening faith and elevating ranks. So when forgiveness is predominant, the testimony is not necessarily leading to death, and witnesses are not its cause. Unlike coercion: when threatened with death, the coerced will prioritize his own life, so coercion does lead to death, making the coercer the cause. Hence witnesses, who are not the cause of death, are not executed in qisas. The coercer is executed. This refutes Imam Shafi'i's analogy. Second proof: The act of killing is attributed to the one with valid choice (the heir), not witnesses. Even if causality is accepted, there is doubt (shubha) which precludes qisas. Diyah (blood money) is due because financial matters are not nullified by doubt. The author of al-Hidayah says the remaining explanation is in Mukhtalif al-Riwayah of Faqih Abu al-Layth.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i on the liability of witnesses who testify in a qisas case and later retract. The Hanafi position is that such witnesses are not liable for qisas because their testimony does not necessarily cause death. The text provides two proofs: First, it is recommended for the victim's family to forgive, so the predominant outcome is forgiveness, breaking the causal link. Second, the act of killing is attributed to the one who exercises valid choice—the coercer, not the witnesses—and there is doubt (shubha) which precludes qisas. Imam Shafi'i analogizes witnesses to a coercer, making them liable. The Hanafi rebuttal is that in coercion the coerced's choice is corrupted, whereas witnesses act voluntarily, so the analogy fails. The text also notes that diyah is still due because financial matters are not nullified by shubha.

Key Terms
مکرہ بکسر الراء (mukrah bi-kasr al-ra'): The coercer; the one who compels another to act.
مکرہ بفتح الراء (mukrah bi-fath al-ra'): The coerced; the one who is compelled to act.
سبب (sabab): Cause; in qisas, a cause leads to death but may not result in liability if there is predominant forgiveness or shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why are witnesses who testify in a qisas case not liable for qisas if they retract?
A) Because they are minors
B) Because forgiveness is predominant and there is shubha
C) Because they were coerced
D) Because the judge is responsible

Key Takeaway
Witnesses in qisas are not liable for retaliation because forgiveness is predominant and shubha precludes qisas; they may still owe diyah.

Shahadat — Testimony

Liability of Substitute Witnesses Upon Retraction
Ruling with proof: substitute witnesses' liability upon retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on substitute witnesses who retract their testimony and explain the basis of liability (daman) using the principle of causation.

Core Idea
Substitute witnesses are liable when they retract because their testimony in court directly caused the loss.

In the system of testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada), the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) testify first, and then substitute witnesses (shuhud al-far') testify based on their testimony. If the substitute witnesses later retract, does liability fall on them? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, which holds them liable due to their direct causal role in the judgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the hukm level. The act is the retraction of substitute witnesses after judgment. The ruling: they are liable (wajib daman).
Liability here means compensation for the loss caused.
2
Understand the scenario
Clarify the specific context: shahada 'ala al-shahada – where substitute witnesses testify on behalf of original witnesses. Their testimony is given in court, leading to a judgment.
This is different from original witnesses who testify firsthand.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is rational: because the testimony was given in the judge's court (majlis al-qada), the loss (talf) is attributed to them. Attribution of loss necessitates liability.
The text uses 'lianna' (because) to indicate causation.
4
Note the consensus
The text states this ruling is bil-ittifaq (by consensus). This means all Hanafi authorities agree, strengthening the ruling's authority.
Consensus (ijma) is a primary source of law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہور فرع نے رجوع کیا تو ضامن ہوں گے
قال واذا رجع شهود الفرع ضمنوا لأن الشهادة فى مجلس القضاء صدرت منهم فكان التلف مضافاً اليهم ترجمہ اور اگر شہود فرع نے رجوع کیا تو ضامن ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ شہادت قاضی کی مجلس میں انھیں سے صادر ہوئی ہے۔ لہذا تلف کرنا بھی انہیں کی جانب منسوب ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شہادت علی الشہادت کی صورت میں شہور فرع نے اپنی شہادت سے رجوع کیا تو بالا تفاق مشہور کا ضمان انھیں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی کی عدالت میں شہود فرع نے گواہی دی ہے۔ لہذا تلف کرنا بھی انھیں کی جانب منسوب ہوگا۔ اور جب تلف کرنا ان کی جانب منسوب ہے تو ضمان بھی انھیں پر واجب ہوگا۔
Substitute witnesses will be liable if they retract. The text says: 'And if the substitute witnesses retract, they are liable because the testimony was given by them in the judge's court, so the loss is attributed to them.' Translation: And if the substitute witnesses retract, then they will be liable. Because the testimony was given by them in the judge's court. Therefore, the loss is also attributed to them. Explanation: In the case of testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada), if the substitute witnesses retract their testimony, then by consensus they are liable because they gave testimony in the judge's court. Hence the loss is attributed to them, and liability is upon them.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding substitute witnesses (shuhud al-far') who retract their testimony after a judgment has been passed. The ruling is that they are liable (daman) for the loss incurred. The proof is that their testimony was given in the court of the judge, so the resulting loss (talf) is attributed to them. Therefore, they must compensate. The text emphasizes that this is by consensus.

Key Terms
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Substitute witnesses who testify on the basis of the original witnesses' testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada).
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss caused by one's action or testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) When they retract their testimony after judgment

Key Takeaway
Substitute witnesses are liable upon retraction because their testimony in court directly caused the loss – a settled Hanafi position by consensus.
