Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Original Witnesses Not Liable If They Deny Appointing Substitute Witnesses
Ruling on liability and judgment validity upon denial of appointment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability and judgment validity when original witnesses deny appointing substitute witnesses, and explain the legal reasoning using the concepts of sabab and khabar muhtamil.

Core Idea
Denial of cause removes liability; a judgment based on a possible report cannot be overturned.

This passage examines a specific scenario in the Hanafi law of testimony: the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) retract by denying that they appointed substitute witnesses (shuhud al-far'). The ruling clarifies that they are not liable for any loss, and the judge's decision based on the substitute witnesses' testimony remains valid. The reasoning hinges on two key principles: denial of the cause (sabab) of loss and the nature of the report as khabar muhtamil (a report subject to possibility).

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the parties: original witnesses (shuhud al-asl), substitute witnesses (shuhud al-far'), and the event: original witnesses retract by denying they appointed the substitutes.
2
Identify the two legal consequences
The passage gives two rulings: (1) no liability on original witnesses, and (2) the judge's judgment remains valid.
3
Analyze the first ruling (no liability)
Liability (daman) is not wajib because the original witnesses deny the cause (sabab) of the loss, which is the appointment. Since they deny the cause, the loss is not attributed to them.
Hanafi principle: denial of cause negates liability.
4
Analyze the second ruling (judgment stands)
The judgment is not nullified because the denial is khabar muhtamil — a report that could be true or false. A finalized judgment cannot be overturned by a mere possible report.
This is analogous to a witness retracting after judgment in a regular case.
5
Note the exception before judgment
If the judge had not yet passed judgment, he would not base his decision on the substitute witnesses' testimony because the cause (the original witnesses' appointment) is denied.
The ruling differs before and after judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو رجع شهود الاصل وقالوا لم نشهد شهود الفرع على شهادتنا فلا ضمان عليهم لانهم انكروا السبب وهو الاشهاد ولا يبطل القضاء لانه خبر محتمل فصار كرجوع الشاهد بخلاف ما قبل القضاء اور اگر شہود اصل نے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ ہم نے اپنی شہادت پر شہور فرع کو شاہد مقرر نہیں کیا ہے تو شہود اصل پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول نے سب یعنی گواہ بنانے سے انکار کیا ہے اور حکم قاضی باطل نہ ہو گا اس لیے کہ یہ خبر تحتمل ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے گواہ نے خود رجوع کیا ہو۔ برخلاف حکم قضا سے پہلے کے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شہور اصل نے یہ کہا کہ ہم نے شہونا کو اپی شہادت پر شاہد نہیں بنایا ہے اور شہود فرع اپنی شہادت پر باقی ہیں تو شہود اصل پر بالا جماع ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ انھوں نے سبب اتلاف یعنی اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کیا ہے یعنی شہود فرع کی شہادت سے مدٹی علیہ کا جو مال تلف ہوا یعنی مدعی کو دینا پڑا۔ اس کا سبب ہم نہیں ہیں کیونکہ ہم نے اپنی شہادت پر شہود فرع کو شاہد نہیں بنایا ہے۔ پس جب شہود اصل سبب اتلاف کے منکر ہیں تو ان پر ضمان اتلاف بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور شہود فرع کی شہادت پر قاضی جو فیصلہ دے چکا ہے وہ بھی باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ شہود اصل کے اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کرنے میں صدق اور کذب دونوں کا احتمال ہے یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ شہو ر اصل اپنے انکار میں بچے ہوں اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ جھوٹے ہوں ، پس محض احتمال کی وجہ سے قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ اگر گواہ اصلی خود قاضی کی عدالت میں گواہی دیتے اور قاضی اس کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دیتا اور پھر یہ اصل گواہ رجوع کرتے تو ان کے رجوع کرنے سے قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوتا اسی طرح ان کے گواہ بنانے کا انکار کرنے سے بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر قاضی نے شہود فرع کی شہادت پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں دیا۔ اور فیصلہ دینے سے پہلے ہی شہود اصل نے شہود فرع کو اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کر دیا تو قاضی شہود فرع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ نہیں دے گا۔ جیسا کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر گواہ
And if the original witnesses retract and say, 'We did not make the substitute witnesses testify on our testimony,' then there is no liability upon them because they have denied the cause (the appointment). And the judgment is not nullified because it is a news report that is subject to possibility. So it is like the retraction of a witness, unlike before judgment. Translation: And if the original witnesses retract and say, 'We did not appoint the substitute witnesses as witnesses on our testimony,' then no liability is wajib on the original witnesses. Because they have denied the cause. And the judge's ruling will not be nullified because this news is subject to possibility. So it is like the witness himself retracting, unlike before judgment. Explanation: If the original witnesses say this and the substitute witnesses remain firm on their testimony, then by consensus there is no liability on the original witnesses because they deny the cause of loss. The loss is not attributed to them. The judgment stands because there is possibility of truth or falsehood. Just as if the original witnesses themselves testified and then retracted, the judgment would not be nullified. But if the judge had not yet passed judgment, he would not base it on the far' witnesses' testimony.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) who retract by denying that they appointed the substitute witnesses. The ruling: they are not liable (no daman) and the judgment remains valid. The proof is that they have denied the cause (sabab) of the loss, and the judgment is based on a report that is subject to possibility of truth and falsehood. Hence, mere denial does not nullify the judgment. This is similar to a regular witness retracting after judgment; the judgment stands. However, if the judge had not yet passed judgment, he would not rely on the far' witnesses' testimony because the cause is denied.

Key Terms
شهود الاصل (shuhud al-asl): Original witnesses whose testimony is the basis for substitute witnesses.
سبب (sabab): Cause; here, the appointment of far' witnesses is the cause that could lead to loss.
خبر محتمل (khabar muhtamil): A report that is subject to possibility (of truth or falsehood); such reports do not nullify a judgment.
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Substitute witnesses who testify based on the original witnesses' testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If original witnesses deny appointing the substitute witnesses after judgment, what happens to the judgment?
A) It is nullified
B) It remains valid
C) It is suspended pending investigation
D) The far' witnesses are executed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, denial of the cause (sabab) removes liability, and a judgment based on a possible report (khabar muhtamil) cannot be reversed by a later contradictory claim.

Liability of Subordinate Witnesses Upon Retraction
Ruling that subordinate witnesses are liable upon retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that subordinate witnesses are liable upon retraction and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on attribution of harm.

Core Idea
Subordinate witnesses who retract after verdict must compensate because their testimony caused the loss.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in the Hanafi school regarding the liability of subordinate witnesses (shuhud al-far') when they retract their testimony after a judge has passed a verdict. The passage clarifies that these witnesses are directly responsible for the loss resulting from their testimony, as it was given in the judge's presence. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish the legal consequences of retraction for different types of witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the retraction of testimony by subordinate witnesses. The ruling is that they are liable (damin) for the value lost.
Subordinate witnesses are those who testify based on the testimony of original witnesses (shahadah 'ala al-shahadah).
2
Locate the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reasoning is that the testimony was issued from them in the judge's court, so the loss is attributed to them.
Attribution of the harmful act to the witness is key for liability.
3
Note the consensus
The passage mentions 'bil-ittifaq' (by consensus) within the Hanafi school, indicating agreement among the three imams.
No intra-madhhab disagreement is recorded on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا رجع شهود الفرع ضمنوا لأن الشهادة فى مجلس القضاء صدرت منهم فكان التلف مضافاً اليهم ترجمہ اور اگر شہود فرع نے رجوع کیا تو ضامن ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ شہادت قاضی کی مجلس میں انھیں سے صادر ہوئی ہے۔ لہذا تلف کرنا بھی انہیں کی جانب منسوب ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شہادت علی الشہادت کی صورت میں شہور فرع نے اپنی شہادت سے رجوع کیا تو بالا تفاق مشہور کا ضمان انھیں پر واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی کی عدالت میں شہود فرع نے گواہی دی ہے۔ لہذا تلف کرنا بھی انھیں کی جانب منسوب ہوگا۔ اور جب تلف کرنا ان کی جانب منسوب ہے تو ضمان بھی انھیں پر واجب ہوگا۔
He said: And if the subordinate witnesses retract, they are liable, because the testimony was issued from them in the court of the judge, so the harm is attributed to them. Translation: And if the subordinate witnesses retract, they will be liable. Because the testimony was issued from them in the judge's court, therefore the loss is also attributed to them. Elaboration: The situation is that if, in the case of testimony upon testimony, the subordinate witnesses retract their testimony, then by consensus the liability of the known value is obligatory upon them, because the subordinate witnesses gave testimony in the judge's court. Therefore, the loss is also attributed to them. And when the loss is attributed to them, then liability is also obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the book of retraction regarding witnesses. It addresses the scenario where subordinate witnesses (shuhud al-far') retract their testimony after the judge has passed a verdict based on their testimony. According to Hanafi jurisprudence, these subordinate witnesses become liable (damin) for the value of the property that was lost as a result of their testimony. The reasoning is straightforward: since the testimony that caused the loss was given directly in the judge's court by these witnesses, the loss is legally attributed to their action. Therefore, they must compensate. This ruling is agreed upon (bil-ittifaq) within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شہود فرع (shuhud al-far'): Subordinate witnesses who testify based on the testimony of original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) in a case of shahadah 'ala al-shahadah.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for a loss that occurred due to one's action.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony after it has been given in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of shahadah 'ala al-shahadah, who is liable when the subordinate witnesses retract after the verdict?
A) The original witnesses
B) The subordinate witnesses
C) Neither
D) Both

Key Takeaway
Subordinate witnesses are liable for retraction after verdict because their testimony directly caused the loss in the judge's court.

Liability of Original Witnesses Upon Denying Appointment
Ruling on liability and verdict validity when original witnesses deny appointment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on liability of original witnesses when they retract by denying the appointment of subordinate witnesses, and distinguish between scenarios before and after the judge's verdict.

Core Idea
Denial of cause negates liability; a possible statement does not overturn a final judgment.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in testimony law: original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) retract their earlier claim by stating they never appointed subordinates (shuhud al-far') to testify on their behalf. The ruling clarifies that such retraction does not make them liable for losses, and crucially, it does not invalidate a verdict already passed. Understanding this distinction—before and after judgment—is essential for applying the Hanafi principles of causa (sabab) and probabilistic statements (khabar muhtamal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its hukm
Determine what is being ruled upon: the retraction of original witnesses by denial of appointment. The hukm is that they are not liable (no daman) and the verdict stands.
2
Analyze the cause (sabab) of liability
Understand that liability depends on establishing the appointment as the cause of loss. The original witnesses deny the appointment, thus negating the cause. According to Hanafi principles, liability arises from the existence of a cause; denial of cause removes liability.
3
Assess the effect on the judge's verdict
The verdict remains valid despite the retraction because the denial is a possible statement (khabar muhtamal) that could be true or false. Hanafi law holds that a probable statement does not overturn a final judgment. Contrast with the case before judgment: if no verdict has been given, the judge cannot rely on the subordinates' testimony after such denial.
4
Apply to analogous situations
Note the similarity to a witness retracting his own testimony in court after a verdict: the verdict stands. This reinforces the principle that once a judgment is passed, mere retraction (or denial) by a witness does not invalidate it.
5
Distinguish before vs. after verdict
The ruling explicitly contrasts: if denial occurs before judgment, the judge does not use the subordinates' testimony. If after, the judgment remains. This distinction is crucial for muftis and judges in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو رجع شهود الاصل وقالوا لم نشهد شهود الفرع على شهادتنا فلا ضمان عليهم لانهم انكروا السبب وهو الاشهاد ولا يبطل القضاء لانه خبر محتمل فصار كرجوع الشاهد بخلاف ما قبل القضاء اور اگر شہود اصل نے رجوع کیا اور کہا کہ ہم نے اپنی شہادت پر شہور فرع کو شاہد مقرر نہیں کیا ہے تو شہود اصل پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول نے سب یعنی گواہ بنانے سے انکار کیا ہے اور حکم قاضی باطل نہ ہو گا اس لیے کہ یہ خبر تحتمل ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے گواہ نے خود رجوع کیا ہو۔ برخلاف حکم قضا سے پہلے کے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شہور اصل نے یہ کہا کہ ہم نے شہونا کو اپی شہادت پر شاہد نہیں بنایا ہے اور شہود فرع اپنی شہادت پر باقی ہیں تو شہود اصل پر بالا جماع ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ انھوں نے سبب اتلاف یعنی اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کیا ہے یعنی شہود فرع کی شہادت سے مدٹی علیہ کا جو مال تلف ہوا یعنی مدعی کو دینا پڑا۔ اس کا سبب ہم نہیں ہیں کیونکہ ہم نے اپنی شہادت پر شہود فرع کو شاہد نہیں بنایا ہے۔ پس جب شہود اصل سبب اتلاف کے منکر ہیں تو ان پر ضمان اتلاف بھی واجب نہ ہوگا اور شہود فرع کی شہادت پر قاضی جو فیصلہ دے چکا ہے وہ بھی باطل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ شہود اصل کے اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کرنے میں صدق اور کذب دونوں کا احتمال ہے یعنی یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ شہو ر اصل اپنے انکار میں بچے ہوں اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ جھوٹے ہوں ، پس محض احتمال کی وجہ سے قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ اگر گواہ اصلی خود قاضی کی عدالت میں گواہی دیتے اور قاضی اس کے مطابق فیصلہ کر دیتا اور پھر یہ اصل گواہ رجوع کرتے تو ان کے رجوع کرنے سے قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوتا اسی طرح ان کے گواہ بنانے کا انکار کرنے سے بھی قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر قاضی نے شہود فرع کی شہادت پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں دیا۔ اور فیصلہ دینے سے پہلے ہی شہود اصل نے شہود فرع کو اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنانے کا انکار کر دیا تو قاضی شہود فرع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ نہیں دے گا۔ جیسا کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کرنے سے پہلے اگر گواہ گواہی سے رجوع کر لیں تو قاضی فیصلہ نہیں دیتا ہے۔
And if the original witnesses retract and say, 'We did not make the subordinate witnesses testify upon our testimony,' then there is no liability upon them because they denied the cause, which is the appointment, and the judgment is not invalidated because it is a possible statement, so it becomes like the retraction of a witness, contrary to before the judgment. And if the original witnesses said, 'We did not appoint the subordinate witnesses as witnesses upon our testimony,' and the subordinate witnesses remain upon their testimony, then by consensus there is no liability upon the original witnesses, because they denied the cause of loss, i.e., making witnesses upon their testimony. That is, the loss of the defendant's property due to the testimony of the subordinates happened; its cause is not us because we did not appoint the subordinates as witnesses upon our testimony. So when the original witnesses deny the cause of loss, loss liability is not obligatory upon them, and the judgment that the judge gave based on the subordinates' testimony will not be invalidated, because the original witnesses' denial of making witnesses upon their testimony has the possibility of truth and falsehood. That is, it is possible that the original witnesses are truthful in their denial, and it is also possible that they are lying. So merely due to possibility, the judge's judgment is not invalidated. Just as if the original witnesses themselves give testimony in the judge's court and the judge gives a verdict accordingly, and then these original witnesses retract, their retraction does not invalidate the judge's verdict. Similarly, their denial of making witnesses does not invalidate the judge's verdict. And if the judge has not given any verdict based on the testimony of the subordinates, and before the verdict, the original witnesses deny making the subordinates as witnesses upon their testimony, then the judge will not give a verdict based on the testimony of the subordinates. Just as before the judge's verdict, if a witness retracts his testimony, the judge does not give a verdict.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This ruling discusses the situation where original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) retract their testimony by claiming that they never appointed the subordinate witnesses (shuhud al-far') to testify on their behalf. In this case, the original witnesses are not liable for any loss because they deny the cause of loss—the appointment. Since their denial is a statement that could be true or false (it is khabar muhtamal), the judge's verdict that has already been passed based on the subordinates' testimony remains valid. The reasoning is similar to when an original witness retracts after giving testimony in court: the verdict stands. However, if the judge has not yet passed a verdict, this denial prevents the judge from using the subordinates' testimony. This distinction before and after the verdict is crucial.

Key Terms
شہود اصل (shuhud al-asl): Original witnesses who possess the primary knowledge of the event and may appoint subordinate witnesses to convey their testimony.
سبب (sabab): The cause or legal reason for liability; here, the appointment of subordinates is the cause leading to the loss.
خبر محتمل (khabar muhtamal): A statement that admits of both truth and falsehood, as opposed to decisive evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If original witnesses retract by saying they never appointed the subordinates, and the judge has already passed a verdict, what happens?
A) The original witnesses are liable
B) The verdict is invalidated
C) The original witnesses are not liable and the verdict stands
D) The judge must retry the case

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, original witnesses who deny appointing subordinates after a verdict are not liable, and the verdict remains valid because their denial is a probable statement.

Liability When Original Witnesses Withdraw After Appointing Substitutes
Ruling on daman when asl say they appointed far' and made a mistake

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on daman when original witnesses (asl) withdraw after appointing substitutes (far') and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Agency of substitutes: Imam Muhammad holds asl liable for withdrawal; Sahibayn do not.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if original witnesses appoint substitutes to testify, but later withdraw their own testimony, are they liable for damages? The answer hinges on whether the substitutes are mere transmitters or representatives. We will explore the proofs of Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and see which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
What is the factual situation? Original witnesses (asl) appoint substitutes (far') to testify. The judge rules based on far'’s testimony. Then asl say they made a mistake (or withdraw). Are asl liable?
2
State Imam Muhammad’s position and proof
Imam Muhammad holds asl liable because far' are representatives (qaim maqam) of asl. Their withdrawal is as if asl themselves withdrew in court, causing loss.
3
State Sahibayn’s position and proof
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold asl not liable because the judge ruled on far'’s testimony, which was witnessed directly. Asl’s withdrawal has no effect on the judgment.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Imam Muhammad’s view, asl must compensate; under Sahibayn’s view, no compensation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is Sahibayn’s (no liability on asl).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الرجوع عن الشهادات
شہود اصل نے کہا کہ ہم نے شہود فرع کو مقرر کیا تھا اور ہم نے غلطی کی تو ضامن ہوں گے یا نہیں اقوال فقہاء
و ان قالوا اشهدناهم وغلطنا ضمنوا و هذا عند محمد وعند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف لا ضمان عليهم لان القضاء وقع بشهادة الفروع لان القاضى يقضى بما يعاين من الحجة وهى شهادتهم وله ان الفروع نقلوا شهادة الاصول فصار كانهم حضروا
ترجمہ اور اگر شہود اصل نے کہا کہ ہم نے فروع کو گواہ کیا تھا اور ہم نے غلطی کی ہے تو اصول ضامن ہوں گے اور یہ امام محمد کے نزدیک ہے اور امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اصلی گواہوں پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قاضی کا حکم فروع کی شہادت پر واقع ہوا ہے کیونکہ قاضی اسی حجت کے ساتھ حکم کرتا ہے۔ جس کا وہ مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور وہ فروع کی گواہی ہے اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فروع نے اصول کی گواہی نقل کی ہے پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا اصول خود حاضر تھے۔ تشریح اگر شہود اصل نے کہا کہ ہم نے فروع کو اپنی شہادت پر شاہد بنایا تھا لیکن ہم سے غلطی ہوئی یا یوں کہا کہ ہم نے ان کو شاہد بنایا تھا مگر رجوع کر لیا تھا تو ان دونوں قول میں امام محمد کے نزدیک شہود اصل ضامن ہوں گے۔ اور شیخین کے نزدیک شہود اصل پر ضمان واجب نہ ہو گا۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاضی کا فیصلہ فروع کی شہادت پر واقع ہوا ہے، اس لئے کہ قاضی اس حجت پر فیصلہ صادر کرتا ہے جس کا وہ مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور قاضی نے فروع کی شہادت کا مشاہدہ کیا ہے نہ کہ اصول کی شہادت کا کیونکہ فروع کی شہادت قاضی کی مجلس میں موجود ہوئی ہے نہ کہ اصول کی شہادت۔ بہر حال قاضی نے جب فروع کی شہادت کا مشاہدہ کیا ہے تو فروع کی شہادت حجت ہوگی اور اسی کے مطابق قاضی فیصلہ دے گا اور اصل کی شہادت چونکہ مجلس قاضی میں نہیں پائی گئی، اس لئے اصول کی شہادت حجت نہ ہو گی اور قاضی نے ان کی شہادت پر فیصلہ نہیں دیا ہے تو ان کا اپنی شہادت سے رجوع کرنا اتلاف کا سبب بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب اصول کا رجوع کرنا اتلاف کا سبب نہیں ہے تو ان پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شہود فرع، شہود اصل کی شہادت قاضی کی مجلس کی طرف منتقل کرنے میں شہود اصل کے قائم مقام ہیں۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قضائے قاضی کے لئے شہود اصل کا عادل ہونا بھی شرعاً معتبر ہے۔ بہر حال جب فروع، اصول کے قائم مقام ہیں اور فروع نے اصول ہی کی شہادت قاضی کی عدالت میں نقل کی ہے۔ تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا شہود اصل نے مجلس قاضی میں خود حاضر ہو کر گواہی دی ہے اور پھر مجلس میں حاضر ہو کر رجوع کیا ہے، اور ایسا کرنے سے اصول پر ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے، لہذا مذکورہ مسئلے میں بھی اصول پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
Book of Withdrawal from Testimony. The original witnesses said: 'We appointed the substitute witnesses and we made a mistake.' Will they be liable? Statements of the jurists: And if they said: 'We made them witnesses and we made a mistake,' they are liable, and this is according to Muhammad. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, there is no liability upon them because the judgment occurred on the testimony of the substitutes, for the judge judges by what he sees of the proof, which is their testimony. And his (Muhammad's) proof is that the substitutes transmitted the testimony of the originals, so it is as if they were present. Translation: And if the original witnesses said: 'We made the substitutes witnesses and we made a mistake,' then the originals will be liable, and this is according to Imam Muhammad. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, there is no liability upon the original witnesses. Because the judge's ruling occurred on the testimony of the substitutes, since the judge rules by the proof he witnesses, and that is the testimony of the substitutes. And Imam Muhammad's proof is that the substitutes transmitted the testimony of the originals, so it became as if the originals themselves were present. Explanation: If the original witnesses said: 'We made the substitutes witnesses upon our testimony, but we made a mistake' or said: 'We made them witnesses but we withdrew,' then in both statements, according to Imam Muhammad, the original witnesses will be liable. And according to the two shaykhs, liability is not obligatory upon the original witnesses. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the judge's ruling occurred on the testimony of the substitutes, because the judge issues a ruling on the proof he witnesses, and the judge witnessed the testimony of the substitutes, not the testimony of the originals, because the testimony of the substitutes was present in the judge's court, not the testimony of the originals. In any case, when the judge witnessed the testimony of the substitutes, the testimony of the substitutes is the proof, and accordingly the judge will give a ruling. And since the testimony of the originals was not present in the judge's court, their testimony is not proof, and the judge did not rule on their testimony. Therefore, their withdrawal from their testimony is not a cause of loss, and when their withdrawal is not a cause of loss, liability is not obligatory upon them. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the substitute witnesses stand in place of the original witnesses in transmitting the testimony of the originals to the judge's court. This is why the uprightness ('adl) of the original witnesses is legally considered for the judge's ruling. In any case, when the substitutes are the representatives of the originals and they transmitted the testimony of the originals to the judge's court, it becomes as if the original witnesses themselves were present in the judge's court and gave testimony, and then withdrew while present in the court. And doing so makes liability obligatory upon the originals. Therefore, in the mentioned issue, liability is obligatory upon the originals.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability (daman) of original witnesses (shuhud asl) when they withdraw from their testimony after having appointed substitute witnesses (shuhud far'). The core issue: if the originals say they appointed the substitutes but made a mistake (or later withdrew), are they liable for damages if the judge ruled based on the substitutes' testimony? Imam Muhammad holds that the originals are liable because the substitutes act as their representatives in transmitting testimony; thus, it is as if the originals themselves testified and then withdrew in court. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that no liability falls on the originals because the judge's ruling is based solely on the testimony of the substitutes, which was directly witnessed in court. The originals' testimony was never presented, so their withdrawal has no effect on the judgment, and thus no liability. The passage then elaborates on the reasoning of each side: the shaykhs emphasize the judge's reliance on what is directly observed (mushahada), while Imam Muhammad emphasizes the agency of the substitutes in conveying the originals' testimony. This difference leads to a practical consequence: according to Imam Muhammad, the originals are liable; according to the shaykhs, they are not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is generally that of the two shaykhs, but the text presents both views with their proofs.

Key Terms
شہود اصل (shuhud al-asl): Original witnesses who appoint substitutes to testify on their behalf.
شہود فرع (shuhud al-far'): Substitute witnesses who testify based on the original witnesses' testimony.
ضمان (daman): Liability for damages, here due to causing loss (itlaf) of the subject matter through withdrawal of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why are original witnesses liable when they withdraw after appointing substitutes?
A) Because they directly testified in court
B) Because the substitutes are their representatives, making their withdrawal equivalent to withdrawing in court
C) Because they made a mistake in appointing the substitutes
D) Because the judge relied on their testimony

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the relied-upon position is that original witnesses are not liable for damages when they withdraw after appointing substitutes, because the judge's ruling is based on the substitutes' testimony.

Liability When Both Original and Substitute Witnesses Withdraw
Ruling on daman when both asl and far' withdraw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on daman when both original and substitute witnesses withdraw, and apply the mufta bihi ruling (Sahibayn's view) to a given scenario.

Core Idea
When both witness groups withdraw, only the substitutes are liable because the judgment was based on their testimony.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in testimony liability. After a judgment based on substituted testimony, both the original witnesses (asl) and the substitute witnesses (far') may withdraw their testimony, causing loss to the defendant. The Hanafi imams differ on who should compensate. Understanding their reasoning—particularly the concept of jihat mutaghayira (mutually exclusive bases)—illuminates how Hanafi law assigns liability for damages arising from judicial decisions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the dispute
Note that there are two groups: original witnesses (asl) and substitute witnesses (far'). Both withdraw after a judgment. The dispute is about who bears the daman (financial liability).
The defendant is the one who suffered loss from the judgment.
2
State the Sahibayn position and its proof
According to Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), only the far' are liable. Their proof: the judge ruled based on the far''s testimony because he witnessed it directly in court. The far''s withdrawal is the direct cause of loss (itlaf).
The asl's testimony was only transmitted through the far'; the judge never witnessed it directly.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and its proof
Imam Muhammad gives the defendant the option to hold either the asl or the far' liable. His proof: the judgment also rests on the asl's testimony because the far' are representatives (nāqilūn) of the asl's testimony. Both bases are valid but mutually exclusive (jihat mutaghayira).
The option cannot be exercised against both; the defendant must choose one group.
4
Identify the mufta bihi and the sub-case
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Sahibayn's view: only the far' are liable. Also note the sub-case: if the far' later accuse the asl of lying or mistake, their statement is disregarded—the judgment stands and they remain liable as they did not withdraw their own testimony.
This sub-case reinforces that liability attaches to the far' for their own withdrawal, not for the asl's purported error.

تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر اصول اور فروع دونوں گروہ نے شہادت سے رجوع کیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک فقط فروع پر ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی کا حکم فروع کی شہادت پر واقع ہوا ہے اور قاضی کا حکم فروع کی شہادت پر اس لئے واقع ہوا ہے کہ قاضی اس حجت پر فیصلہ کرتا ہے جس کا وہ مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور فروع کی شہادت چونکہ قاضی کی مجلس میں موجود ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی فروع کی شہادت اور حجت کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور جب قاضی فروع کی شہادت کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے تو اس پر فیصلہ دے گا اور جب قاضی نے فروع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے تو فروع کا رجوع کرنا ہی مشہور بہ کے اتلاف کا سبب ہوگا اور جب فروع کا رجوع کرنا اتلاف مشہود کا سبب ہے تو ضمان فروع ہی پر واجب ہوگا اصول پر واجب نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام محمد کے نزدیک مدعی علیہ کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے وہ اصول کو ضامن بنائے اور جی چاہے فروع کو ضامن بنائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شیخین کی بیان کردہ دلیل سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی نے فروع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے اور امام محمد کی بیان کردہ دلیل "ان الفروع نقلوا شهادة الاصول" سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی نے اصول کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے۔ پس شیخین کی بیان کردہ دلیل کا تقاضا ہے کہ رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں فروع پر ضمان واجب ہو اور امام محمد کی بیان کردہ دلیل کا تقاضا ہے کہ اصول پر ضمان واجب ہو اور دونوں پر عمل کرنا چونکہ اولی ہے اس نسبت ایک کو ترک کرنے کے۔ اس لئے دونوں دلیلوں پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مدعی علیہ کو اختیار دیا گیا کہ وہ اصول کو ضامن بنائے لیکن اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ دونوں دلیلوں کو جمع کر کے آدھے آدھے کا ضامن اصول اور فروع کو کیا جائے تو جواب ہے کہ دونوں جہتیں متغائر ہیں اس لئے جمع نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔
And if the originals and the substitutes both withdraw, liability according to them (the two shaykhs) is only on the substitutes, because the judgment occurred on their testimony. And according to Muhammad, the defendant has the option: if he wishes he can hold the originals liable, and if he wishes he can hold the substitutes liable, because the judgment occurred on the testimony of the substitutes from the aspect they mentioned, and on the testimony of the originals from the aspect he mentioned. So he is given choice between them, and the two aspects are different, so they are not combined in imposing liability. And if the substitute witnesses say: 'The original witnesses lied or made a mistake in that,' no attention is paid to that, because what has been executed of the judgment is not invalidated by their statement, and liability is not obligatory upon them, because they did not withdraw from their testimony; they only testified against others regarding withdrawal. Translation: And if both groups, the originals and the substitutes, withdrew, then according to the two shaykhs, liability is only on the substitutes, because the judge's ruling occurred on their testimony. And according to Imam Muhammad, the defendant has the option: if he wishes he can hold the originals liable, and if he wishes he can hold the substitutes liable. Because the judgment occurred on the testimony of the substitutes in the manner mentioned by the two shaykhs, and on the testimony of the originals in the manner mentioned by Imam Muhammad. Therefore, he has a choice between them, and the two aspects are mutually exclusive. So they cannot be combined in imposing liability. And if the substitutes say that the originals are lying or made a mistake in that, their statement is not paid attention to, because the judgment that has passed is not invalidated by their statement, and liability is not obligatory upon them, because they did not withdraw from their testimony; they only testified about the withdrawal of others. Explanation: The author of Al-Hidayah said that if both groups withdrew from testimony, then according to the two shaykhs, liability is only on the substitutes, because the judge's ruling occurred on the testimony of the substitutes. And the judge's ruling occurred on the testimony of the substitutes because the judge rules on the proof he witnesses, and since the substitutes' testimony is present in the judge's court, the judge witnesses their testimony and proof, and when he witnesses it, he gives a ruling accordingly. And when the judge gave a ruling on the substitutes' testimony, the substitutes' withdrawal is the cause of loss of the subject matter. Since their withdrawal is the cause of loss, liability is only on them, not on the originals. According to Imam Muhammad, the defendant has the option: if he wishes he can hold the originals liable, and if he wishes he can hold the substitutes liable. The proof is that from the proof presented by the two shaykhs, it is understood that the judge ruled on the testimony of the substitutes, and from Imam Muhammad's proof, 'the substitutes transmitted the testimony of the originals,' it is understood that the judge ruled on the testimony of the originals. Thus, the implication of the two shaykhs' proof is that upon withdrawal, liability is on the substitutes, and the implication of Imam Muhammad's proof is that liability is on the originals. Since acting on both proofs is preferable to abandoning one, the defendant is given the option to hold either liable. But if someone objects that the two proofs could be combined by making each liable for half, the answer is that the two aspects are different, so they cannot be combined.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on withdrawal from testimony, now considering the scenario where both the original witnesses (asl) and the substitute witnesses (far') withdraw their testimony. The passage also addresses a separate sub-case where the far' accuse the asl of lying or mistake after the judgment. The intra-Hanafi dispute continues: Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that only the substitutes are liable for damages (daman) because the judge's ruling was based solely on their testimony, which was witnessed in court. Imam Muhammad gives the defendant (the party against whom the judgment was given) the option to hold either the originals or the substitutes liable. This is because, from one perspective, the ruling is on the substitutes' testimony (as Sahibayn argue), and from another, it is on the originals' testimony (as the substitutes are their representatives). Since both perspectives are valid, the defendant may choose which group to pursue, but cannot hold both liable simultaneously because the two bases are mutually exclusive. The third sub-case: if the substitutes themselves later claim that the originals were lying or mistaken, this statement is disregarded entirely. The judgment stands, and the substitutes are not liable because they have not withdrawn their own testimony; they merely accused others of wrongdoing. The commentary by the author of Al-Hidayah (likely al-Marghinani) explains the reasoning in detail, emphasizing that the defendant's option in Imam Muhammad's view is a way to honor both proofs. It also refutes a potential objection that liability could be split between the two groups, stating that since the two bases are different, they cannot be combined.

Key Terms
مدعی علیہ (mudda'a 'alayhi): The defendant against whom the judgment was passed; he is the one who can claim damages from the witnesses.
اتلاف (itlaf): Causing loss or damage to the property or right in question; here, the withdrawal of testimony causes loss to the defendant.
جہت متغائر (jihat mutaghayira): Mutually exclusive aspects or bases; here, the bases for liability of asl and far' are different and cannot be combined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, when both original and substitute witnesses withdraw after a judgment, who is liable for damages?
A) Both groups are jointly liable
B) Only the original witnesses (asl) are liable
C) Only the substitute witnesses (far') are liable
D) The defendant may choose which group to hold liable

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute over liability when both witness groups withdraw, the relied-upon position holds only the substitutes liable, as the judgment was based on their directly witnessed testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony

Liability When Original and Branch Witnesses Retract
Dispute on liability between original and branch witnesses after retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on liability when both original and branch witnesses retract, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the dispute.

Core Idea
When both original and branch witnesses retract, the two shaykhs hold only branches liable; Muhammad gives the defendant a choice.

The testimony of branch witnesses (shuhud al-far') is based on the testimony of original witnesses (shuhud al-asl). When both groups retract after a judgment has been passed, who is responsible for the loss? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on this question, focusing on the reasoning behind each position and the practical implications for litigants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is retraction (ruju') of testimony after a judgment has been based on it. The dispute is: when both original and branch witnesses retract, who must compensate the defendant?
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that only the branch witnesses are liable. Imam Muhammad holds that the defendant may choose to hold either the originals or the branches liable.
3
Trace the reasoning behind each position
The two shaykhs argue that the judge's ruling was based directly on the branch testimony present in court, so retraction by branches causes the loss. Muhammad argues the ruling can be attributed to both: branches as transmitters, originals as the basis. Therefore the defendant may choose.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the two shaykhs, the defendant can only claim from branches; under Muhammad, from either group. This affects the defendant's chance of recovery and the witnesses' exposure to liability.
The two aspects (original and branch testimony) are distinct, so they cannot be combined in a single liability.
5
Examine the scenario where branches accuse originals of falsehood
If after judgment the branches say the originals lied or erred, this statement is not heeded and does not impose liability on the branches, because they did not retract their own testimony.
The judge's ruling is not invalidated by mere allegation, and liability only follows retraction by the testifier themselves.

و لو رجع الاصول والفروع جميعا يجب الضمان عندهما على الفروع لا غير لان القضاء وقع بشهادتهم وعند محمد المشهود عليه بالخيار ان شاء ضمن الأصول وان شاء ضمن الفروع لان القضاء وقع بشهادة الفروع من الوجه الذى ذكرا وبشهادة الاصول من الوجه الذى ذكر فيتخير بينهما والجهتان متغايرتان فلا يجمع بينهم في التضمين وان قال شهود الفرع كذب شهود الاصل او غلطوا في ذلك لم يُلتفت الى ذلك لان ما أمضى من القضاء لا ينتقض بقولهم ولا يجب الضمان عليهم لانهم ما رجعوا عن شهادتهم انما شهدوا على غيرهم بالرجوع

ترجمہ اور اگر اصول اور فروع دونوں گروہ نے رجوع کیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک صرف فروع پر ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ اس لیے کہ قاضی کا حکم انھیں کی شہادت پر واقع ہوا ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک مدعی علیہ کو اختیار ہے۔ اگر چاہے تو اصول کو ضامن بنائے اور اگر چاہیے فروع کو ضامن بنائے ۔ اس لئے کہ قضاء فروع کی شہادت پر اس طریقہ سے واقع ہوئی ہے جو شیخین نے ذکر کیا ہے اور اصول کی شہادت پر اس طریقہ سے واقع ہوئی ہے جو امام محمد نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ لہذا اس کو دونوں کے درمیان اختیار ہوگا اور دونوں جہتیں باہم متفائر ہیں۔ لہذا ضامن بنانے میں اصول اور فروع دونوں کو جمع نہیں کیا جائے گا اور اگر فروع نے کہا کہ شہود اصل جھوٹے ہیں یا انھوں نے اس بارے میں غلطی کی ہے تو ان کے اس قول کی طرف توجہ نہیں کی جائے گی کیونکہ حکم قضاء جو گزر چکا ان کے قول سے نہیں ٹوٹے گا اور فروع پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ انھوں نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اپنے علاوہ پر رجوع کرنے کی گواہی دی ہے ۔

تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر اصول اور فروع دونوں گروہ نے شہادت سے رجوع کیا تو شیخین کے نزدیک فقط فروع پر ضمان واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قاضی کا حکم فروع کی شہادت پر واقع ہوا ہے اور قاضی کا حکم فروع کی شہادت پر اس لئے واقع ہوا ہے کہ قاضی اس حجت پر فیصلہ کرتا ہے جس کا وہ مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور فروع کی شہادت چونکہ قاضی کی مجلس میں موجود ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی فروع کی شہادت اور حجت کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے اور جب قاضی فروع کی شہادت کا مشاہدہ کرتا ہے تو اس پر فیصلہ دے گا اور جب قاضی نے فروع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے تو فروع کا رجوع کرنا ہی مشہور بہ کے اتلاف کا سبب ہوگا اور جب فروع کا رجوع کرنا اتلاف مشہود کا سبب ہے تو ضمان فروع ہی پر واجب ہوگا اصول پر واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ حضرت امام محمد کے نزدیک مدعی علیہ کو اختیار ہے جی چاہے وہ اصول کو ضامن بنائے اور جی ہے فروع کو ضامن بنائے ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شیخین کی بیان کردہ دلیل سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی نے فروع کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے اور اما محمد کی بیان کردہ دلیل "ان الفروع نقلوا شهادة الاصول" سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قاضی نے اصول کی شہادت پر فیصلہ دیا ہے۔ پس شیخین کی بیان کردہ دلیل کا تقاضا ہے کہ رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں فروع پر ضمان واجب ہو اور امام محمد کی بیان کردہ دلیل کا تقاضا ہے کہ اصول پر ضمان واجب ہو اور دونوں پر عمل کرنا چونکہ اولی ہے یہ نسبت ایک کو ترک کرنے کے۔ اس لئے دونوں دلیلوں پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مدعی عالیہ کو اختیار دیا گیا کہ وہ اصول کو ضامن بنائے لیکن اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ دونوں دلیلوں کو جمع کر کے آدھے آدھے کا ضامن اصول اور فروع دونوں گروہ کو کیوں نہیں بنایا گیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ دونوں دلیلیں بالکل متفائز ہیں کیونکہ شہادت اصول ، اصل حق پر ہے اور شہادت فروع، شہادت اصول پر ہے اور ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی مجانست نہیں ہے اور جب ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی مجانست نہیں ہے اور اصول اور فروع کو شہادت واحدہ کے حکم میں قرار دے کر ضامن بنانے میں سب کو اکھٹا نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ ہر فریق کو علیحدہ علیحد ضامن بنانے میں مدعی علیہ کو اختیار ہوگا۔

صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر قضائے قاضی کے بعد شہود فرع نے کہا کہ شہود اصل نے مدعی علیہ پر جھوٹی گواہی دی، یا شہود اصل نے اس بارے میں غلطی کی تو شہود فرع کے اس قول کی طرف توجہ نہیں کی جائے گی، کیوں کہ قاضی جو فیصلہ دے چکا ہے وہ ان کے اس قول کی وجہ سے باطل نہ ہوگا ۔ اسلئے کہ ان کے اس قول میں صدق اور کذب دونوں کا احتمال ہے اور احتمال کی وجہ سے قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا قاضی کا فیصلہ باطل نہ ہوگا اور اس کہنے کی وجہ سے فروع پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ فروع نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اس بات کی گواہی دی ہے کہ اصول نے اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کیا ہے اور یہ قطعا مفید نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال یہ کہنے سے فروع ضامن نہ ہوں گے اور اصول نے بھی چونکہ قاضی کی مجلس میں رجوع نہیں کیا ہے ۔ اس لئے وہ بھی ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔
And if both the original (asl) and branch (far') witnesses retract, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) the liability is upon the branch witnesses only, because the judgment was based on their testimony. According to Muhammad, the defendant has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the original witnesses liable, and if he wishes, he may hold the branch witnesses liable, because the judgment was based on the testimony of the branch witnesses from the aspect mentioned by the two, and based on the testimony of the original witnesses from the aspect mentioned by him, so he chooses between them. The two aspects are distinct, so they are not combined in holding liable. And if the branch witnesses say, 'The original witnesses lied or erred in that,' it is not heeded, because the judgment that has been passed is not invalidated by their statement, and liability is not incumbent upon them because they did not retract their testimony; they only testified against others regarding retraction.

Translation: And if both original and branch groups retracted, according to the two shaykhs, only the branch witnesses are liable, because the judge's ruling was based on their testimony. According to Imam Muhammad, the defendant has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the originals liable, and if he wishes, the branches. Because the ruling was based on the branch testimony in the manner mentioned by the two, and on the original testimony in the manner mentioned by Imam Muhammad. Therefore, he has choice between them. The two aspects are distinct, so the originals and branches are not combined in liability. And if the branch witnesses say that the original witnesses lied or erred, their statement is not heeded, because the judge's ruling that has passed is not invalidated by their statement, and liability is not obligatory upon the branches because they did not retract their own testimony; they only testified about others' retraction.

Commentary: The author of Hidayah said: If both original and branch witnesses retract, according to the two shaykhs, only the branches are liable because the judge's ruling was based on the branch testimony. The judge rules on the proof he observes, and branch testimony is present in the judge's court, so he observes it and rules based on it. When the judge rules on branch testimony, the retraction of the branches causes the loss of the subject matter, so liability is on them, not on the originals. According to Imam Muhammad, the defendant has a choice to hold either group liable. The evidence: The reasoning of the two shaykhs indicates the judge ruled on branch testimony; Imam Muhammad's reasoning (that the branches transmitted the originals' testimony) indicates the judge ruled on original testimony. Acting on both proofs is better than abandoning one, so the defendant is given a choice. If it is objected that the proofs could be combined by holding each group half-liable, the answer is that the two proofs are completely distinct: the originals' testimony is on the original right, the branches' testimony is on the originals' testimony, and there is no similarity between them. So they are not combined as a single testimony; the defendant has the choice to hold either group liable.

The author of Hidayah said: If after the judge's ruling the branch witnesses say that the original witnesses gave false testimony or erred, their statement is not heeded because the judge's ruling is not invalidated by their statement, as it involves the possibility of truth or falsehood, and probability does not invalidate a judge's ruling. Also, no liability is on the branches because they did not retract their own testimony; they only testified that the originals retracted, which is of no effect. Thus, the branches are not liable, and the originals also did not retract in the judge's court, so they too are not liable.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage addresses a ruling on retraction of testimony when both original witnesses (who witnessed the event) and branch witnesses (who testify based on original witnesses' testimony) retract after the judge's ruling. The passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute. The position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) is that only the branch witnesses are liable to compensate the defendant if they retract, because the judge's ruling was directly based on their testimony in court. Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that the defendant has a choice: he may hold either the original witnesses or the branch witnesses liable, because the ruling can be attributed to both: the branches for transmitting, and the originals for providing the basis. The two aspects are distinct, so they cannot be combined in a single liability claim. The passage also discusses a scenario where branch witnesses accuse original witnesses of falsehood or error; this is disregarded because it does not constitute a retraction by the branches themselves and the judge's ruling is not overturned by mere allegation. Nor are the branches liable in this case, as they did not retract their own testimony. The commentary by the author of Hidayah explains the reasoning: the judge rules on what he observes, and only branch testimony is observed in court; Muhammad's view considers the original testimony as the basis. The dispute is resolved by giving the defendant a choice, as acting on both evidences is preferable to discarding one. An objection about splitting liability is rejected due to the distinct nature of the two testimonies.

Key Terms
اصل (asl): Original witness who directly witnessed the event.
فرع (far'): Branch witness who testifies based on the original witness's testimony.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of testimony after it has been given and acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, when both original and branch witnesses retract after a judgment based on their testimony, who is liable?
A) Both original and branch witnesses equally
B) Only the original witnesses
C) Only the branch witnesses
D) The defendant has a choice

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, when both original and branch witnesses retract after judgment, the two shaykhs hold only branches liable, while Imam Muhammad gives the defendant a choice.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Liability When Character Witnesses Retract Their Testimony
Dispute on liability of character witnesses when they retract their testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the liability of character witnesses who retract their tazkiyah, and explain the reasoning based on the concept of 'illat al-'illah.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah as ‘illat al-‘illah makes retracting character witnesses liable; as a mere condition, they are not.

In Hanafi law, character witnesses (muzakkiyun) may testify to the probity of main witnesses. What happens if they later retract? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The outcome turns on a subtle distinction: is tazkiyah a cause that enables the judge’s ruling, or merely a condition?

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: character witnesses are liable upon retraction.
Abu Hanifa holds that they must compensate the defendant.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State the position of the Sahibayn: they are not liable.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the analogy: the Sahibayn compare tazkiyah to witnesses of chastity (shuhud al-ihsan), which is a pure condition.
A condition does not cause the ruling, so retraction does not create liability.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes: tazkiyah is 'illat al-'illah (the cause that gives effect to the main testimony).
Without tazkiyah, the judge cannot act; hence it is a cause of the cause, not a mere condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the character witnesses pay compensation; under the Sahibayn, they do not.
This affects who bears the loss when character testimony is retracted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان رجع المزكون عن التزكية ضمنوا ولهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يضمنون لانهم اثنوا على الشهود خيرا فصاروا كشهود الاحصان وله ان التزكية اعمال للشهادة اذ القاضى لا يعمل بها الا بالتزكية فصارت علة العلة بخلاف شهود الاحصان لانه شرط محض

ترجمہ اور اگر تزکیہ اور تعدیل کرنے والوں نے تزکیہ سے رجوع کیا تو وہ ضامن ہوں گے اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔ اس لئے کہ تعدیل کرنے والوں نے گواہوں کی اچھی تعریف کی ہے۔ پس ایسے ہو گئے جیسے احصان کے گواہ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ شہادت کو عمل دلانا ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی شہادت پر عمل نہیں کرے گا مگر تزکیہ ہے۔ پس تزکیہ علة العلة کے معنی میں ہو گیا بر خلاف احصان کے گواہوں کے کیونکہ یہ شرط محض ہے ۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر گواہوں نے کسی کے خلاف مال کی گواہی دی پھر تزکیہ کرنے والوں نے ان گواہوں کا تزکیہ اور قاضی کے مدعی علیہ کے خلاف مال کا فیصلہ کر دیا اور اس فیصلہ کی بنیاد پر مدعی نے مال مشہود بہ پر قبضہ کر لیا۔ اس کے بعد تزکیہ کرنے والوں نے اپنے تزکیہ اور تعدیل سے رجوع کر لیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تزکیہ کرنے والے مدعی علیہ کے لئے مال مشہور بہ کے ضامن ہوں گے۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک اور امام محمد ہیں۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ تزکیہ کرنے والے ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ کرنے والوں نے گواہوں کی تعریف کی ہے، کسی دعوی پر گواہی نہیں ہے۔ پس قاضی کا وہ فیصلہ جس کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ کا مال تلف ہوا ہے تزکیہ پر واقع نہیں ہوا ہے بلکہ گواہوں کی گواہی پر واقع ہوا ہے اور جب قاضی کا فیصلہ گواہی پر واقع ہوا اور تزکیہ پر واقع نہیں ہوا تو مدعی علیہ کے مال کا تلف ہونا تزکیہ کرنے والوں کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا اور جب اتلاف تزکیہ کرنے والوں کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے تو تزکیہ سے رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں تزکیہ کرنے والوں پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
He said: And if the witnesses who give testimony of character (muzakkiyun) retract from the tazkiyah, they become liable. According to Abu Hanifa, this is the case. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: They are not liable, because they praised the witnesses well, so they become like witnesses of chastity (shuhud al-ihsan). And his (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is that tazkiyah gives effect to the testimony, because the judge does not act upon testimony except through tazkiyah, so it becomes the cause of the cause (illat al-'illah), unlike witnesses of chastity, because that is a pure condition.

Translation: And if the character witnesses (those who attest to probity) retract from their testimony, they will be liable, and this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Sahibayn) said: They will not be liable, because they praised the witnesses well, so they become like witnesses of chastity. Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that tazkiyah gives effect to the testimony, because the judge does not act on testimony except through tazkiyah. So it becomes the cause of the cause, unlike witnesses of chastity, because that is a pure condition.

Commentary: The scenario: witnesses gave testimony about property against someone, then character witnesses testified to their probity, and the judge ruled against the defendant based on the original testimony, and the plaintiff took possession. Then the character witnesses retracted. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the character witnesses are liable to the defendant for the property. Imam Malik and Imam Muhammad also hold this view. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said the character witnesses are not liable. Their evidence is that the character witnesses merely praised the witnesses; they did not testify on the claim. So the judge's ruling was based on the original testimony, not on the tazkiyah. Therefore, the loss of the defendant's property is not attributed to the character witnesses, so they are not liable upon retraction.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage deals with the retraction of character witnesses (al-muzakkiyun) who testify to the probity of the main witnesses. The passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such witnesses are liable for compensation if they retract after the judge has ruled based on the main testimony, because tazkiyah (attestation of integrity) is necessary for the judge to accept the testimony; thus, it is the cause of the cause ('illat al-'illah) — the effective cause that enables the main testimony to be operative. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that character witnesses are not liable, comparing them to witnesses of chastity in hudud cases, which is a pure condition (shart mahd) and not a cause of the ruling. The commentary explains the scenario: original witnesses testify about property, character witnesses attest to their probity, the judge rules against the defendant, the plaintiff takes possession, then the character witnesses retract. Abu Hanifa (and also Imam Malik and Muhammad in one narration) finds them liable; the two companions do not. The reasoning of the two companions is that the ruling was based on the original testimony, not on the tazkiyah, so retraction of tazkiyah does not cause loss attributable to them.

Key Terms
تزكية (tazkiyah): Testimony of character witnesses attesting to the probity of the main witnesses.
مزكون (muzakkiyun): Witnesses who testify to the character/probity of other witnesses.
عله العله (illat al-'illah): Cause of the cause; a secondary cause that enables the primary cause to be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) regarding character witnesses who retract their tazkiyah?
A) They are liable for compensation
B) They are not liable because tazkiyah is a pure condition
C) They are liable only if the original witnesses also retract
D) They are liable only if the defendant suffers loss

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa holds retracting character witnesses liable because tazkiyah is the cause of the cause; the Sahibayn do not, seeing it as a mere condition.

Retraction of Tazkiyah: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn on Liability and the 'Illat al-'Illah
Ruling on retraction of tazkiyah with Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn's disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on liability for retraction of tazkiyah, explain Abu Hanifa's proof using the concept of 'illat al-'illah, and refute the Sahibayn's analogy with witnesses of ihsan.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah is the 'cause of the cause' of the judge's verdict; its retraction incurs liability, unlike mere conditions like ihsan.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute: when verifiers (muzakkun) retract their verification of witnesses after a judgment, does that make them liable for damages? Imam Abu Hanifa holds they are liable because tazkiyah is the 'illat al-'illah (cause of the cause) that enables the testimony. The Sahibayn disagree, comparing verifiers to witnesses of ihsan whose retraction does not incur liability. By understanding the causation chain, we see why Abu Hanifa's position prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
State the two positions clearly: Abu Hanifa says verifiers are liable (yadmanun) upon retraction; Sahibayn say they are not liable (la yadmanun).
The conflict is within the Hanafi school itself, so it is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize verifiers to witnesses of ihsan (who testify that an adulterer is married). Just as retraction of ihsan testimony does not make them liable for blood-money, retraction of tazkiyah should not make verifiers liable. Their reasoning: tazkiyah is mere praise, not testimony; the judge's verdict is based on testimony, not on tazkiyah.
The qiyas (analogy) is that both tazkiyah and ihsan are not the direct cause of the verdict or punishment.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that tazkiyah is the 'illat al-'illah (cause of the cause) of the judge's verdict. The judge only acts on testimony after verification, so tazkiyah makes the testimony operative. Retraction of the cause of the cause is like retraction of the cause itself, hence liability.
The chain: tazkiyah enables testimony -> testimony causes verdict -> verdict causes loss. Thus tazkiyah is linked to the loss.
4
Differentiate tazkiyah from ihsan
Ihsan (being married) is a mere condition (shart) for the penalty of stoning, not a cause. The cause of stoning is zina. Tazkiyah, in contrast, is what makes the testimony effective; it is not just a condition but a cause of the testimony's operation. Thus the analogy fails.
This distinction is crucial: a condition does not generate liability upon retraction; a cause does.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, the defendant can claim compensation from the verifiers; according to Sahibayn, he cannot. The text and the later Hanafi tradition give weight to Abu Hanifa's view, making it the mufta bihi (operative position).
Imam Malik and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) also side with Abu Hanifa, strengthening its adoption.

کو رجم کر دیا گیا۔ پھر احسان کے گواہوں نے احسان یعنی شادی شدہ ہونے کی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو یہ احسان کے گواہ عارف کے ورثاء کے لئے دیت کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے پس جس طرح احسان کے گواہ رجوع کرنے سے دیت کے ضامن نہیں ہوتے اسی طرح تزکیہ کرنے والے بھی تزکیہ سے رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں مال مشہود یہ کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔ حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ گواہی کو کارآمد بنانے کی علت ہے یعنی قاضی اس گواہی کے موافق عمل کرتا ہے جس گواہی کے گواہوں کی تعدیل کر دی گئی ہو۔ اور گواہی قاضی کے فیصلہ کی علت ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کی علت تو شہادت ہے اور شہادت کارآمد ہونے کی علت تعدیل ہے ۔ بس تعدیل کر نا علۃ العالیہ کے معنی میں ہو گیا اور حکم جس طرح علت کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح علتہ العلمیہ کی طرف بھی منسوب ہوتا ہے۔
خلاصہ یہ کہ قاضی کے حکم کے نتیجہ میں مدعی علیہ کے مال کا تلف ہونا جس طرح علت یونی گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہے۔ اسی طرح علیہ العلہ یعنی تزکیہ کرنے والوں کے تزکیہ اور تعدیل کی طرف بھی منسوب ہے اور جب مال کا اختلاف تزکیہ کرنے والوں کے تزکیہ کی طرف بھی منسوب ہے تو تزکیہ سے رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں تزکیہ کرنے والوں پر بھی ضمان واجب ہوگا۔
بخلاف شهود الاحصان .... الخ سے صاحبین کے قیاں کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ علی العلہ کے معنی میں ہے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے اور احسان یعنی زانی کا محصن ہونا رجم کے لئے شرط ہے اور عالیۃ العالیہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حد زنا کی علت زنا ہے اور احسان کے گواہ زنا کو ثابت نہیں کرتے ۔ اس لئے کہ زنا تو احسان سے پہلے ہی ثابت ہو چکا ہے۔ پس جب احسان کے گواہ زنا کو ثابت نہیں کرتے تو احسان ، حد زنا یعنی رجم کے لئے علیہ العلہ کے معنی میں بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب احسان علیہ العالیہ کے معنی میں نہیں ہے اور تزکیہ علتہ العلہ کے معنی میں ہے تو اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے تزکیہ کو احصان پر اور تزکیہ کرنے والوں کو شہود احصان پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے تزکیہ کوعیۃ العالیہ کے معنی میں کہا ہے اور علیہ العلہ نہیں کہا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت مالِ مشہور بہ کے اختلاف کی علت نہیں ہے بلکہ سبب ہے جس کی طرف قاضی کا حکم منسوب ہے۔ پس جب شہادت علت نہیں ہے تو تزکیۃ علیہ العلہ کیسے ہو جائے گا۔ اس وجہ سے تزکیہ کو علتہ العلہ کے معنی میں کہا گیا ہے۔
The answer to why the two groups are not made jointly liable is that the two proofs are completely distinct: the testimony of the original (asl) is on the underlying right, and the testimony of the subordinates (furu') is on the testimony of the original. There is no similarity between them. Since there is no similarity, they are not combined under a single testimony to be made liable together; rather, the defendant has the option to hold each party separately liable. The author of Hidayah said: If after the judge's verdict the subordinate witnesses say that the original witnesses gave false testimony against the defendant, or that the original witnesses made a mistake in that matter, then the subordinate witnesses' statement is not heeded, because the judge's verdict already passed is not invalidated by their statement. This is because their statement may be true or false, and mere probability does not invalidate the judge's ruling. Thus the judge's verdict does not become invalid, and liability is not imposed on the subordinates due to this statement, because the subordinates did not retract their own testimony; rather, they testified that the original witnesses retracted their testimony, which is of no benefit. Therefore, the subordinates are not liable, and since the original witnesses did not retract in the judge's court, they are also not liable. The verifiers (muzakkun) and those who declared the witnesses upright ('adl) retracted their tazkiyah: they will be liable. He said: 'And if the verifiers retract their verification, they are liable — this is according to Abu Hanifa. And they two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: they are not liable, because they praised the witnesses well, so they become like witnesses of ihsan. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that verification activates the testimony, because the judge only acts on testimony with verification. So it becomes the cause of the cause, unlike witnesses of ihsan, because it is a pure condition.' Explanation: And if the verifiers and modifiers retract their tazkiyah, they will be liable, and this is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said they will not be liable. This is because the modifiers praised the witnesses well. So they become like witnesses of ihsan. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that tazkiyah makes the testimony operative. This is because the judge will not act on testimony except with tazkiyah. So tazkiyah becomes in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, unlike witnesses of ihsan, because it is a pure condition. Elaboration of the case scenario: If witnesses gave testimony of property against someone, then the verifiers verified those witnesses, and the judge decided in favor of the plaintiff against the defendant, and based on that verdict the plaintiff took possession of the property in question. Thereafter, the verifiers retracted their tazkiyah and modification. According to Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifa, the verifiers will be liable to the defendant for the property in question. This is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Muhammad. The Sahibayn said the verifiers will not be liable. Sahibayn's proof is that the verifiers merely praised the witnesses; it is not testimony on a claim. Therefore, the judge's verdict by which the defendant's property was destroyed was based on the testimony, not on the tazkiyah. Since the judge's verdict was based on testimony and not on tazkiyah, the destruction of the defendant's property is not attributed to the verifiers. When the destruction is not attributed to them, then upon retraction of tazkiyah, liability is not obligatory on them. And these verifiers become like witnesses of ihsan: for example, if four witnesses testified to zina against 'Arif, then several witnesses testified to 'Arif being muhsan (married). Consequently, 'Arif was stoned. Then the witnesses of ihsan retracted their testimony of ihsan (being married). Those witnesses of ihsan are not liable for the blood-money (diya) to 'Arif's heirs. Just as witnesses of ihsan are not liable for blood-money upon retraction, similarly verifiers are not liable for the property in question upon retraction of tazkiyah. Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that tazkiyah is the cause that makes the testimony operative, i.e., the judge acts according to the testimony whose witnesses have been verified. And testimony is the cause of the judge's verdict. The conclusion is that the cause of the judge's verdict is the testimony, and the cause of the testimony being operative is the verification. Thus verification is 'illat al-'illah (the cause of the cause). Just as the ruling is attributed to the cause, it is also attributed to the cause of the cause. The summary is that the destruction of the defendant's property as a result of the judge's ruling is attributed to the cause, i.e., the witnesses, and also to the cause of the cause, i.e., the tazkiyah and modification of the verifiers. Since the destruction of property is also attributed to the tazkiyah of the verifiers, liability becomes obligatory upon them when they retract. 'Unlike witnesses of ihsan...' etc. is the answer to the qiyas of the Sahibayn. The gist of the answer is that tazkiyah is in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, as has passed before, whereas ihsan (being married) is a condition for stoning, not 'illat al-'illah. Because the cause of the hadd of zina is zina itself, and witnesses of ihsan do not prove zina; zina is already proven before ihsan. Since they do not prove zina, ihsan is not 'illat al-'illah for the hadd of zina (stoning). When ihsan is not 'illat al-'illah, and tazkiyah is 'illat al-'illah, then with this distinction it is incorrect to analogize tazkiyah to ihsan and verifiers to witnesses of ihsan. The author of Hidayah said tazkiyah is in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, not 'illat al-'illah. The reason is that testimony is not the cause of the destruction of the property in question; rather, it is a sabab (means) to which the judge's ruling is attributed. Since testimony is not a cause, how can tazkiyah be 'illat al-'illah? For this reason, tazkiyah is said to be in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on retraction of tazkiyah (verification of witnesses' credibility). The author presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the verifiers (muzakkun) retract their verification after the judge has acted on the testimony, they become liable (damir) to compensate the defendant for the property lost. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, comparing the verifiers to witnesses of ihsan (who testify that an adulterer is married), whose retraction does not incur liability. Abu Hanifa's proof is that tazkiyah is the 'illat al-'illah (the cause of the cause): the judge's verdict is based on testimony, but testimony only becomes operative through verification. Thus the verifiers are at the root of the causation chain, so their retraction triggers liability just like retraction of the testimony itself. The author refutes the Sahibayn's analogy by showing that witnesses of ihsan only prove a condition (shart) for punishment, not a cause. The section also clarifies a subtle point: the author of Hidayah calls tazkiyah 'in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah' rather than actual 'illat al-'illah, because testimony itself is a sabab (means), not a cause, so tazkiyah is the cause of that means. This lesson is crucial for understanding causation and liability in Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The act of verifying and commending witnesses as upright ('adl) before the judge accepts their testimony.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction of a previous statement or testimony. Here, retraction of tazkiyah by the verifiers.
علة العلة ('illat al-'illah): The cause of the cause. Tazkiyah is the cause that makes the testimony operative, and the testimony is the cause of the judge's verdict. Thus retraction of the 'illat al-'illah is like retraction of the cause itself.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage. Here, the verifiers become responsible for the property lost by the defendant due to the verdict based on retracted tazkiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why are verifiers (muzakkun) liable for damages if they retract their tazkiyah?
A) Because tazkiyah is itself a testimony (shahada).
B) Because tazkiyah is the 'illat al-'illah (cause of the cause) that makes the testimony operative.
C) Because they are considered original witnesses (shuhud asl).
D) Because the judge's verdict is directly based on tazkiyah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, retraction of tazkiyah after a judgment entails liability because tazkiyah is the cause of the cause of the verdict, unlike mere conditions like ihsan.

Shahadat — Testimony
advanced
8 min
Liability for Retracting Tazkiyah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for retracting tazkiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on liability for retracting tazkiyah and explain why tazkiyah is considered 'illat al-'illah rather than a mere condition.

Core Idea
Tazkiyah is the cause of the cause — retracting it triggers liability, unlike retracting a condition.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the legal consequences of retracting a declaration that witnesses are upright (tazkiyah). The disagreement hinges on classifying tazkiyah as either a condition (shart) or a cause of the cause ('illat al-'illah). Understanding this distinction is essential for mastering Hanafi causal reasoning in testimony law.

Guided Path
1
State the Positions
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa (liability upon retracting tazkiyah) and the Sahibayn (no liability). Notice the key difference in outcome.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; both sides are within the school.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's Analogy
Understand the analogy to witnesses of ihsan (marital status) in zina cases. The Sahibayn argue that just as witnesses of ihsan are not liable upon retraction because ihsan is a condition, tazkiyah is also a condition, so no liability.
They use qiyas (analogy) from the law of zina.
3
Follow Imam Abu Hanifa's Response
Grasp why Imam Abu Hanifa rejects the analogy. He classifies tazkiyah as 'illat al-'illah (cause of the cause) — it makes the testimony effective. Consequently, the loss is attributed to tazkiyah, and retraction creates liability.
The distinction between 'illat al-'illah and shart is the crux.
4
Understand the Terminology
Learn the Hanafi distinctions among illa (cause), sabab (means), shart (condition), and alamat (sign) as illustrated in the passage. This framework is crucial for proper legal reasoning.
This classification is not merely lexical; it determines rulings like liability.

تزکیہ کرنے والے ایسے ہو گئے جیسے احسان کے گواہ ، یعنی اگر چار گواہوں نے عارف کے زنا کی گواہی دی پھر چند گواہوں نے عارف کے محضن یعنی شادی شدہ ہونے کی گواہی دی۔ چنانچہ عارف کو رجم کر دیا گیا۔ پھر احسان کے گواہوں نے احسان یعنی شادی شدہ ہونے کی گواہی سے رجوع کیا تو یہ احسان کے گواہ عارف کے ورثاء کے لئے دیت کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے پس جس طرح احسان کے گواہ رجوع کرنے سے دیت کے ضامن نہیں ہوتے اسی طرح تزکیہ کرنے گواہوں کی تعدیل کر دی گئی ہو۔ اور گواہی قاضی کے فیصلہ کی علت ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ کی علت تو شہادت ہے اور شہادت کارآمد ہونے کی علت تعدیل ہے ۔ بس تعدیل کر نا علۃ العالیہ کے معنی میں ہو گیا اور حکم جس طرح علت کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح علتہ العلمیہ کی طرف بھی منسوب ہوتا ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ قاضی کے حکم کے نتیجہ میں مدعی علیہ کے مال کا تلف ہونا جس طرح علت یونی گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہے۔ اسی طرح
