ضمان واجب ہوگا۔ بخلاف شهود الاحصان .... الخ سے صاحبین کے قیاں کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تزکیہ علی العلہ کے معنی میں ہے جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے اور احسان یعنی زانی کا محصن ہونا رجم کے لئے شرط ہے اور عالیۃ العالیہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حد زنا کی علت زنا ہے اور احسان کے گواہ زنا کو ثابت نہیں کرتے ۔ اس لئے کہ زنا تو احسان سے پہلے ہی ثابت ہو چکا ہے۔ پس جب احسان کے گواہ زنا کو ثابت نہیں کرتے تو احسان ، حد زنا یعنی رجم کے لئے علیہ العلہ کے معنی میں بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب احسان علیہ العالیہ کے معنی میں نہیں ہے اور تزکیہ علتہ العلہ کے معنی میں ہے تو اس فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے تزکیہ کو احصان پر اور تزکیہ کرنے والوں کو شہود احصان پر قیاس کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے تزکیہ کوعیۃ العالیہ کے معنی میں کہا ہے اور علیہ العلہ نہیں کہا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شہادت مالِ مشہور بہ کے اختلاف کی علت نہیں ہے بلکہ سبب ہے جس کی طرف قاضی کا حکم منسوب ہے۔ پس جب شہادت علت نہیں ہے تو تزکیۃ علیہ العلہ کیسے ہو جائے گا۔ اس وجہ سے تزکیہ کو علتہ العلہ کے معنی میں کہا گیا ہے۔ فوائد. علت ، سبب ، شرط اور علامت کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ علت حکم کے اندر مؤثر ہوتی ہے، سبب بغیر تا ثیر کے حکم کی طرف مفضی ہوتا ہے اور شرط نہ حکم کے اندر مؤثر ہوتی ہے اور نہ حکم کی طرف مفضی ہوتی ہے بلکہ حکم کا وجود اس کے وجود پر موقوف ہوتا ہے اور علامت وہ ہے جس پر حکم دلالت کرے لیکن حکم کا وجود اس کے وجود پر موقوف نہ ہو۔ جیسے کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے انت طالق ان دخلت الدار کہا تو انت طالق ، وقوع طلاق کی علت اور دخول دار شرط ہے اور شہادت حکم قاضی کے لئے سبب ہے اور ٹرین آنے سے پہلے گھنٹی بجنا ٹرین کی آمد کی علامت ہے۔
Those who perform tazkiyah become like the witnesses of ihsan (marital status). That is, if four witnesses testified to Zayd's zina, then some witnesses testified that Zayd is muhsan (married). Consequently, Zayd was stoned. Then the witnesses of ihsan retracted their testimony about ihsan (being married), so these witnesses of ihsan will not be liable for diyah to Zayd's heirs. So just as the witnesses of ihsan are not liable for diyah upon retraction, likewise those who perform tazkiyah upon retracting tazkiyah will not be liable for the property that was the subject of the testimony. The argument of Imam Abu Hanifa is that tazkiyah is the cause (illa) that makes the testimony effective – that is, the judge acts in accordance with the testimony whose witnesses have been declared upright (ta'dil). And the testimony is the cause of the judge's decision. The conclusion is that the cause of the judge's decision is the testimony, and the cause of the testimony being effective is ta'dil (tazkiyah). So ta'dil becomes in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah (the cause of the cause). And just as the ruling is attributed to the cause, it is also attributed to the 'illat al-'illah. In summary, the loss of the defendant's property as a result of the judge's ruling is attributed to the cause, i.e., the witnesses, and also attributed to the 'illat al-'illah, i.e., the tazkiyah and ta'dil of those who performed tazkiyah. And when the property loss is attributed to the tazkiyah of those who performed tazkiyah, then upon retraction of tazkiyah, liability is also obligatory on those who performed tazkiyah. Contrary to the witnesses of ihsan... from this the answer to the qiyas of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is given. The essence of the answer is that tazkiyah is in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, as has passed, and ihsan (being married) for the adulterer is a condition (shart) for rajm, not 'illat al-'illah. Because the cause of the hadd of zina is zina itself, and the witnesses of ihsan do not establish zina, since zina had already been established before the ihsan testimony. So when the witnesses of ihsan do not establish zina, then ihsan is not in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah for the hadd of zina (rajm). And when ihsan is not in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, and tazkiyah is in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah, then with this difference, it is not correct to apply qiyas (analogy) of tazkiyah to ihsan nor those who perform tazkiyah to witnesses of ihsan. The author of Hidayah said that tazkiyah is in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah and not 'illat al-'illah? That is because testimony is not the cause of the loss of the property in question, but rather a sabab (means) to which the judge's ruling is attributed. So when testimony is not a cause, how can tazkiyah be 'illat al-'illah? For this reason, tazkiyah is said to be in the meaning of 'illat al-'illah. Benefits: The difference between cause (illa), means (sabab), condition (shart), and sign (alamat) is that cause is effective in the ruling, means leads to the ruling without being effective, condition neither is effective nor leads, but the existence of the ruling depends on its existence, and sign is that which indicates the ruling but the existence of the ruling does not depend on its existence. For example, if someone said to his wife 'you are divorced if you enter the house', then 'you are divorced' is the cause of divorce occurring, and entering the house is the condition, and testimony is the means for the judge's ruling, and the bell ringing before the train arrives is a sign of the train's arrival.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of those who perform tazkiyah (declaring witnesses upright) when they retract their tazkiyah. The text first presents the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) who analogize tazkiyah to the testimony of ihsan (marital status), arguing that just as witnesses of ihsan are not liable upon retraction because their testimony is merely a condition, likewise those who perform tazkiyah should not be liable. Imam Abu Hanifa opposes this, arguing that tazkiyah is not a condition but rather the cause of the cause ('illat al-'illah) – it makes the testimony effective. Since the judge's ruling and consequent property loss are attributed to both the testimony (the immediate cause) and the tazkiyah (the cause of the cause), retracting tazkiyah entails liability. The text then explains the distinction: ihsan is a pure condition (shart) for rajm, not a cause, while tazkiyah directly causes the testimony to be acted upon. The author of al-Hidayah refines this by noting that testimony is a sabab (means) rather than a 'illa (cause), so tazkiyah is 'illat al-'illah (cause of the cause) rather than 'illat al-illah? Actually, the text clarifies that testimony is a sabab, and tazkiyah is what makes the sabab effective, so it is 'illat al-'illah. Finally, the passage provides a useful distinction between cause (illa), means (sabab), condition (shart), and sign (alamat) with examples from Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تزکیہ (tazkiyah): The act of declaring witnesses upright and trustworthy (ta'dil) so that their testimony is accepted.
علت (illa): The cause that directly affects the ruling; an effective cause.
سبب (sabab): A means or occasion that leads to a ruling but is not directly effective.
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the existence of the ruling depends, but it does not cause the ruling.
علت العلہ ('illat al-'illah): The cause of the cause; an indirect cause that enables the immediate cause to be effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why are those who retract tazkiyah liable for damages?
A) Because tazkiyah is a condition (shart) for accepting testimony
B) Because tazkiyah is 'illat al-'illah (the cause of the cause) and the loss is attributed to it
C) Because they directly caused the loss by lying
D) Because they are considered co-witnesses

Key Takeaway
Retracting tazkiyah imposes liability because tazkiyah is the cause of the testimony being effective ('illat al-'illah), not merely a condition.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Liability When Witnesses to Oath and Condition Retract
Determining liability when witnesses to oath and condition both retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that liability is attributed to the cause (sabab) rather than the condition (shart) in witness retraction cases, and distinguish the majority position from Imam Zufar's view.

Core Idea
Liability follows the cause (sabab), not the condition (shart).

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute concerning liability when witnesses to both the cause and condition of an oath retract. The case involves an oath of emancipation or divorce conditioned on entering a house. Two witnesses testify to the oath itself, two to the occurrence of the condition. After the judge rules on these testimonies, all four retract. The Hanafi school's majority holds that only the oath witnesses are liable, while Imam Zufar argues for equal liability. This lesson explains the reasoning and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the components
Recognize that there are two sets of witnesses: one testifies to the oath (cause), the other to the condition. The judge's ruling is based on the oath testimony.
2
State the majority Hanafi position
Only the witnesses to the oath are liable for the value of the slave or half mahr because the oath is the direct cause.
This is the mufta bihi view from Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
3
Present Imam Zufar's counter-position
Imam Zufar holds all four witnesses equally liable because the loss resulted from the combined testimonies.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The cause (sabab) is what the judge relies on; the condition is merely a precondition. As long as attribution to the cause is possible, it is not shifted to the condition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, only the oath witnesses pay compensation. According to Imam Zufar, all four pay equally.

تلف کرنا سبب کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے نہ کہ شرط کی طرف۔ کیونکہ جب تک سب کی طرف حکم کو منسوب کرنا ممکن ہوتا ہے اس وقت تک شرط کی طرف رجوع نہیں کیا جاتا۔ پس جب تلف کرنا سبب کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے تو یہاں غلام یا نصف مہر کو تلف کرنا ان گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہو
Two witnesses testified to the oath and two witnesses testified to the existence of the condition, then all four witnesses retracted. So the liability is upon the witnesses of the oath in particular. He said: 'And if two witnesses testify to the oath and two witnesses testify to the existence of the condition, then they retract, the liability is especially upon the witnesses of the oath because they are the cause (sabab), and the loss is attributed to those who establish the cause, not to the pure condition. Do you not see that the judge gives judgment based on the testimony of the oath, not on the testimony of the condition? And if only the witnesses of the condition retract, the later scholars (mashayikh) differed on it. And the meaning of the issue is the oath of emancipation and oath of divorce before consummation.' Translation: And if two witnesses testified to the oath and two witnesses testified to the existence of the condition, then all four retracted, then the liability is specifically on the witnesses of the oath because they are the cause, and loss is attributed to those who establish the cause, not to those who establish the pure condition. Do you not see that the judge gives judgment based on the testimony of the oath, not on the witnesses of the condition? And if only the witnesses of the condition retracted, the later scholars differed on it. And the meaning of the issue is the oath of emancipation and oath of divorce before consummation. Explanation of the case: Two persons testified to the oath of emancipation – for example, they testified that Khalid said to his slave: 'If you enter this house, you are free' – or testified to the oath of divorce before consummation – for example, they said that Khalid said to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter this house, you are divorced'. Then the other witnesses testified to the existence of the condition, i.e., they testified that the slave or the woman entered the house. Then the judge gave judgment that the slave is free or the wife is divorced. Then all four witnesses retracted their testimony. Then the liability for the price of the slave or half the mahr is specifically upon the witnesses of the oath. That is, Khalid is entitled to compensation from those witnesses who testified that Khalid said to his slave 'if you enter this house, you are free' or to his non-consummated wife 'if you enter this house, you are divorced'. And those witnesses who testified that the condition of entering the house occurred – they are not liable. Imam Zufar said that the liability is equally upon all four witnesses. Imam Zufar's argument is that the slave or half the mahr was lost due to the testimony of both parties, i.e., all four witnesses, so when the loss is attributed to all four, upon retraction the liability is equally upon all four. Our argument is that the cause of the slave's freedom and the woman's divorce is this very oath – 'you are free' and 'you are divorced' which are conditional on entering the house – this is the cause of the slave's freedom and the wife's divorce. This is why the judge gives judgment of freedom based on the testimony establishing the master's statement 'you are free', and gives judgment of divorce based on the husband's statement 'you are divorced'. In any case, the cause of freedom and divorce is the oath of emancipation and the oath of divorce. And entering the house is merely a condition for their occurrence. And loss is attributed to the cause, not to the condition, because as long as it is possible to attribute the ruling to the cause, one does not refer to the condition. So when loss is attributed to the cause, here the loss of the slave or half the mahr is attributed to those witnesses (who testified to the oath).
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding liability when witnesses to both the cause (sabab) and the condition (shart) retract their testimonies. The specific case involves an oath of emancipation or oath of divorce before consummation, conditioned upon entering a house. Two witnesses testify to the oath itself (the cause), and two witnesses testify that the condition (entering the house) occurred. After the judge rules based on these testimonies (slave freed or wife divorced), all four witnesses retract. The relied-upon Hanafi position (from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) is that only the witnesses who testified to the oath are liable for the value of the slave or half the mahr (if the wife was not consummated). This is because the oath is the direct cause (sabab) of the freedom or divorce – the judge's ruling is directly based on the existence of the oath. The condition (entering the house) is merely a precondition, not the cause. The text then presents the view of Imam Zufar, who argues that all four witnesses are equally liable because the loss resulted from the combined testimony of both sets of witnesses. The Hanafi response (the 'our argument' section) reaffirms that only the cause is attributed, not the condition. The text also notes that if only the witnesses of the condition retract, later scholars (mashayikh) differed – some would hold them liable, others not. This case illustrates the Hanafi principle that in matters of liability (daman), the causal connection (isnad) is assigned to the direct cause (sabab) rather than the condition (shart).

Key Terms
یمین (yameen): An oath, specifically an oath of emancipation or divorce conditional on a future event.
شرط (shart): A condition, such as entering a house, upon which the effect of the oath depends.
سبب (sabab): A cause or means that directly leads to a legal outcome, such as the oath leading to freedom or divorce.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation for loss caused by one's action.
عتاق (itiq): Emancipation of a slave; specifically, an oath of emancipation (yameen al-itiq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where two witnesses testify to the oath and two to the condition, and all four retract, who is liable according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) All four witnesses are equally liable
B) Only the witnesses to the condition are liable
C) Only the witnesses to the oath are liable
D) No one is liable

Key Takeaway
Liability for loss caused by witness retraction is attributed to the direct cause (sabab), not the condition (shart), so only witnesses to the cause are liable.

Liability When Witnesses of Oath and Condition Retract
Explaining daman allocation when all four witnesses retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for daman when witnesses retract and explain why only witnesses of the cause (oath) bear liability.

Core Idea
Loss is attributed to the cause (sabab), not the condition (shart).

When witnesses retract after a judgment based on their testimony, liability for the loss must be assigned. This lesson examines a scenario where two sets of witnesses testify—one to a conditional oath (cause) and another to the condition's occurrence. The Hanafi school's ruling hinges on causation: the cause, not the condition, triggers the loss. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly allocating daman among witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the retraction of witnesses after a judgment. The ruling is that daman (guarantee) is wajib. Determine on whom it falls according to the Hanafi majority.
The passage explicitly states 'الضمان على شهود اليمين خاصة'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas based on a general principle: loss is attributed to those who establish the cause, not the mere condition. The text says 'لانه السبب والتلف يُضاف الى مثبتى السبب دون الشرط المحض'.
This is a talil (reasoning) argument.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase shows that the cause (oath) is the effective factor for the loss. The judge rules only on the oath testimony, indicating that the condition testimony is not independently causative.
The author reinforces with 'الا ترى ان القاضى يقضى بشهادة اليمين دون شهود الشرط'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Imam Zufar holds that all four witnesses share liability equally because they all contributed. The Hanafi response distinguishes cause from condition. The tarjih (preferred view) is that only oath witnesses are liable, even if only condition witnesses retract.
Al-Marghinani endorses the majority view as the correct one.

صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مسئلہ کی مراد یمین طلاق قبل الدخول ہے۔ خادم نے صورت مسئلہ میں دونوں کا لحاظ رکھا ہے ۔ یمین طلاق میں قبل الدخول کی قید اس لئے مذکور ہے کہ اگر بعد الدخول یمین طلاق کی گواہی دی گئی تو رجوع کرنیکی صورت میں گواہ مہر کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ دخول کی وجہ سے شوہر پر مہر واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ خواہ وہ طلاق دے یا نہ دے۔ اور جب مہر شوہر پر دخول کی وجہ سے واجب ہے تو گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی کے ذریعہ کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی ہے اور جب گواہوں نے کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی تو ان پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہو
He said: And if two witnesses testify to the oath and two witnesses to the existence of the condition, then they all retract, then the guarantee is upon the witnesses of the oath specifically, because the oath is the cause, and the loss is attributed to those who establish the cause, not to the mere condition. Do you not see that the judge gives judgment based on the testimony of the oath, not on the witnesses of the condition? And if only the witnesses of the condition retract, the scholars differed concerning it. The meaning of the case is the oath of emancipation and divorce before consummation. Translation: And if two groups give testimony of the oath and two groups give testimony of the existence of the condition, then all four retract, then the guarantee is specifically obligatory upon the witnesses of the oath, because they are the cause, and the loss will be attributed to those who establish the cause, not to those who establish mere condition. Do you not see that the judge gives judgment based on the testimony of the oath, not on the witnesses of the condition. And if only the witnesses of the condition retract, the scholars differed in it. And the meaning of the case is the oath of emancipation and the oath of divorce before consummation. Explanation: The scenario is that two persons testified to the oath of emancipation, e.g., they testified that Khalid said to his slave: 'If you enter this house, you are free,' or they testified to the oath of divorce before consummation, e.g., that Khalid said to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter this house, you are divorced.' Then the other witnesses testified to the existence of the condition, i.e., they testified that the slave or the woman entered the house. Then the judge gave judgment that the slave is free or the wife is divorced. Then all four witnesses retracted their testimony. So the guarantee of the value of the slave or half the mahr is specifically obligatory upon the witnesses of the oath. That is, the guarantee for Khalid is obligatory upon those witnesses who testified that Khalid said to his slave: 'If you enter this house, you are free,' or to his wife before consummation: 'If you enter this house, you are divorced.' And upon those witnesses who testified that the condition of entering the house occurred, no guarantee is obligatory. Imam Zufar said: The guarantee is equally obligatory upon all four witnesses. Imam Zufar's proof is that the slave or half the mahr was lost due to the testimony of both parties, i.e., all four witnesses. So when the loss is attributed to all four, then upon retraction, the guarantee is also equally obligatory upon all four. Our proof is that the cause of the slave's freedom and the woman's divorce is the oath itself, i.e., 'you are free' and 'you are divorced' which are suspended on entering the house. This is the cause of the slave's freedom and the wife's divorce. This is why the judge gives judgment of freedom based on the master's statement 'you are free' being established by testimony, and gives judgment of divorce based on the husband's statement 'you are divorced' being established. In any case, the cause of freedom and divorce is the oath of emancipation and the oath of divorce. And the occurrence of entering the house is merely a condition. And loss is attributed to the cause, not to the condition. Because as long as the ruling can be attributed to the cause, it is not referred to the condition. So when loss is attributed to the cause, here the loss of the slave or half the mahr is attributed to those witnesses who established the cause through their testimony, and not attributed to those who established mere condition. And when loss is attributed to the witnesses who established the cause (the oath), then upon retraction, the guarantee is obligatory upon them, not upon those who testified to the existence of the condition (entering the house). The author of Hidayah said: If only the witnesses of the condition retract, then there is difference among the scholars. Some scholars hold that in this case the witnesses who testified to the existence of the condition are liable, but the correct opinion is that even in this case they are not liable. The author of Hidayah says: The intended meaning of the case is the oath of divorce before consummation. The servant has considered both in the scenario. The restriction of 'before consummation' in the oath of divorce is mentioned because if testimony is given regarding an oath of divorce after consummation, then upon retraction the witnesses would not be liable for the mahr, because due to consummation, the mahr becomes obligatory upon the husband, whether he divorces or not. And when the mahr is obligatory upon the husband due to consummation, then the witnesses have not caused any loss through their testimony, and when they have not caused any loss, then no guarantee is obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning retraction of witnesses in a conditional oath case. The author (Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) states the ruling: When two witnesses testify to the oath (e.g., a conditional emancipation or divorce statement) and two other witnesses testify that the condition occurred, and then all four retract, the guarantee (daman) is only on the witnesses of the oath. The reason is that the oath is the cause (sabab) of the loss (the value of the slave or half the mahr), while the condition is merely a prerequisite. The judge's verdict is based on the oath testimony, not the condition testimony. This is illustrated: the oath of emancipation (e.g., 'If you enter this house, you are free') is what triggers freedom; the actual entry is just the condition. Therefore, loss is attributed to those who established the cause. The author notes a difference of opinion: If only the condition witnesses retract, some scholars hold them liable, but the correct view (mufta bihi) is that they are not liable. Imam Zufar (al-Zafar) disagreed, arguing that both sets of witnesses contributed equally to the loss, so all four should share liability. The author refutes this by emphasizing that the cause alone is the basis for judgment. Finally, the scope is clarified: The case applies to oaths of emancipation and oaths of divorce before consummation. After consummation, the mahr is already due, so divorce does not cause a new loss, hence no daman on retraction.

Key Terms
يمين (yameen): An oath, here specifically a conditional oath of emancipation (yameen 'itaq) or divorce (yameen talaq) suspended on an event.
شرط (shart): A condition, here the occurrence of entering the house, upon which the oath depends.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee/liability to pay compensation for loss caused by testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All four witnesses equally
B) Only the witnesses of the oath
C) Only the witnesses of the condition
D) None of them

Key Takeaway
The cause of the loss, not the condition, determines who is liable when witnesses retract.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Liability of Witnesses Who Retract: Cause vs Condition
Distinguishes liability of witnesses who established cause vs condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between witnesses who establish a cause versus a condition, and apply the Hanafi rule that only cause witnesses are liable upon retraction.

Core Idea
Liability follows direct causation: condition witnesses are never liable, even if they retract alone.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a critical distinction in the law of witness retraction (rujūʿ ʿan al-shahādah): not all witnesses who retract are liable for damages. The key is whether their testimony established a cause (sabab) that directly led to a legal consequence, or merely a condition (sharṭ). Understanding this principle is essential for correctly assigning liability in cases where testimony is withdrawn after a judgment has been executed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of witnesses
The passage distinguishes between witnesses who establish the cause (sabab) and those who establish a condition (shart). Note that the cause directly produces the legal effect (e.g., divorce), while the condition is a prerequisite.
Example: In a yamīn ṭalāq, the oath itself is the cause; entering the house is the condition.
2
Understand the attribution of loss (talf)
The loss is attributed only to witnesses who established the cause. Therefore, upon retraction, they are liable (ḍāmin). Condition witnesses do not cause the loss directly.
The Hanafi principle: 'al-talf yudāfu ilā man asbaba lā man sharraṭa' (loss is attributed to the causer, not the condition-setter).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars held that if only condition witnesses retract, they become liable. The correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) in al-Hidayah is that they are still not liable, because their testimony did not cause the loss.
The dispute is only about the scenario where condition witnesses alone retract. The ruling for cause witnesses is unanimous.
4
Apply the ruling to the special case of post-consummation
If testimony concerned an oath of divorce after consummation, witnesses are not liable even if they retract, because the mahr becomes obligatory due to consummation itself, not due to the testimony.
This shows that liability only arises when the testimony directly caused a loss that would not have occurred otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گا جنھوں نے اپنی گواہی سے سبب ثابت کیا ہے اور ان گواہوں کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو گا جنھوں نے محض شرط ثابت کی ہے۔ اور جب تلف کرنا یمین (سبب) ثابت کرنے والے گواہوں کی طرف منسوب ہے تو رجوع کرنے کی صورت میں ضمان بھی انھیں پر واجب ہوگا، وجود شرط یعنی دخول دار کی گواہی دینے والوں پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اگر فقط شہود شرط نے رجوع کیا تو علماء کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض علماء کا خیال ہے کہ اس صورت میں وجود شرط کی گواہی دینے والے گواہ ضامن ہوں گے لیکن صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی ضامن نہ ہوں گے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ مسئلہ کی مراد یمین طلاق قبل الدخول ہے۔ خادم نے صورت مسئلہ میں دونوں کا لحاظ رکھا ہے۔ یمین طلاق میں قبل الدخول کی قید اس لئے مذکور ہے کہ اگر بعد الدخول یمین طلاق کی گواہی دی گئی تو رجوع کرنیکی صورت میں گواہ مہر کے ضامن نہ ہوں گے کیونکہ دخول کی وجہ سے شوہر پر مہر واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ خواہ وہ طلاق دے یا نہ دے۔ اور جب مہر شوہر پر دخول کی وجہ سے واجب ہے تو گواہوں نے اپنی گواہی کے ذریعہ کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی ہے اور جب گواہوں نے کوئی چیز تلف نہیں کی تو ان پر ضمان بھی واجب نہ ہو
That [liability] is attributed to those who established the cause (sabab) with their testimony, and it is not attributed to those who merely established a condition (shart). And when the destruction (talf) is attributed to the witnesses who established the cause (sabab), then upon retraction, liability (daman) is obligatory upon them. There is no liability upon those who testified to the existence of the condition, i.e., entering the house.
The author of al-Hidayah said: If only the witnesses of the condition retract, there is a difference of opinion among scholars. Some scholars think that in this case the witnesses who testified to the existence of the condition are liable, but the correct view is that even in this case they are not liable.
The author of al-Hidayah says that the intended case is an oath of divorce before consummation. The servant (khādim) has considered both aspects in the scenario. The condition of 'before consummation' is mentioned in the oath of divorce because if testimony was given for an oath of divorce after consummation, then upon retraction the witnesses would not be liable for the mahr, because due to consummation, the mahr becomes obligatory upon the husband, whether he divorces or not. And when the mahr is obligatory upon the husband due to consummation, the witnesses have not caused any destruction by their testimony, and since the witnesses have not caused any destruction, liability is not obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses a key rule in the chapter of retraction of testimony (Kitab al-Ruju' 'an al-Shahadat). It distinguishes between two types of witnesses: those whose testimony establishes a cause (sabab) that directly leads to a legal consequence, and those whose testimony merely establishes a condition (shart) that is a prerequisite for the cause. The ruling: upon retraction, only the witnesses who established the cause are liable to compensate for the loss (damān), because their testimony is directly attributed to the destruction of the right (e.g., payment of mahr or restitution). The witnesses of the condition are not liable, because their testimony did not directly cause the loss; the cause itself was the operative factor.

The author then addresses a disagreement: if only the condition witnesses retract, some scholars hold them liable, but the correct view (al-ṣaḥīḥ) is that they are still not liable. The rationale is that the condition alone does not produce the legal effect without the cause.

Finally, the author clarifies that the typical example is an oath of divorce before consummation (qabl al-dukhul). If the oath was after consummation, the witnesses would not be liable even if they retract, because the mahr becomes obligatory upon the husband due to consummation itself, not due to the testimony. Hence, the witnesses caused no 'talf' (destruction) of the right, and no damān is due. This is a fine point of Hanafi legal reasoning, emphasizing direct causation (isnād al-talf) for liability.

Key Terms
شہادت (shahādat): Testimony given in court; evidence presented by witnesses.
رجوع (rujūʿ): Retraction or withdrawal of testimony after the judgment was based upon it.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for a loss caused by one's action.
سبب (sabab): The direct cause that legally produces an effect (e.g., divorce, payment).
شرط (sharṭ): A condition that must exist for the cause to operate, but does not itself produce the ruling.
یمین طلاق (yamīn ṭalāq): An oath of divorce; a conditional divorce where the husband swears to divorce if a certain event occurs.
قبل الدخول (qabl al-dukhūl): Before consummation of marriage; a key factor in determining mahr obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi view in al-Hidayah, when only condition witnesses retract, are they liable?
A) Yes, because their testimony was necessary for the judgment
B) No, because they did not directly cause the loss
C) Yes, but only if the cause witnesses did not retract
D) No, because they were not the only witnesses

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, liability for retracted testimony only attaches to witnesses who established the direct cause of the loss, not those who established a mere condition.

Dispute Between Principal and Agent Over Purchased Slave
Ruling on whose word is accepted in agency purchase disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rules for whose word is accepted in disputes between principal and agent over a purchased slave, and identify the reasoning of Abu Hanifa versus the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Whose word is accepted depends on whether the agent can still perform and whether he is accused of self-dealing.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a detailed dispute between a principal and an agent over the purchase of a slave that died or is alive. The ruling hinges on two key Hanafi principles: the word is for the denier (al-qawl li al-munkir) and the agent as a trustee (amin). Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) when the slave is alive and the price has not been paid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
The passage distinguishes two main situations: the slave died before the dispute, or the slave is still alive. Each situation further depends on whether the price was paid to the agent.
Four sub-cases emerge: dead+paid, dead+unpaid, alive+paid, alive+unpaid.
2
Apply the maxim 'al-qawl li al-munkir'
When the slave died and the price was not paid, the agent claims reimbursement from the principal. The principal denies. Since the denier's word is accepted, the principal prevails.
The agent is claiming a right; the principal is the munkir.
3
Analyze the trustee (amin) concept
When the price was paid, the agent holds the principal's money as a trustee. His claim to have bought the slave is accepted because he is clearing his trust responsibility.
This applies whether the slave died or is alive.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For the case where the slave is alive and the price was not paid, the Sahibayn accept the agent's word because he can still buy the slave anew, so he has no motive to lie. Abu Hanifa accepts the principal's word because the agent may have bought for himself and now tries to pass a bad deal to the principal.
Abu Hanifa sees the agent as being in a position of accusation (mawdi' tuhmah).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as they are the majority and the text presents their view first.
The tarjih is based on the principle that the agent's ability to repurchase removes the accusation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موکل نے وکیل کو ایک غلام ہزار روپے کے عوض خریدنے کا حکم دیا وکیل نے کہا میں نے خریدا اور وہ میرے پاس فوت ہو گیا اور موکل نے کہا تو نے اسے اپنے لئے خریدا تھا تو موکل کا قول قابل قبول ہوگا
قال ومن امر رجلا بشراء عبد بالف فقال قد فعلت ومات عندى وقال الآمر اشتريته لنفسك فالقول قول الآمر فان كان دفع اليه الالف فالقول قول المأمور لان فى الوجه الاول اخبر عما لا يملك استينافه وهو الرجوع بالثمن على الأمر وهو ينكر والقول للمنكر وفى الوجه الثانى هو امين يريد الخروج عن عهدة الامانة فيقبل قوله ولو كان العبد حيا حين اختلفا ان كان الثمن منقودا فالقول للمامور لانه امين وان لم يكر منقودا فکذالک عند ابی یوسف و محمد لانه يملك استيناف الشراء فلا يتهم في الاخبار عنه وعند ابي حنيفة القول للآمر لانه موضع تهمة بان اشتراه لنفسه فاذا رأى الصفقة خاسرة الزمها الأمر بخلاف ما اذ كان الثمن منقودا لانه امين فيه فيقبل قوله تبعا لذالك ولا ثمن في يده ههن ترجمہ. ایک شخص نے ایک شخص کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض ایک غلام خریدنے کا حکم دیا۔ پس وکیل نے کہا کہ میں نے کیا ہے لیکن غلام میرے پاس مر گیا ہے اور مؤکل نے کہا کہ تو نے اس غلام کو اپنے واسطے خریدا تھا تو موکل کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ پس اگر مؤکل نے وکیل ایک ہزار رو پیدے دیے ہوں تو وکیل کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ پہلی صورت میں وکیل نے ایسی چیز کی خبر دی ہے جس کو ایجاد کرنے کا مالک نہیں ہے اور وہ مؤکل سے ثمن واپس لینا ہے حالانکہ موکل اس کا منکر ہے اور قول منکر ہی کا معتبر ہوتا ہے اور دوسری صورت میں وکیلا امین ہے وہ امانت کی ذمہ داری سے نکلنا چاہتا ہے۔ لہذا اسی کا قول قبول ہوگا اور اگر جس وقت ان دونوں نے اختلاف کیا ہے اس وقت غلام زندہ ہو ( پس ) اگر شمن (وکیل کو ) دے دیا گیا ہوتو وکیل کا قول قبول ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ وہ امین ہے اور اگر شمن نہیں دیا گیا تو بھی صاحبیر کے نزدیک ایسا ہی ہے کیونکہ وہ از سر نو خریدنے کا مالک ہے تو وہ خرید کرنے کی خبر دینے میں متہم نہ ہوگا۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک موکل
A person ordered a man to buy a slave for one thousand rupees. The agent said, 'I bought it, and it died with me.' The principal said, 'You bought it for yourself.' So the claim of the principal is accepted. A narration: 'And whoever orders a man to buy a slave for a thousand, and he says I have done it and it died with me, and the orderer says you bought it for yourself, then the word is the word of the orderer. If he had given him the thousand, then the word is the word of the commanded (agent), because in the first case he reports something he cannot initiate anew, which is claiming reimbursement of the price from the orderer while he denies it, and the word is for the denier. In the second case, he is a trustee wanting to exit from the trust obligation, so his word is accepted. If the slave was alive when they disagreed, if the price was paid, the word is for the commanded (agent) because he is a trustee. If the price was not paid, it is likewise according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad because he can initiate the purchase anew, so he is not accused in reporting about it. According to Abu Hanifa, the word is for the orderer because he is in a position of accusation that he bought it for himself, so when he sees the bargain is a loss, he attributes it to the orderer. Contrary to when the price was paid, because he is a trustee in it, so his word is accepted by following that, and there is no price in his hand.' Translation: A person ordered a person to buy a slave for one thousand rupees. The agent said, 'I bought it, but the slave died with me,' and the principal said, 'You bought this slave for yourself,' so the principal's word is accepted. If the principal had given the agent one thousand rupees, then the agent's word is accepted. Because in the first case, the agent reported something he cannot initiate anew, which is claiming the price back from the principal while the latter denies it, and the word is for the denier. In the second case, the agent is a trustee wanting to exit from the trust obligation, so his word is accepted. If at the time of their dispute the slave is alive, then if the price was given to the agent, the agent's word is accepted because he is a trustee. If the price was not given, it is likewise according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because he can buy anew, so he is not accused. According to Abu Hanifa, the principal's word is accepted.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage covers the dispute between an agent and principal regarding a purchase. The ruling distinguishes two main cases. First case: the agent says he bought a slave and it died with him, but the principal says he bought it for himself. If the principal had not paid the price to the agent, the principal's word is accepted because the agent is claiming reimbursement which the principal denies. The principle is 'the word is for the denier' (al-qawl li al-munkir). If the principal had paid the price, the agent's word is accepted because he is a trustee (amin) and wants to clear his trust. Second case: if the slave is still alive at the time of dispute, the same rule applies if the price was paid: agent's word. If the price was not paid, there is a disagreement between the sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Abu Hanifa. The sahibayn say the agent's word is accepted because he can still buy the slave again, so he is not accused of lying. Abu Hanifa says the principal's word is accepted because the agent might have bought it for himself and, seeing a bad deal, attributes it to the principal. The text presents the sahibayn's view as the relied-upone position.

Key Terms
آمر (aamir): The person who orders the purchase; the principal.
مأمور (ma'moor): The person ordered to perform the purchase; the agent.
امین (ameen): A trustee; the agent is considered an amin in handling the principal's money.
منکر (munkir): The one who denies the claim; in disputes, the denier's word is preferred.
موقع تہمہ (mawdi' tuhmah): A position of accusation; a situation where the person is suspected of acting in self-interest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where the principal ordered the agent to buy a slave for 1000 and the slave is still alive, and the price has not been paid, what is the ruling according to the majority of the Hanafi school (Sahibayn)?
A) The principal's word is accepted.
B) The agent's word is accepted.
C) The slave is divided equally.
D) The dispute is solved by the judge arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
In agency purchase disputes, whose word is accepted depends on whether the agent is a claimant or a trustee, and on the agent's ability to perform the task anew.

Excluding Confession in Agency for Litigation: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Ruling on excluding confession in agency for litigation with views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on excluding confession in agency for litigation and distinguish between the views of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, including the plaintiff-defendant distinction.

Core Idea
In absolute agency for litigation, the agent may confess or deny; excluding confession is valid only when the principal is certain of the opponent's falsehood, and only for a plaintiff.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding agency for litigation (wakalah bil khusumat). The central question is whether a principal can validly exclude the agent's authority to confess on his behalf. The views of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad are presented, with the author al-Marghinani reconciling them by highlighting the principal's certainty and the distinction between plaintiff and defendant. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct fatwa on agency limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal issue
The dispute is whether a principal can validly exclude the agent's authority to confess in a litigation agency. Without such exclusion (absolute agency), the agent has jawab mutlaq – authority to both confess and deny.
2
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's position
He holds that excluding confession is invalid because it would authorize only denial, which may be false, and agency for falsehood is prohibited.
Abu Yusuf focuses on the potential for falsehood regardless of the principal's intention.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's position and distinction
Imam Muhammad holds that exclusion is valid if the principal explicitly states it, indicating certainty of the opponent's falsehood. He further distinguishes: for the plaintiff, exclusion is valid; for the defendant, it is not due to the possibility of a compulsory oath (yamin) that cannot be delegated.
Muhammad's view is more nuanced and is adopted as mufta bihi.
4
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is that in absolute agency, the agent has both confession and denial. For the plaintiff, excluding confession is valid; for the defendant, it is not. This balances the principal's certainty with procedural constraints.
The author of al-Hidayah reconciles the views by adopting Muhammad's distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
اشرفی البدایه بعد امد
اقرار کے استثناء کا مالک اس وجہ سے نہیں ہے کہ اگر اس کو اقرار کے استثنی کا مالک بنا دیا گیا تو اس سے یہ لازم آئے گا کہ موکل صرف انکار کا مالک ہو یعنی مؤکل انکار کرتا رہے خواہ وہ حق پر ہو یا باطل پر ہو حالانکہ یہ بات شرعاً جائز نہیں ہے۔ بحر حال جب بقول امام ابویوسف توکیل بالخصومت سے اقرار کا استثناء کرنا درست نہیں ہے تو اس سے اتناء کرنا بھی درست نہ ہوگا اور اگر یہ بات تسلیم کر لیں کہ نہ اقرار کا استثنا درست ہے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے روایت ہے تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہرگز نہیں ہے کہ اقرار حقوق تو کیل میں سے نہیں ہے بلکہ مؤکل کا اقرار کے استثناء کی صراحت کرنا اس بات کی واضح دلیل ہے کہ موکل انکار کا مالک ہے اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ موکل کا انکار کرج اس لئے جائز ہے کہ بہت ممکن ہے کہ موکل کا خصم حق پر ہو لیکن جب مؤکل نے اقرار کے استثناء کی صراحت فرمادی تو اس سے یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ موکل کو پورا پورا یقین ہے کہ اس کا خصم باطل پر ہے پس جب خصم کے باطل پر ہونے کا یقین ہے تو مؤکل کے لئے انکار متعین ہو گیا ہے۔ اور جب مؤکل کے لئے خصم کی بات کا انکار متعین ہو گیا تو اس کے لئے اقرار کا استثناء کر کے صرف انکار کا وکیل کرنا درست اور جائز ہو گیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ اگر تو کیل با خصومت مطلق ہو یعنی اقرار کا استثناء نہ کیا گیا ہو تو اس تو کیل کو اس پر محمول کیا جائے گا جو مسلمان کے حال کے مناسب ہو اور مسلمان کے حال کے مناسب مطلق جواب ہے یعنی وکیل کو اس بات کا اختیار ہے کہ وہ اقرار کرے یا انکار کرے اور جھگڑا اور صرف انکار کرتے رہنا مسلمان کے حال کے مناسب نہیں ہے وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ مطلق جواب تمام احوال میں جائز ہے اور جھگڑا اور صرف انکار کرتے رہنا حرام ہے اور تو کیل بالحرام بھی حرام ۔ لہذا مسلمان ظاہر حال کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اس تو کیل کو مجاز یعنی جواب پر محمول کریں گے۔ بہر حال یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ توکیل بالخصومت کے مطلق ہونے کی صورت میں وکیل مطابقاً جواب کا مالک ہوگا ، اقرار اور ا نکار دونوں کا اختیار ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ انھوں نے مدعی اور مدنی علیہ کے درمیان فرق کیا ہے یعنی اگر تو کیل بالخصومت مدگی کی جانب سے ہو تو مدعی کے لئے انکار کا استثناء کرنا درست ہے کیونکہ مدعی کو اصل خصومت میں اختیار ہے وہ مدعی عالیہ کی بات کا اقرار بھی کر سکتا ہے اور اس کا انکار بھی کر سکتا ہے پس جب مدعی کو دونوں باتوں کا اختیار ہے تو اس کے حق میں اقرار کا استثناء کرنا مفید ہو گا یعنی وہ اپنے وکیل کو کہہ سکتا ہے کہ تجھ کو اقرار کا اختیار نہیں ہے ۔ اور اگر مدعلی علیہ کی جانب سے توکیل بالخصومت ہو تو مدعی عالیہ کے لئے اقرار کا استثناء کرنا درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اقرار کا استثناء مدعلی علیہ کے حق میں مفید نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ مدعی نے جو دعویٰ کیا ہے وہ اس کو بینہ کے ذریعہ ثابت کرنے کا یا مدنی منیہ سے یمین کا مطالبہ کر کے مدعی علیہ کو اقرار کرنے پر مجبور کرے گا مگر چونکہ ایمان اور قسموں میں نیابت جاری نہیں تی سے اس لئے وکیل یمین کو اپنے موکل پر محول کرے گا۔ اور جب یمین موکل پر محول ہوگئی تو موکل اقرار پر مجبور ہو سکتا ہے اور جب موکل اقرا جمہور: لیا تو اس کے حق میں اقرار کا استثناء درست نہ ہو گا۔
Book of Agency. [Commentary heading]. He is not the owner of the exclusion of confession because if he is made the owner of the exclusion of confession, then it would necessitate that the principal is only the owner of denial, meaning the principal continues to deny whether he is upon truth or falsehood, while this is not permissible in Sharia. In any case, when according to the statement of Imam Abu Yusuf, excluding confession from agency for litigation is not valid, then including it [in the agency] is also not valid. And if we accept that excluding confession is valid, as narrated from Imam Muhammad, then its meaning is not that confession is not from the rights of agency, but rather the principal's explicit statement of excluding confession is clear evidence that the principal is the owner of denial. Its detail is that the principal's denial is permissible because it is very possible that the principal's opponent is upon the truth, but when the principal explicitly excludes confession, then it is established that the principal has full certainty that his opponent is upon falsehood. So when there is certainty that the opponent is upon falsehood, then denial becomes determined for the principal. And when denial of the opponent's statement is determined for the principal, then for him, excluding confession and appointing an agent only for denial is correct and permissible. The author of Hidayah said: If the agency for litigation is absolute, i.e., confession was not excluded, then that agent will be interpreted according to what is suitable for the state of a Muslim, and what is suitable for the state of a Muslim is the absolute answer, i.e., the agent has the authority to either confess or deny. And mere denial continuously is not suitable for the state of a Muslim. The reason is that the absolute answer is permissible in all circumstances, while falsehood and continuous denial are prohibited, and agency for what is prohibited is also prohibited. Therefore, considering the apparent state of a Muslim, they will interpret that agent as having authority [metaphorically] for the answer. In any case, it is established that in the case of absolute agency for litigation, the agent is the owner of the answer accordingly, and has authority over both confession and denial. The author of Hidayah said: It is narrated from Imam Muhammad that he made a distinction between the plaintiff and the defendant. That is, if the agency for litigation is on behalf of the plaintiff, then it is valid for the plaintiff to exclude denial [i.e., only authorize confession? Actually the text says 'inkar ka istithna' which is exclusion of denial? But context is about confession. There may be confusion; the text likely means exclusion of confession is valid for plaintiff? Actually the passage says: 'if agency is on behalf of the plaintiff, then for the plaintiff, excluding denial is valid' - but earlier discussion is about excluding confession. This might be a typo in the OCR. We will follow the text as is. The intended meaning: For the plaintiff, excluding confession (i.e., only authorizing denial) is valid because the plaintiff has choice. For the defendant, excluding confession is not valid because the defendant may be compelled to confess via oath.]
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on excluding confession in an agency for litigation (wakalah bil khusumat). The author begins by stating the problem: if a principal excludes confession from the agent's authority, he would only be authorizing denial, even if the principal is in the wrong, which is impermissible. However, if the principal explicitly states the exclusion, it indicates that he is certain of the opponent's falsehood, so it becomes permissible. The author then presents the intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Yusuf holds that excluding confession is not valid because it leads to the principal authorizing only denial, which is not permissible. Imam Muhammad holds that if the principal explicitly excludes confession, it is valid because it shows certainty. The author of Hidayah reconciles by stating that if the agency is absolute (no exclusion), the agent is considered authorized for both confession and denial (jawab mutlaq), as this is appropriate for a Muslim. Then Imam Muhammad's distinction: for the plaintiff, excluding confession is valid because he has full discretion; for the defendant, it is not valid because the defendant may be forced to confess through an oath that cannot be delegated.

Key Terms
استثناء الاقرار (istithna al-iqrar): Excluding the authority of confession from the agent in a litigation agency.
توکیل بالخصومت (tawkil bil khusumat): Agency for litigation, where the agent is appointed to represent the principal in a legal dispute.
جواب مطلق (jawab mutlaq): The absolute answer in litigation, which includes both confession (iqrar) and denial (inkar).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, why is it not valid for a defendant to exclude confession from his agent in litigation?
A) Because the defendant has no choice in the matter and may be forced to confess through an oath that cannot be delegated.
B) Because the defendant is always truthful and confession is mandatory.
C) Because the plaintiff can force the defendant to confess directly.
D) Because the agent is not allowed to confess at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits excluding confession in litigation agency only when the principal has certainty of the opponent's falsehood, and further restricts this to the plaintiff due to the defendant's potential oath.

Validity of Agent's Confession Inside and Outside Court
Dispute on whether the agent's confession is valid only in court or everywhere

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intra-Hanafi positions on the validity of an agent's confession outside the court and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) used by each side.

Core Idea
An agent's confession in litigation is only valid in the court because it is metaphorically part of litigation, which requires the court setting.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a crucial intra-Hanafi disagreement: can an agent appointed for litigation (wakalah bil khusumat) confess on behalf of the principal outside the presence of the judge? Imam Abu Yusuf argues yes, because the agent stands in place of the principal. The majority (Sahibayn) argues no, because confession is only considered 'litigation' (khusumat) metaphorically, and that metaphor applies only when the statement is made as an answer in court. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists use linguistic concepts like haqiqah and majaz in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
Read the beginning of the passage to locate Imam Abu Yusuf's view (confession valid both in and out of court) and the opposing view of 'the two parties' (al-tarafayn, i.e., the Sahibayn) who restrict validity to the court.
The source uses 'the two parties' to refer to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, or alternatively both Sahibayn.
2
Analyze Abu Yusuf's Analogy
Abu Yusuf argues that the agent stands in the place of the principal. Since the principal's own confession is not restricted to court, the agent's confession should also be valid everywhere. Identify this qiyas (analogy) and its basis.
This is a form of tamthil (likening) based on the representative relationship.
3
Deconstruct the Sahibayn's Distinction
The Sahibayn distinguish between haqiqah (real) and majaz (metaphorical). Confession is 'khusumat' only metaphorically, and this metaphor works only when the statement is a 'jawab' (answer) in a court proceeding. Outside court, there is no 'jawab' and thus no metaphor. Trace this reasoning step by step.
They cite Quranic verses where recompense is called by the name of the original act to justify using 'khusumat' for 'iqrar'.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Its Consequence
The text indicates that the preferred view (mufta bihi) is the restriction to court. The consequence: if an agent confesses outside court, he is no longer an agent for absolute answer but only for the restricted answer (confession), which contradicts his mandate.
This shows how the ruling affects the outcome in practice.

(خصومت ) کے نام کے ساتھ موسوم کر دیا گیا ہے بہر حال اقرار مجاز خصومت ہے البتہ اقرار مجلس قاضی کے ساتھ مختص ہے یعنی اگر قاضی کی مجلس میں وکیل نے اپنے مؤکل پر اقرار کیا تو یہ اقرار معتبر ہو گا اور اگر غیر مجلس قاضی میں اقرار کیا تو معتبر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ جب مستحق نے مطالبہ کیا تو ایسا ہی جواب دیا جائیگا جس کا وہ مستحق ہے اور یہ وہی جواب ہے جو قاضی کی مجلس میں ہے۔ پس یہ جواب یعنی اقرار قاضی کی مجلس کے ساتھ مختص ہو گیا۔ لیکن اگر اس بات پر بینہ قائم کر دیا گیا کہ وکیل نے غیر مجلس قاضی میں اقرار کیا ہے تو وکیل وکالت سے خارج ہو جائے گا اور اس کو مال دینے کا حکم نہ کیا جائیگا کیونکہ مطلق جواب کا وکیل رہنا ممکن نہ رہا اس طور پر کہ وکیل انکار کا مالک تو ہو نہیں سکے گا کیونکہ انکار کرنے کی صورت میں وکیل کے کلام میں تناقص ہو جائیگا کہ پہلے اقرار کیا تھا اور اب انکار کرتا ہے پس غیر مجلس قاضی میں اقرار کے بعد اگر اس کو وکیل باقی رکھا گیا تو وہ جواب مقید یعنی صرف اقرار کا وکیل ہوگا حالانکہ موکل نے اس کو جواب مقید (اقرار) کا
Returning to the difference, the author of Hidayah said: When it is established that agency for litigation includes confession on behalf of the principal, then Hadrat Imam Abu Yusuf said that the effect regarding the judge and something else [?] both are equal. [Then the text continues] He confesses in the court; both cases are permissible because the agent is the representative of the principal. Therefore, what the principal owns, the agent also owns. And the principal's confession is not restricted to the court, but is valid both in and out of court. So his agent's confession is also not restricted to the court, but is valid in both places. As for why the principal's confession is not restricted to the court, the answer is that the principal's confession is effective by itself, whereas only that thing is restricted to the court which is not effective by itself but becomes effective together with something else like the denial of the oath. And the two parties [or the two sides] say that there is a difference between the court and outside the court, i.e., in the court the agent's confession on behalf of his principal is valid, and outside it is not valid. The proof of this difference is that it has already passed that agency for litigation refers to the absolute answer, and the absolute answer, by its generality, includes the reality (i.e., litigation/denial) as well as the metaphorical (i.e., confession). In summary, the agent can deny and can confess, but denial is the reality of litigation, and confession is metaphorical litigation. But confession is metaphorical litigation only in the court; outside the court it is not litigation, neither real nor metaphorical. That it is not real litigation is obvious, and it is not metaphorical litigation because confession is considered litigation only because it is an answer, while outside the court, an answer is not valid. So when outside the court an answer is not valid, confession outside the court is also not metaphorical litigation. And when confession outside the court is not metaphorical litigation, then that confession is not valid, because only that confession is valid which is metaphorical litigation. In any case, it is established that the agent's confession outside the court is not valid and permissible. As for how confession in the court is metaphorical litigation, the answer is that either because confession occurs as a counterpart to litigation, i.e., there is a correspondence between litigation and confession. So here, one of the two counterparts, i.e., litigation, is used to mean the other, i.e., confession. And using one counterpart for the other is permissible metaphorically, as in Allah's statement "So whoever has assaulted you, assault him in the like manner" where the recompense for assault is metaphorically called assault, and "The recompense for an evil is an evil like it" where the recompense for evil is metaphorically called evil. Or confession is metaphorical litigation because litigation is the cause of confession, so the cause (confession) is named with the name of the effect (litigation). In any case, confession is metaphorical litigation, but confession is restricted to the court, meaning if the agent confesses on behalf of his principal in the court, this confession is valid, and if he confesses outside the court, it is not valid, because the apparent is that when the claimant makes a demand, only the answer that he deserves will be given, and that is the answer that is in the court. So this answer, i.e., confession, became restricted to the court. But if evidence is established that the agent confessed outside the court, then the agent will be removed from the agency and will not be ordered to give money, because it is no longer possible for him to remain an agent for the absolute answer in such a way that he could be the owner of denial, because in the case of denial there would be contradiction in the agent's statement, as he first confessed and now denies. So after confessing outside the court, if he is kept as an agent, he will be an agent for a restricted answer, i.e., only confession, even though the principal appointed him for the restricted answer (confession). [The text ends abruptly.]
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether an agent's confession (iqrar) on behalf of his principal in a litigation agency is valid only inside the court (majlis al-qadi) or also outside. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it is valid in both places because the agent stands in the place of the principal, and the principal's own confession is not limited to the court; hence the agent's is not either. The opposing view (attributed to 'the two parties' or the Sahibayn) holds that it is only valid in court. Their reasoning is that the agent's authority in litigation is ultimately about 'jawab' (answer) in the court; outside the court, there is no litigation, so confession cannot be considered part of the litigation. The passage then provides a sophisticated analysis using the concepts of haqiqah (real) and majaz (metaphorical) to show that confession is considered 'khusumat' (litigation) only metaphorically, and only when it occurs in the court. It cites Quranic verses as examples of metaphorical usage. Finally, it states that if an agent confesses outside the court, he is effectively removed from the agency for absolute answer and becomes only an agent for confession (restricted answer), which contradicts the original mandate.

Key Terms
مجلس قاضی (majlis al-qadi): The court session or the presence of the judge, where legal proceedings are conducted.
اقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of a claim. In litigation, it is considered a form of answer (jawab).
حقیقت و مجاز (haqiqah wa majaz): Literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meaning. The text uses this distinction to classify confession as a metaphorical form of litigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the 'two parties' (Sahibayn) in the text, why is the agent's confession outside the court not valid?
A) Because the agent is not a representative outside court.
B) Because confession is only considered litigation metaphorically when it occurs as an answer in court.
C) Because the principal must be present.
D) Because outside court, only denial is allowed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preferred view (mufta bihi) is that an agent's confession in a litigation agency is valid only inside the court, not outside, based on the linguistic principle that confession is metaphorical litigation.

The Hanafi Definition of Plaintiff and Defendant in Da'wa
Defining the key terms plaintiff and defendant in litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of plaintiff and defendant and apply it to distinguish the parties in a legal claim using the principle that consideration is given to meanings, not forms.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the plaintiff is not compelled to litigate if he abandons the claim; the defendant is compelled – and he is the denier.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, we examine the foundational definitions that shape the entire law of claims (da'wa). Knowing who is plaintiff and who is defendant determines the burden of proof and the right to take an oath. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the designation depends on legal compulsion and meaning, not merely on who initiates the claim. This lesson unpacks the core definition, alternative views, and the crucial principle that meanings override forms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition from al-Quduri
The matn states: 'The plaintiff is one who is not compelled to continue litigation if he abandons it; the defendant is one who is compelled to litigation.' This is the general correct definition.
This definition focuses on compulsion.
2
Recognize the alternative definitions from the mashayikh
Other scholars defined the plaintiff as one who does not deserve without proof (like an outsider claiming property from a possessor), or one who argues against the apparent. These are subsumed under the general definition.
They highlight different aspects of the same reality.
3
Understand the hadith evidence linking defendant and denier
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Proof is upon the plaintiff, and the oath is upon the denier.' Another hadith says: 'The oath is upon the defendant.' Combining both shows that the defendant is the denier.
This is why Imam Muhammad's definition (defendant = denier) is considered correct.
4
Apply the principle that consideration is given to meanings, not forms
In the example of the depositor (mudi') who claims he returned the deposit, in form he is a plaintiff (claiming return), but in meaning he is a defendant (denying liability for loss). Therefore, his statement is accepted with his oath.
This illustrates how to identify the true plaintiff and defendant in ambiguous cases.

Source Text

تشریح وکالت کے ابواب میں سب سے زیادہ مشہور وکالت بالخصومت ہے اور وکالت بالخصومت دعوی کا سبب داعی ہے اور دعوی اس کا مسبب ہے اور مسبب چونکہ سبب کے بعد ہوتا ہے اس لئے مصنف ہدایہ نے کتاب الدعومی کو وکالت کے بعد ذکر فرمایا ہے دعوی لغت میں اس قول کا نام ہے جس سے انسان دوسرے آدمی پر حق واجب کرنے کا ارادہ کرے اور فقہاء کی اصلاح میں دعوی اس شخص ( قاضی ) کی مجلس میں حق کے مطالبہ کا نام ہے جو شخص ثبوت حق کی صورت میں چھٹکارا دلانے پر قادر ہو۔ دعوی کا سبب وہی ہے جو بیع کا سبب ہے یعنی تعلق البقاء المقدور بتعاطى المعاملات، کیونکہ مدعی کا دعوی یا بقاء نسل کی طرف راجع ہوگا یا بقاء نفس کی طرف یا ان دونوں کے توابع کی طرف اور تینوں صورتوں میں زندگی کو باقی رکھنا مقصود ہوتا ہے۔
