۳۔ مدعی برشی معلوم ہو۔
اس دعوی کے ساتھ مدعی علیہ پر حکم متعلق ہوتا ہو۔
کیونکہ مجلس غیر قاضی میں دعوی صیح نہیں ہوتا اور خصم اگر حاضر نہ ہو یہی یہ مجہول ہو یا دعوئی سے مدعی علیہ پر کچھ لازم نہ ہوتا ہوتو ان صورتوں میں دعوئی فاسد ہوگا۔ دعویٰ کا حکم یہ ہے کہ خصم پر نعم بالا کے ساتھ جواب واجب ہو۔
مدعی پر ترک دعوی سے خصومت پر جبر نہیں اور مدعی علیہ پر جبر ہے
قال المدعى من لا يجبر على الخصومة اذا تركها والمدعى عليه من يجبر على الخصومة ومعرفة الفرق بينهما من اهم ما يبتنى عليه مسائل الدعوى وقد اختلف عبارات المشائخ فيه فمنها ما قال في الكتاب وهو حد عام صحيح وقيل المدعى من لا يستحق الابحجة كالخارج والمدعى عليه من يكون مستحقا بقوله من غیر حجة كذى اليد وقيل المدعى من يتمسك بغير الظاهر والمدعى عليه من يتمسك بالظاهر وقال محمد في الاصل المدعى عليه هو المنكر وهذا صحيح لكن الشان فى معرفته والترجيح بالفقة عند الحذاق من اصحابنا لان الاعتبار للمعاني دون الصور فان المودع اذا قال رددت الوديعة فالقول قوله مع اليمين وان كان مدعيا للرد صورة لانه ينكر الضمان معنى
ترجمہ مدعی وہ شخص ہے کہ اگر وہ دعوی ترک کرے تو اس کو خصومت پر مجبور نہ کیا جائے اور مدعی علیہ وہ ہے جس کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا
جائے جن امور پر مسائل دعوئی بنی ہیں ان میں سب سے زیادہ اہم ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق کو بچانا ہے اس بارے میں مشائخ کی عبارتیں مختلف ہیں ۔ منجملہ ان میں سے ایک وہ ہے جس کو قدوری میں بیان کیا ہے یہ تعریف عام ہے صحیح ہے اور کہا گیا کہ مدعی وہ شخص ہے جو بغیر حجت کے مستحق نہ ہو جیسے وہ شخص جو دوسرے کے قبضہ میں کسی عین کا دعوی کرتا ہو اور مدلی علیہ وہ شخص ہے جو صرف اپنے قول سے بغیر صحت کے مستحق ہو جیسے قابض اور کہا گیا کہ مدعی وہ ہے جو خلاف ظاہر سے استدلال کرے اور مدعی علیہ وہ ہے جو ظاہر سے استدلال کرے اور امام محمد نے مبسوط میں کہا کہ مدعی علیہ وہ شخص ہے جو منکر ہو یہ قول اگر چہ صحیح ہے لیکن گفتگو اسی کی شناخت میں ہے اور فقہ کے ذریعہ ترجیح دینے کا حق ہمارے علماء میں ماہرین کو حاصل ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اعتبار معانی کا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ صورتوں کا چنا نچہ اگر مودع (بفتح الدال ) نے کہا کہ میں ودیعت واپس کر چکا تو مع الیمین اس کا قول معتبر ہو گا اگر چہ وہ صورۃ واپس کرنے کا مدعی ہے کیونکہ وہ معنی منمان کا منکر ہے۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ جن امور پر مسائل دعوی معنی ہیں ان میں سب سے زیادہ اہم بات مدعی اور مدعلی علیہ کے درمیان فرق کی شناخت ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے البينة على المدعى واليمين علی من انکر ۔ یعنی مدعی پر بینہ ہے اور مدعی علیہ پر یمین ہے لہذا ان دونوں کی معرفت ضروری ہوئی یہی وجہ ہے کہ مدعی اور مدعی علیہ کی تعریف میں مشائخ کا زبر دست اختلاف ہے چنانچہ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ مدعی وہ شخص ہے جس کو خصومت پر مجبور نہ کیا جائے یعنی دعوی کرنے کے بعد اگر وہ دعوی کو ترک کرنا چاہے تو اس کو ترک کر دے اس پر کسی طرح کا جبر نہیں ہے اور موٹی عالیہ وہ شخص ہے جس کو خصومت پر مجبور کیا جائے یعنی مدعی کے
دعوی کرنے کے بعد اس پر جواب دینا لازم ہے خصومت سے پہلو تہی کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ یہ تعریف عام بھی ہے اور مسیح بھی ہے عام تو اس لئے ہے کہ مدعی مدعی علیہ کے سلسلہ میں جس قدر تعریفیں کی گئیں ہیں یہ تعریف ان سب کو شامل ہے اور صحیح اس لئے ہے کہ یہ تعریف اپنے تمام افراد کو جامع اور دخول غیر سے مانع ہے بعض حضرات مشائخ نے کہا کہ مدعی وہ شخص ہے جو صرف حجت سے مستحق ہو سکتا ہو یعنی یا تو وہ خود بینہ پیش کرے یا مدعی علیہ اقرار کرے اور یا مدنی علیہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کرے۔ جیسے وہ شخص جو ایسے عین کا دعوی کرتا ہے جو دوسرے آدمی کے قبضہ میں ہو اس صورت میں مدعی اس مین فی کا مستحق اسی وقت ہو گا جبکہ حجت شرعیہ موجود ہو یعنی مدعی علیہ ( قابض ) اس دعوی کا اقرار کرے یا مدعی جینہ پیش کر دے یا بینہ ہونے کی صورت میں مطالبہ یمین پر مدعی علیہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دے اور مدعلی علیہ وہ شخص ہے جو صرف اپنے قول سے بغیر حجت کے مستحق ہو جائے جیسے وہ شخص فی الحال عین شی پر قابض ہے چنانچہ اگر قا بض نے یہ کہا کہ یہ شی میری ملک ہے تو صرف اتنا کہنے سے اس کا حق ثابت ہو جائے گا جب تک کہ مدعی اپنا استحقاق ثابت نہ کر دے بعض حضرات علماء نے کہا کہ مدعی وہ شخص ہے جو خلاف ظاہر سے استدلال کرے یعنی اس کا قول ظاہر کے خلاف ہو اور مدعی علیہ وہ شخص ہے جس کا قول ظاہر حال
کے موافق ہو۔ حضرت امام محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ منکر کو کہتے ہیں صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اما محمدکا یہ قول صیح ہے کیونکہ ایک حدیث میں فرمایا گیا ہے الیمین علی من انکر اور ایک حدیث میں ہے الیمین علی المدعیٰ علیہ دونوں حدیثوں کو جمع کرنے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مدعی علیہ اور منکر دونوں ایک ہیں یعنی مدعی علیہ ہی منکر ہوتا ہے۔
Book of Lawsuit (Da'wa). Translation: This book is about the statement of claims. Book of Da'wa. Explanation: Among the chapters of agency, the most famous is agency in litigation, and agency in litigation is the cause (sabab) of the claim, and the claim is its effect (musabbab). Since the effect comes after the cause, the author of al-Hidayah mentioned the Book of Da'wa after agency. Linguistically, 'da'wa' is the name for a statement by which a person intends to make a right obligatory upon another person. In the terminology of jurists, 'da'wa' is the name for demanding a right in the court of a person (the judge) who has the power to deliver relief upon proof of the right. The cause of da'wa is the same as the cause of sale: the connection of possible continuation through transactions, because the plaintiff's claim either relates to the continuation of lineage, or the continuation of life, or the subsidiaries of both, and in all three cases, the aim is to preserve life.
Conditions for a valid da'wa: (1) The court of a judge. (2) The plaintiff's claim is against a present opponent. (3) The plaintiff is known (defined). (4) A ruling relates to the defendant through this claim. Because a claim in a non-judge court is not valid, and if the opponent is not present, or is unknown, or nothing is obligatory upon the defendant through the claim, then in these cases the claim is invalid. The ruling of da'wa is that the opponent is obligated to respond with consent or compulsion. The plaintiff is not compelled to continue the litigation if he abandons it, but the defendant is compelled.
He said: The plaintiff is one who is not compelled to continue litigation if he leaves it, and the defendant is one who is compelled to litigation. Knowing the difference between them is among the most important matters upon which issues of da'wa are based. The expressions of the mashayikh have differed concerning it. Among them is what is said in al-Kitab (al-Quduri): it is a general, correct definition. It is also said: The plaintiff is one who does not deserve (the right) except with proof, like the outsider; and the defendant is one who deserves by his statement without proof, like the possessor. It is also said: The plaintiff is one who adheres to what is contrary to the apparent, and the defendant is one who adheres to the apparent. Muhammad said in al-Asl: The defendant is the denier (munkir), and this is correct, but the difficulty is in knowing him (identifying him). The preference (tarjih) through fiqh belongs to the experts among our companions, because consideration is given to meanings (ma'ani), not forms (suwar). For example, if the depositor (mudi') says, 'I returned the deposit,' his statement is accepted with his oath, even though in form he is a claimant of return, because in meaning he is denying liability.
Translation: The plaintiff is the one who, if he abandons the claim, he is not compelled to litigation; and the defendant is the one who is compelled to litigation. Among the matters on which issues of da'wa are based, the most important is understanding the difference between these two. The expressions of the mashayikh regarding this differ. Among them is that which is mentioned in al-Quduri; this definition is general and correct. And it is said: The plaintiff is the one who does not deserve without proof, like one who claims a specific property in another's possession; and the defendant is the one who deserves by his own statement without proof, like the possessor. And it is said: The plaintiff is the one who argues against the apparent, and the defendant is the one who argues with the apparent. Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut: The defendant is the one who is the denier. This statement, although correct, the discussion is about its identification. The right of tarjih through fiqh belongs to the experts among our scholars. Because consideration is given to meanings, not forms. So if the depositor (with fatha on dal) said, 'I have returned the deposit,' his statement is accepted with his oath, even though in form he is a claimant of return, because in meaning he is the denier of liability. Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah says that among the matters on which issues of da'wa are based, the most important is the knowledge of the difference between the plaintiff and the defendant, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Proof is upon the plaintiff, and the oath is upon the one who denies.' So knowledge of both is necessary. This is why there is strong disagreement among the mashayikh in the definition of plaintiff and defendant. Thus, the author of al-Quduri said: The plaintiff is the one who is not compelled to litigation, i.e., if after filing the claim he wishes to abandon it, he may abandon it without any compulsion; and the defendant is the one who is compelled to litigation, i.e., after the plaintiff's claim, it is obligatory upon him to respond, and he is not allowed to evade litigation. The author of al-Hidayah said that this definition is general and correct. General because it encompasses all definitions given in the context of plaintiff and defendant; correct because it includes all its instances and prevents the entry of others. Some mashayikh said: The plaintiff is the one who can only become entitled through proof, i.e., either he himself presents evidence, or the defendant confesses, or the defendant refuses to take an oath. For example, the one who claims a specific property in another's possession; in this case, the plaintiff becomes entitled to that property only when a legal proof exists: either the defendant (possessor) confesses to the claim, or the plaintiff presents evidence, or the defendant refuses to take an oath when the oath is demanded from him. And the defendant is the one who becomes entitled by his own statement without proof, like the one who is currently in possession of the specific property. So if the possessor says, 'This property is mine,' merely stating it establishes his right until the plaintiff proves his entitlement. Some scholars said: The plaintiff is the one who argues against the apparent, i.e., his statement is contrary to the apparent; and the defendant is the one whose statement is in accordance with the apparent situation. Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut: The defendant is called the denier. The author of al-Hidayah said that Imam Muhammad's statement is correct because in one hadith it is said: 'The oath is upon the one who denies,' and in another hadith: 'The oath is upon the defendant.' Combining the two hadiths shows that the defendant and the denier are the same, i.e., the defendant is the denier.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the definitions of 'plaintiff' (mudda'i) and 'defendant' (mudda'a alayhi) as foundational terms in the Hanafi law of claims (da'wa). The author begins by explaining the placement of the Book of Da'wa after Agency: agency in litigation (wakala bil khusuma) is the cause, and da'wa is the effect. Then, the linguistic and technical definitions of da'wa are given. The core of the passage is the statement: 'The plaintiff is not compelled to litigation if he abandons it; the defendant is compelled.' This definition from al-Quduri (the matn of al-Hidayah) is said to be general (shamil) and correct (sahih). The passage then presents three alternative definitions from the mashayikh: (1) plaintiff is one who does not deserve without proof vs. defendant who deserves by his own statement (like the possessor); (2) plaintiff is one who argues against the apparent vs. defendant who argues with the apparent; (3) Imam Muhammad's definition: the defendant is the denier (munkir). The author prefers Imam Muhammad's definition because it aligns with the hadith 'al-yamin 'ala man ankara' (the oath is upon the denier) and another hadith 'al-yamin 'ala al-mudda'a alayhi' (the oath is upon the defendant), showing they are identical. However, the passage notes that the identification of who is the denier in practice may require expert judgment. The key principle is that consideration is given to meanings (ma'ani) not forms (suwar). The example of the depositor (mudi') illustrates: if he claims he returned the deposit, in form he is a plaintiff (claiming return), but in meaning he is a defendant (denying liability for loss), so his statement is accepted with an oath. This passage helps students understand that the categorization of parties in a lawsuit is not always obvious from who initiates the claim, but depends on who bears the burden of proof and who is legally compelled to respond.

Key Terms
مدعی (mudda'i): The plaintiff: the one who is not compelled to continue litigation if he abandons it; he must bring proof (bayyina) to establish his right.
مدعى عليه (mudda'a alayhi): The defendant: the one who is compelled to respond to the claim; he is the denier (munkir) and may take an oath to deny the claim.
منكر (munkir): The denier: one who denies the claim; in the context of da'wa, the defendant is the denier.
بينة (bayyina): Proof/evidence; the burden of proof is on the plaintiff (al-bayyina 'ala al-mudda'i).
يمين (yamin): Oath; the defendant may be required to swear an oath to deny the claim if the plaintiff has no proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is the correct definition of the defendant (mudda'a alayhi) as stated by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut?
A) The one who is not compelled to litigation if he abandons the claim.
B) The one who is the denier (munkir).
C) The one who argues with the apparent.
D) The one who does not deserve without proof.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the plaintiff bears the burden of proof and is not compelled to litigate; the defendant is compelled and is the denier, with his statement accepted under oath.

Swearing by Revealed Scriptures for Ahl al-Kitab
Ruling on swearing by attributes besides Allah for Jews and Christians

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on swearing by attributes besides Allah for Jews and Christians and explain the istihsan-based reasoning.

Core Idea
Jews and Christians may swear by their scriptures because they are divinely revealed; other entities may not be venerated with Allah's name.

In Hanafi fiqh, the default is that oaths are taken only by Allah's name. However, a special concession is made for Jews and Christians based on istihsan. This lesson explores the reasoning behind allowing them to swear by the Torah and Gospel while prohibiting the veneration of other entities like fire.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule on oaths
Recall that in Hanafi law, an oath is valid only if it invokes Allah or one of His names/attributes. Swearing by other entities is generally impermissible.
2
Note the exception for Ahl al-Kitab
The passage cites Imam Khasaf: Jews and Christians may swear by attributes of their religion (e.g., Torah, Gospel) because these are revered divine books.
The exception is specific to their scriptures, not all sacred objects.
3
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The proof is that mentioning fire alongside Allah would venerate fire, which is inappropriate. In contrast, the Torah and Gospel are already revered, so swearing by them alongside Allah causes no harm.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference), not explicit text.
4
Contrast with other entities
For non-Muslims other than Ahl al-Kitab (e.g., idol worshippers), only Allah's name is used in oaths, as their objects of worship are not divinely revealed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام خصاف نے ذکر کیا کہ یہود اور نصاری اللہ کے علاوہ اپنے مذہب کے مطابق دوسرے اوصاف ذکر کر سکتے ہیں لیکن ان کے علاوہ سے صرف اللہ کے نام کی قسم لی جائے گی اس کو ہمارے بعض مشائخ نے پسند کیا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر اللہ کے نام کے ساتھ آگ کا ذکر کیا گیا تو آگ کی بھی تعظیم ہو گی حالانکہ آگ کی تعظیم کسی طرح مناسب نہیں ہے اس کے برخلاف تورات وانجیل کہ اللہ کی ساری کتاب میں معظم ہیں لہذا اللہ کے نام کے ساتھ ان کو ذکر کرنے میں اگر انکی تعظیم ہوتی ہے تو اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔
Imam Khasaf mentioned that Jews and Christians can mention other attributes according to their religion besides Allah, but for others besides them, only Allah's name is taken in oath. Some of our mashayikh preferred this. The proof is that if fire is mentioned with Allah's name, then fire would also be venerated, which is inappropriate. In contrast, the Torah and Gospel are revered books of Allah, so if their mention with Allah's name results in their veneration, there is no harm.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses the permissibility of non-Muslims swearing by other than Allah's name. The author follows Imam Khasaf's report that Jews and Christians may swear by attributes of their religion (e.g., the Torah or Gospel) because these are divinely revealed books. For others (like idol worshippers), only Allah's name is used. The reasoning is based on istihsan: mentioning fire with Allah would venerate fire (improper), but the Torah and Gospel are already venerated, so swearing by them alongside Allah's name is acceptable.

Key Terms
مشائخ (mashayikh): Later Hanafi scholars whose opinions may carry weight but not necessarily mufta bihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why may Jews and Christians swear by the Torah or Gospel but not by fire?
A) Because fire is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the Torah and Gospel are revered divine books, whereas fire is not
C) Because Jews and Christians only believe in the Torah and Gospel
D) Because swearing by fire is prohibited for Muslims

Key Takeaway
Jews and Christians may swear by their scriptures due to istihsan, as they are divinely revealed and their veneration is acceptable.

beginner
6 min
No Aggravation of Oath for Muslim with Time or Place
Ruling that taghliz is not wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taghliz al-yamin and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the purpose of veneration and the principle of removing hardship.

Core Idea
Taghliz of oath by time or place is not wajib: the purpose is veneration, already achieved, and it causes hardship.

When a Muslim takes an oath in court, should the judge require a specific time (like Friday) or place (like the mosque) to make the oath more solemn? The Hanafi school says no – the purpose of the oath is to venerate Allah, which is already present. Requiring such aggravation (taghliz) would impose unnecessary hardship on the judge, which Islamic law removes. Let's examine the ruling and its rational basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Find the exact statement: taghliz al-yamin (aggravation of the oath) upon a Muslim by specifying a time or place is not obligatory (لا يجب). The subject is the act of the judge administering the oath, not the oath itself.
The ruling is about the judge's requirement, not the witness's obligation.
2
Determine the hukm level
The text says 'la yajib' (not obligatory). In Hanafi terms, this means the act is not wajib; it is permissible (mubah) but not required. There is no sin in omitting it.
Distinguish from 'haram' – the text does not forbid it; it simply removes the obligation.
3
Extract the first rational proof: purpose of veneration
The purpose (maqsud) of the oath is to venerate the one sworn by (Allah). This veneration is already achieved by the very act of swearing by Allah, without needing extra time/place. Thus, taghliz adds nothing essential.
This is a goal-based (maqasidi) reasoning: if the objective is already met, an extra condition is unnecessary.
4
Extract the second rational proof: prevention of hardship
If taghliz were obligatory, the judge would be forced to attend a specific time/place to administer the oath. This would cause hardship (haraj) on the judge. Islamic law aims to remove hardship (raf' al-haraj), so such an obligation would contradict this principle.
The principle of raf' al-haraj is a core Hanafi usul maxim derived from Quran and Sunnah.
5
State the conclusion and practical effect
Therefore, taghliz is not wajib. The judge has full discretion to administer the oath wherever and whenever convenient. The ruling is based on rational proofs (dalil aqli) using maqsad and harm prevention.
A judge may still choose to administer the oath in a mosque if it is convenient, but it is not required.

Source Text

قال ولا يجب تغليط اليمين على المسلم بزمان ولامكان لان المقصود تعظيم المقسم به وهو حاصل بدون ذالک وفی ایجاب ذالك حرج على القاضي حيث يكلف حضورها وهو مدفوع ترجمہ اور مسل پر قسم کی تغلیظ زمانہ اور مکان کے ساتھ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ مقصود اس کی تعظیم ہے جس کی قسم کھائی جاتی ہے اور وہ بغیر اس کے بھی حاصل ہے اور اس کو واجب کرنے میں قاضی پر حرج ہے کیونکہ اس کو وہاں حاضر ہونے کا مکلف کیا جائے گا حالانکہ حرج کو دور کیا گیا ہے۔ یا تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ مسلمان کی قسم کو غلیظ کرنے کے لئے کسی تبرک زمان یا مکان کا ذکر کرنا واجب نہیں ہے یعنی یہ ضروری نہیں کہ کسی تبرک زمان یا مکان میں قسم لی جائے۔ کیونکہ قسم سے اس معبود کی تعظیم مقصود ہے جس کے نام کی قسم کھائی ہے اور یقی اس زمان اور مکان کو ذکر کئے بغیر بھی حاصل ہے نیز زمان یا مکان کو متعین کرنے میں قاضی کو حرج میں مبتلاء کہ نالازم آتا ہے کیونکہ زمان اور مکان کی تعیین کی صورت میں قاضی پر وہاں حاضر ہونا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ شریعت اسلام نے حرج کو دور کیا ہے پس یہ بات واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ قاضی خود مختار ہے جہاں چاہے قسم لے۔
He said: It is not obligatory to aggravate the oath upon a Muslim with time or place, because the purpose is veneration of the one by whom the oath is sworn, and that is achieved without that. Requiring that causes hardship for the judge as he would be obliged to attend, and hardship is repelled. Translation: And for a Muslim, aggravation of the oath with time and place is not obligatory, because the purpose is veneration of the one sworn by, and that is achieved without it. Requiring it causes hardship for the judge because he would be required to attend there, whereas hardship is removed. Or explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that to aggravate a Muslim's oath, mentioning a blessed time or place is not obligatory, i.e., it is not necessary to take the oath in a blessed time or place. Because the purpose of the oath is veneration of the deity sworn by, and that is achieved without mentioning time or place. Additionally, specifying time/place would oblige the judge to attend, causing hardship, whereas Islamic law has removed hardship. So it is not obligatory; rather, the judge is free to administer the oath wherever he wishes.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage explains that for a Muslim, the judge does not need to specify a virtuous time or place (like Friday, the mosque, etc.) when administering an oath. The purpose is reverence for Allah, which is already present. Requiring such would impose hardship on the judge, which is contrary to the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). The ruling is based on rational reasoning and the principle of ease. The judge is free to administer the oath wherever and whenever he chooses.

Key Terms
تغلیط (taghliz): Aggravation or intensification of the oath by specifying a particular time or place to enhance its solemnity.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that Islamic law seeks to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is it not obligatory to aggravate a Muslim's oath with a specific time or place?
A) Because Muslims are already truthful
B) Because the purpose of veneration is achieved without it, and it causes hardship for the judge
C) Because the Quran does not mention it
D) Because it would make the oath too severe

Key Takeaway
Taghliz of a Muslim's oath by time or place is not wajib because the purpose of veneration is already met, and requiring it contradicts the principle of removing hardship.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Phrasing of Oath: Cause vs. Result in Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oath phrasing across claims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule on oath formulation in claims of sale, usurpation, marriage, and divorce, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad from Abu Yusuf, including the consensus exceptions.

Core Idea
In oath formulation, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prioritize the present result to protect defendants; Abu Yusuf prioritizes the cause unless an allusion is made.

When a defendant is sued for sale, usurpation, marriage, or divorce, the judge must administer an oath. The key question is whether the oath should refer to the original act (sabab, e.g., 'I did not sell') or the current state (hasil, e.g., 'there is no valid sale now'). This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and the consensus exceptions that arise when the cause is not subject to nullification or when the plaintiff's right would be lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, in claims of sale, usurpation, marriage, and divorce, the defendant swears on the present result (hasil). For example, in a sale claim, he swears 'there is no valid sale now'.
The rationale is that the cause may have been superseded by a later event (rescission, khul', renewal), so swearing on the cause could force the defendant into perjury or harm.
2
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the defendant swears on the cause (sabab) in all these cases unless the defendant alludes (ta'rid) to a possible nullification. Only then does the oath shift to the result.
Abu Yusuf places more weight on the original act, reasoning that the default is to deny the cause.
3
Examine the intermediate opinion (qil)
Another view states that the oath should be tailored to the defendant's denial: if he denies the cause, he swears on the cause; if he denies the result, he swears on the result.
This reconciles the two positions by focusing on what the defendant is actually contesting.
4
Recognize consensus exceptions where oath is on the cause
There are cases where swearing on the cause is agreed upon: (a) when the cause cannot be superseded by a nullifier (e.g., a Muslim slave claiming freedom, because freedom once proven cannot be reversed), and (b) when swearing on the result would harm the plaintiff's right (e.g., a divorced woman claiming maintenance, or a pre-emption claim).
In these exceptions, the oath is always on the cause by consensus to protect the plaintiff.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن ادعى انه ابتاع من هذا عبده بالف فجحد استحلف بالله ما بينكما بيع قائم فيه ولا يستحلف بالله ما بعت لانه قد يباع العين ثم يقال فيه ويستحلف فى الغضب بالله ما يستحق علیک رده و لا یحلف بالله ما غصبت لانه قد يغضب ثم يفسخ بالهبة والبيع وفى النكاح بالله ما بينكما نكاح قائم في الحال لانه قد يطرء عليه الخلع وفى الدعوى الطلاق بالله ماهى بائن منك الساعة بما ذكرت ولا يستحلف بالله ماطلقها لان النكاح قد يجدد بعد الابانة فيحلف على الحاصل في هذه الوجوه لانه لو حلف على السبب يتضرر المدعى عليه وهذا قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد اما على قول أبي يوسف يحلف في جميع ذالک علی السبب الا اذا عرض المدعى عليه بما ذكرنا فحينئذ يحلف على الحاصل وقيل ينظر الى انكار المدعى عليه ان انكر السبب يحلف عليه وان انكر الحكم يحلف على الحاصل فالحاصل هو الأصل عندهما اذا كان سببا " يرتفع برافع الااذا كان فيه ترك النظر في جانب المدعى فحينئذ يحلف على السبب بالاجماع وذالك مثل ان تدعى مبتوتة نفقة العدة والزوج ممن لايراها او ادعى شفعة بالجوار والمشترى لا يراها لانه لو حلف على الحاصل يصدق في يمينه في معتقدة فيفوت النظر في حق المدعى وان كان سببا لا يرتفع برافع فالتحليف على السبب بالاجماع كالعبد المسلم اذا ادعى العتق على مولاه بخلاف الامة والعبد الكافر لانه يتكرر الرق عليها بالرد واللحاق وعليه بنقض العهد واللحاق ولا يكرر على العبد المسلم
He said: And whoever claims that he bought a slave from him for a thousand, and the defendant denies, he is made to swear: 'By Allah, there is no valid sale between us regarding it,' and he is not made to swear: 'By Allah, I did not sell,' because the item may be sold and then rescinded. And in usurpation, he swears: 'By Allah, you are not entitled to its return,' and he is not made to swear: 'By Allah, I did not usurp,' because he may have usurped and then dissolved by gift or sale. And in marriage: 'By Allah, there is no marriage existing between you now,' because khul' may have intervened. And in a claim of divorce: 'By Allah, she is not irrevocably divorced from you at this moment for what she mentioned,' and he is not made to swear: 'By Allah, he did not divorce her,' because marriage may be renewed after irrevocable divorce. So in these cases, he swears on the result, because if he swore on the cause, the defendant would be harmed. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. As for the statement of Abu Yusuf, he swears in all these on the cause unless the defendant alludes to what we mentioned; then he swears on the result. And it is said: one looks at the defendant's denial: if he denies the cause, he swears on it; if he denies the ruling, he swears on the result. So the result is the original according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) when the cause is something that can be superseded by a nullifier, except when there is a neglect of consideration for the plaintiff; then he swears on the cause by consensus. For example, a divorced woman claiming maintenance for the waiting period and the husband does not see her, or one claims pre-emption by vicinage and the buyer does not see it—because if he swears on the result, he would be truthful in his belief, and the plaintiff's right is lost. And if the cause is not subject to be superseded by a nullifier, then swearing on the cause is by consensus, like a Muslim slave claiming freedom from his master, unlike a female slave or a non-Muslim slave, because slavery can recur upon her by return and joining, and upon him by breach of covenant and joining, and it does not recur upon the Muslim slave.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This is a detailed lesson on the formulation of oaths in various legal claims. The general rule from Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that the oath should be on the present result (hasil) rather than the original cause (sabab). For example, in a claim of sale, the defendant swears 'there is no valid sale now' because a sale may have been rescinded. This principle protects the defendant from swearing falsely about an act that may no longer be in effect. Imam Abu Yusuf differs, holding that the oath should be on the cause unless the defendant alludes to a possible change. Another opinion (qil) looks at the defendant's denial: if he denies the cause, he swears on it; if he denies the result, he swears on the result. However, there are exceptions by consensus where swearing on the cause is required, such as when a divorced woman claims maintenance (to prevent the husband from easily swearing falsely) or in pre-emption claims. Similarly, for a Muslim slave claiming freedom, the oath is on the cause (emancipation) because the cause cannot recur once proven.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The original act giving rise to the claim (e.g., the sale, the usurpation, the marriage, the divorce).
حاصل (hasil): The present state or outcome resulting from the cause (e.g., existence of a valid sale now).
تعریض (ta'rid): Allusion; the defendant hints at a possible nullification without explicitly stating it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the general rule from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding the oath in a claim of sale?
A) The defendant swears: 'By Allah, I did not sell.'
B) The defendant swears: 'By Allah, there is no valid sale now.'
C) The defendant swears: 'By Allah, the plaintiff is lying.'
D) The defendant swears: 'By Allah, I do not owe the money.'

Key Takeaway
In standard claims of sale, usurpation, marriage, and divorce, the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) requires the oath on the present result (hasal) to protect the defendant from perjury due to subsequent nullification.
